1401 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Lanning v. Pilcher


CASE NO. 1D07-6564


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 9092; 34 Fla. L. Weekly D 1373



July 8, 2009, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected October 21, 2009.
Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at Lanning v. Pilcher, 16 So. 3d 294, 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 13118 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Aug. 26, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. John C. Cooper, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners brought an action against public entities and individuals, challenging Art. VII, § 4(c), Fla. Const. and the statutes enacted to implement that provision. The Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida) entered a final order upholding the constitutional provision. The property owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The public entities and individuals argued that the trial court should have dismissed the case pursuant to § 194.171, Fla. Stat. The appellate court disagreed. The point of the case was that the Florida property tax scheme had a discriminatory effect on nonresidents. The case had nothing to do with the assessment made on any particular property, and so the 60-day provision in § 194.171 and the policy considerations underlying the statute did not come into play. The property owners asserted a series of federal constitutional challenges to Art. VII, § 4(c), Fla. Const., but all of the supporting arguments had been rejected before in comparable cases. A Florida resident who owned vacation or business property in the state was not entitled to a tax benefit under Art. VII, § 4(c), Fla. Const. and was in the same position with respect to that property as a nonresident. Art. VII, § 4(c), Fla. Const. was valid under the United States Constitution and did not violate a nonresident's rights under the Equal Protection Clause, the Privileges and Immunities Clause, or the Commerce Clause. Likewise, § 193.155, Fla. Stat. was constitutionally valid.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

1404 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Abbott Labs. v. Mylan Pharms., Inc.


CASE NO.: 1D08-0602


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


15 So. 3d 642; 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 8512; 34 Fla. L. Weekly D 1265



June 22, 2009, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Mylan Pharms., Inc. v. Abbott Labs., 2009 Fla. LEXIS 2286 (Fla., Dec. 29, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An appeal from an order of the Division of Administrative Hearings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a drug manufacturer, challenged the order of the Division of Administrative Hearings, which entered a summary final order in a rule challenge proceeding brought by appellee, a manufacturer of a competing generic drug, and held that Fla. Admin. Code Ann. R. 64B16-27.500(6), which was part of the negative drug formulary (NDF) rule established under § 465.025(6), Fla. Stat. (2007), was invalid.


OVERVIEW: Appellant manufactured a levothyroxine sodium (LS) drug product, Synthroid(R), and appellee manufactured a competing generic drug. The NDF listed LS, and the Administrative Law Judge (ALJ) determined that the rule was invalid on the grounds that it constituted an invalid exercise of legislative delegated authority because it conflicted with the provisions of § 465.0251(1), Fla. Stat. (2007), which removed a generic drug from the NDF if the generic drug was "A" rated as therapeutically equivalent to a reference listed drug as referred to in the Orange Book published the United States Food and Drug Administration (FDA). The ALJ's order, in effect, removed LS from the NDF and permitted Florida pharmacists to substitute appellee's generic LS product for a prescription for Synthroid(R) or any other "A" rated LS drug product. The court held that the ALJ erred in interpreting § 465.0251(1) to apply to editions of the Orange Book subsequent to the date of the 2001 enactment of the statute. Therefore, the court revered the order. The court further rejected appellee's contention that appellant lacked standing to bring the appeal and that the mootness doctrine applied to the appeal.


OUTCOME: The Court reversed the order and remanded the case to the ALJ for further proceedings.


 

1405 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Columbia Hosp. Corp. v. Fain


No. 4D08-4578


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 8773; 34 Fla. L. Weekly D 1223



June 17, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 19, 2009.
Rehearing denied by, Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at Columbia Hosp. Corp. v. Fain, 16 So. 3d 236, 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 11600 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Aug. 19, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Petition for writ of certiorari to the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; David Krathen, Judge; L.T. Case No. 08-1429 09.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner medical center sought a writ of certiorari seeking to quash an order of the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), which denied its objections to respondent personal representative's discovery requests pursuant to Art. X, § 25, Fla. Const. (Amendment 7) for incident reports for a decedent's fall and all adverse medical incident reports involving falls of patients under "fall precautions."


OVERVIEW: The decedent fell from a hospital bed while an inpatient at the medical center and subsequently died. The medical center objected to the representative's discovery requests. The court of appeal held that the trial court's order denying the medical center's objections to the discovery requests for Amendment 7 material did not depart from the essential requirements of law. A request for Amendment 7 materials was not an ordinary discovery request that could be subjected to overbreadth, irrelevance, or burdensomeness objections. The trial court did not fail to consider or rule on the medical center's claim of procedural protections under § 381.028, Fla. Stat. (2008). The decedent's estate offered to work with the medical center and make necessary compromises in order to facilitate the discovery it sought. The estate did not contest the requirement that it had to pay the reasonable costs associated with the discovery before production. The medical center had not been required to produce the materials prior to payment. The Health Care Quality Improvement Act of 1986, 42 U.S.C.S. § 11101 et seq., did not require the states to provide confidentiality for peer review materials.


OUTCOME: The court of appeal denied the petition.

1407 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


In re M. V.-B v. Dep't of Children & Family Servs.


Case No. 2D08-3616


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


19 So. 3d 381; 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 7256; 34 Fla. L. Weekly D 1157



June 10, 2009, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 30, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Pasco County; William R. Webb, Judge.
M. V.-B. v. Dep't of Children & Family Servs., 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 3210 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., Apr. 15, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a father and the paternal grandparents, appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Pasco County (Florida) maintaining the child's placement with a licensed foster care family and rejected the grandparents' request for the court to transfer placement to them.


OVERVIEW: The Guardian Ad Litem challenged the grandparents' standing tho bring the appeal and the appellate court's jurisdiction to consider the appeal as filed by the father. In dismissing the grandparents' appeal, the appellate court noted that the case actually involved an attempt to change custody of the child postdisposition under § 39.522, Fla. Stat., and the grandparents could not even demonstrate that any interested party filed a petition to change custody under that statute. As to the father's appeal, the appellate court held that the orders entered in dependency proceedings after the entry of the order adjudicating dependency and before an order terminating supervision or jurisdiction were not appealable pursuant to Fla. R. App. P. 9.130(a)(4). While such order could be challenged by common law certiorari when appropriate, the father argued nothing that would have suggested that certiorari would provide a possible remedy.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

 

1408 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


K.A. v. State


No. 4D08-2283


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


12 So. 3d 869; 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 7296; 34 Fla. L. Weekly D 8



June 10, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 29, 2009


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Elijah H. Williams, Judge; L.T. Case No. 07-9955 DL00A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida) found defendant, a juvenile, guilty of resisting arrest without violence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion for judgment of dismissal because the evidence was insufficient as a matter of law to supporting the finding of guilt. Defendant argued that the deputy named in the petition was not engaged in the lawful execution of a lawful duty, but rather, was merely on duty when he assisted another deputy in walking defendant to the patrol care. Defendant asserted that he was subjected to an illegal stop and arrest for mere speech. While the State argued that the deputy could have lawfully taken defendant into custody for violating three separate statutes, the appellate court concluded that there was no evidence that the deputies had been called to a disturbance and thus, defendant was not interfering with their investigation, defendant's encouraging others not to run away could not support an arrest for inciting a riot, and defendant's failure to stop yelling could not support an arrest for refusal to aid police officers who told him to stop yelling.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the case was remanded with directions for the trial court to vacate the finding of guilty and placement on probation.

 

1409 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Fla. Eye Clinic, P.A. v. Gmach


Case No. 5D09-64


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


14 So. 3d 1044; 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 6557; 34 Fla. L. Weekly D 1080



May 29, 2009, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 8, 2009.
Rehearing denied by Fla. Eye Clinic, P.A. v. Gmach, 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 13610 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Aug. 20, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Petition for Certiorari Review of Order from the Circuit Court for Seminole County, James E.C. Perry, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent patient brought a medical malpractice action against petitioner eye clinic in the Circuit Court for Seminole County (Florida). The trial court ordered the eye clinic to produce in discovery incident reports concerning complaints of infections and related investigations at the eye clinic over a period of time. The eye clinic filed a petition for certiorari review of the discovery order.


OVERVIEW: During the course of discovery in the medical malpractice action the patient served a request for production of documents seeking, inter alia, incident reports concerning complaints of infections and related investigations at the eye clinic over a period of time. The eye clinic objected to the discovery on the bases of work-product and attorney-client privilege. It also contended that the information sought was overly broad, not limited to a reasonable time, and would have been unduly burdensome to obtain. On appeal, the court found that the adverse incident reports in question were never reviewed by counsel. Thus, the reports were not attorney work product as they did not contain any attorney's mental impressions, conclusions, opinions, or theories concerning the eye clinic's case. In any event, to the extent that the reports truly were created in anticipation of litigation, they still did not amount to anything more than fact work product due to their failure to contain any mental impressions, conclusions, opinions, or theories of defense counsel. In any event, a fact work-product privilege was unavailable under Art. X, § 25, Fla. Const.


OUTCOME: The petition was denied.

 

1410 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Demings v. Orange County Citizens Review Bd.


CASE NO. 5D08-1063


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


15 So. 3d 604; 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 6554; 34 Fla. L. Weekly D 1085



May 29, 2009, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 3, 2009.
Rehearing denied by Demings v. Orange County Citizens Review Bd., 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 11491 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., July 10, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, Maura T. Smith, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, the Orange County, Florida Citizen's Review Board (CRB) filed an action in the Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida), to enforce a subpoena. Appellant sheriff filed a complaint for declaratory judgment and supplemental relief to challenge the CRB's authority to independently investigate a complaint against a sheriff's deputy. The court held that the CRB was authorized to independently investigate the complaint. The sheriff appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Orange County, Florida Charter and ordinances establishes the CRB and authorized it to review and investigate citizen complaints of excessive force and abuse of power. The sheriff challenged the CRB's power to compel the sheriff's deputies to appear and testify in CRB investigations by subpoena. On appeal, the court found that, pursuant to § 112.533(1)(a), Fla. Stat. (2008), and Art. VIII, § 1(d), Fla. Const., the county could not interfere with the sheriff's independent exercise of his duty to investigate alleged misconduct by his deputies either by forcing him to appoint members to the CRB or by mandating his participation in CRB proceedings, either in person or through his deputies or employees. Therefore, the basic structure or composition of the CRB was constitutionally infirm. Further, those provisions of the charter and ordinance authorizing the CRB to compel the attendance of Sheriff's employees to appear for questioning by the CRB, or to produce documents, are also unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The order on appeal was reversed, and the case was remand for entry of judgment.

 

1411 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Abram v. State, Dep't of Health, Bd. of Med.


No. 4D08-1965


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


13 So. 3d 85; 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 5435; 34 Fla. L. Weekly D 1006



May 20, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 5, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the State of Florida, Department of Health; L.T. Case No. 2006-09853.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee Department of Health, Board of Medicine (Florida), entered a final decision in a physician disciplinary case that adopted an administrative complaint as the Board's findings of fact and conclusions of law, and determined that appellant orthopedic surgeon's conduct in performing a wrong-site procedure violated statutory law. The surgeon appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Department filed an administrative complaint with the Board against the surgeon alleging that the surgeon, by performing a surgical procedure on a patient's vertebra level rather that was not the intended level, violated § 456.072(1)(aa), Fla. Stat. (2004) by performing a wrong-site procedure. According to the administrative record, the surgeon immediately notified the patient and the patient did not suffer any harm. The surgeon filed an election of rights indicating that he did not dispute the Department's allegations of fact, but requested an informal hearing before the Board to submit mitigation evidence. Following a hearing, the Board voted to accept the administrative complaint's legal conclusion that the surgeon violated the statute by performing a wrong-site procedure. The Board then entered a decision that imposed discipline. The appellate court rejected the surgeon's contention that the statute contained an irrebutable presumption that performing such a procedure fell below the standard of care and, thus, violated his due process rights because the statute had no such presumption and did not place the issue of a violation of the standard of care at issue.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the Board's decision.

15 So. 3d 34; 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 5827; 34 Fla. L. Weekly D 986

1413 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


C.A.T. v. Dep't of Children & Families


Case No. 5D08-2350


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


10 So. 3d 682; 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 3996; 34 Fla. L. Weekly D 876



April 29, 2009, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by C.A.T. v. Dep't of Children & Families, 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 9175 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., June 8, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Brevard County, John M. Griesbaum, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee department of children and families (DCF) filed a petition for termination of parental rights against appellant father. The petition was filed on an expedited basis pursuant to § 39.806(3), Fla. Stat. (2007). The Circuit Court for Brevard County (Florida), inter alia, terminated the father's parental rights to his son. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The father first argued that the definition of "abandonment" in § 39.01, Fla. Stat. (2007) was unconstitutionally vague. However, the appellate court had rejected a similar vagueness challenge in a different case. The father was not offered a case plan for reunification before initiation of this termination proceeding. The father was offered a case plan in an earlier case, but he refused it, proceeded to hearing, and was found to be non-offending. The trial court's order that the father submit to a substance abuse evaluation and drug screens was not a case plan. The father had not received DCF's services since the original case plan in 2002, and he was never offered a case plan with services as an alternative to losing his parental rights in the current proceedings. Thus, the DCF failed to prove that it could forego intermediate efforts at reunification. This was not a case of egregious abuse or danger to the child. There was evidence of a bond between the child and the father. The DCF failed to prove that termination was the least restrictive means of protecting the child from harm, which was required in a § 39.806(1) proceeding. The trial court erred in entering the order.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

1414 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Ortiz v. State


Case No. 5D08-1653


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 3460; 34 Fla. L. Weekly D 829



April 24, 2009, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On rehearing at, Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at, En banc Ortiz v. State, 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 16858 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Nov. 13, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, Jose R. Rodriguez, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following the denial of defendant's motion to suppress, the Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida) accepted defendant's plea of nolo contendere to trafficking in cocaine and possession of drug paraphernalia, in which defendant reserved the right to appeal the denial of his motion to suppress. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A deputy received a call that a six-year-old child's parental failed to pick him up from the after-school program. The deputy retrieved the child and too the child to the address provided by the school. The child told the deputy that his parents were or should be home. The child invited the deputy into his house, where they found the door to the master bedroom locked but no answer when the deputy knocked. The deputy opened the door. On appeal, defendant argued that law enforcement's warrantless entry into his home and the subsequent seizure of cocaine and drug paraphernalia were improper. The appellate court agreed. The State offered no evidence to demonstrate a reasonable belief that the child's parents were inside the house and might be in need of medical attention. There was no indication of foul play and no car in the driveway. The deputy's alleged concern for the well-being of the parents after he entered the house and found the locked master bedroom was insufficient to justify the warrantless entry. The appellate court also concluded that the record failed to establish that the child could validly consent to entry of the locked master bedroom.


OUTCOME: Defendants convictions were reversed.

 

1415 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


M. V.-B. v. Dep't of Children & Family Servs.


Case No. 2D08-3616


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 3210; 34 Fla. L. Weekly D 753



April 15, 2009, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:

NOT FINAL UNTIL TIME EXPIRES TO FILE REHEARING MOTION AND, IF FILED, DETERMINED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Clarified by, Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at, Appeal dismissed by In re M. V.-B v. Dep't of Children & Family Servs., 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 7256 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., June 10, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Pasco County; William R. Webb, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the father and the paternal grandparents of a minor child, sought review of an order entered by the Circuit Court for Pasco County, Florida, in dependency proceedings regarding the child. The order, entered by the trial court after adjudicating the child dependent, maintained the child's placement with a licensed foster care family and rejected the grandparents' request for the court to transfer placement to them.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court declined to reverse or quash the challenged order, finding that it had no appellate jurisdiction over what was a nonfinal order and no basis to grant relief as a matter of common law certiorari. The grandparents were not parties in the dependency proceeding and therefore, they lacked standing to appeal the order. While, the appellate court would not rule out the possibility that grandparents might have legal rights sufficient to maintain a petition for writ of certiorari, the facts in the instant case did not support such a right in the instant case. As to the father, while the order adjudicating dependency was appealable as a final order under §39.510, Fla. Stat. (2007), the statute could not authorize appeals of non-final orders such as the instant order. The appellate court further held that orders entered in dependency proceedings after the entry of an adjudication order and before an order terminating supervision or jurisdiction were not appealable pursuant to Fla. R. App. P. 9.130(a)(4). Finally, while such orders could be challenged by common law certiorari, the father had argued nothing that would suggest that certiorari would provide a remedy.


OUTCOME: The appellate court dismissed the appeal.

 

1416 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Drake v. Walton County


CASE NO. 1D07-3202


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


6 So. 3d 717; 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 3236; 34 Fla. L. Weekly D 745



April 14, 2009, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 30, 2009.
Appeal dismissed by, Review denied by Walton County v. Drake, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1603 (Fla., Sept. 17, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An appeal from the Circuit Court for Walton County. W. Howard Laporte, Judge.
Drake v. Walton County, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 17597 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Nov. 21, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the successor trustee of two trusts, appealed a final judgment of the Circuit Court for Walton County, Florida, entered in favor of appellee county on claims that included inverse condemnation. The appellate court reversed, but the trustee filed motions, inter alia, for rehearing, clarification, and certification. The appellate court granted clarification only so that it could clarify that two separate takings occurred.


OVERVIEW: The inverse condemnation claim involved the county's diversion of water across a portion of property originally purchased by the trustee's deceased parents. Before the parents purchased the property in 1988, a ditch draining a lake's outflow had been stabilized and did not discharge water across the property. That drainage was not changed until the county acted in 1995, diverting waters across the property to alleviate flooding of other properties that was caused by a hurricane. Efforts to thereafter restabilize the water flow failed. In 2004, the county successfully redirected water flow away from the property, but in 2005, under emergency conditions, the county again diverted flow over the property. The continued flow constituted a taking. The county could not choose to act and protect the property of one owner by diverting floodwater onto the subject property without compensation to the trustee. Further, while § 252.43(6), Fla. Stat. allowed the county to act in an emergency, that did not preclude the trustee, as an innocent property owner from initiating her takings claim. The statute could not restrict the rights granted to the trustee under Art. X, § 6, Fla. Const.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed as to all issues except the inverse condemnation claims. With regard to those claims, the appellate court reversed and remanded with directions that judgment be entered in favor of the trustee on those claims.

 

1417 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Amison v. State


Case No. 2D07-5928


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


5 So. 3d 798; 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 2906; 34 Fla. L. Weekly D 670



April 1, 2009, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 17, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Pasco County; Pat Siracusa, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded no contest in the Circuit Court for Pasco County (Florida) to possession of marijuana in excess of 20 grams, reserving the right to appeal the denial of his motion to suppress evidence. Following the conviction, defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A Florida Fish and Wildlife Conservation Commission officer testified that he was on resource patrol in a wildlife management area when he saw defendant's pickup truck, near a river, backing away. The officer stopped the truck to conduct a resource inspection. As the officer approached the truck, he smelled marijuana. Defendant and a passenger admitted to having smoked marijuana earlier. The officer found a bag of marijuana in a search of the truck. On cross-examination, the officer indicated that he did not observe defendant participating in any regulated activities. He also had no reason to believe that defendant was involved in criminal activity or violating traffic laws. The officer believed he had the authority to detain anyone for a regulatory inspection in the wildlife management area. On appeal, the court found that the officer needed reasonable suspicion to stop defendant's truck under § 372.07, Fla. Stat. (2007) (renumbered as § 379.3311, Fla. Stat. (2008)) and § 372.76, Fla. Stat. (renumbered as § 379.334, Fla. Stat. (2008)). Because the trial court found no reasonable suspicion existed for the stop of defendant's truck, the court erred in denying the motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: The denial of the motion to suppress was reversed, and the case was remanded for the trial court to grant the motion, which entitled defendant to discharge.

 

1418 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Haliburton v. State


No. 4D09-417


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


7 So. 3d 601; 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 2952; 34 Fla. L. Weekly D 682



April 1, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 20, 2009.
Rehearing denied by Haliburton v. State, 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 18227 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., May 20, 2009)
Review denied by Haliburton v. State, 18 So. 3d 528, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1443 (Fla., 2009)
Petition dismissed by Haliburton v. State, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 2096 (Fla., Dec. 8, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal of order denying rule 3.850 motion from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Sandra K. Mcsorley, Judge; L.T. Case No. 2002CF003729AXX.
Haliburton v. State, 861 So. 2d 1165, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 19880 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner sought review of the order of the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), which denied his Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(a) and 3.850 motions. The motions raised variants of the same claim, and the trial court denied them in a single order ruling that the claim was impermissibly successive.


OVERVIEW: The judge instructed the jury that aggravated battery based on the great bodily harm theory was a lesser-included offense of aggravated battery with a firearm. The prisoner argued that regardless of whether a firearm was used or not, the judge did not have discretion to impose a lesser punishment. The issue the prisoner raised was preserved and argued on direct appeal and was rejected on the merits. He then raised the same claim in a Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(a) motion to correct illegal sentence which was denied on the merits and affirmed. He raised the same and similar variants of the same claim again in a motion for postconviction relief. That motion was also denied and affirmed on the merits. The instant motions again raised variants of the same issue that had been repeatedly denied and rejected on appeal. The appellate court held the alleged error was not the type of error that could be raised at any time and which called for disturbing the finality of the conviction. The evidence of an aggravated battery was strong if not overwhelming. The jury had an opportunity to exercise its "pardon power" by convicting of simple battery but refused to do so.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1419 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


R.M. v. Dep't of Children & Families

9 So. 3d 40; 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 3617; 34 Fla. L. Weekly D 503

1421 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Martinez


No. 4D09-177


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


4 So. 3d 712; 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 1485; 34 Fla. L. Weekly D 425



February 24, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 3, 2009.
Rehearing denied by State v. Martinez, 4 So. 3d 712, 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 3488 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist. 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Petition for writ of certiorari to the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Susan Lebow, Judge; L.T. Case No. 03-19397 CF10A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defense counsel moved to dismiss a charge against defendant based on prosecutorial misconduct--listening to telephone conversations between counsel and defendant at the county jail. The Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), denied the motion, but ordered disqualification of the State Attorney's Office. The State petitioned for a writ of certiorari or prohibition. Defendant moved to dismiss the petition.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the appellate court did not have jurisdiction based on Weir. In Weir, the Florida Supreme Court held that the State's ability to seek certiorari review of an interlocutory order in a criminal case was limited to pretrial orders. Once jeopardy attached, the State could not get immediate review of a nonfinal order. Although review might be available in the event of a mistrial, in general, the state supreme court found no exception to this rule. The appellate court agreed with defendant's argument and concluded that even if extraordinary writ jurisdiction might be invoked to review an order entered after a criminal trial commenced, it would deny the petition in this case because the trial court did not depart from the essential requirements of law. The record supported the trial court's findings that the case law cited was distinguishable and that there was no waiver of the attorney-client privilege based on the circumstances. In addition, the trial court expressly found that the calls contained trial strategy and that the conversations included privileged information that had been discussed throughout the State Attorney's Office.


OUTCOME: The petition was dismissed.

 

1422 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Chen


Case No. 2D06-4735


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


1 So. 3d 1257; 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 1054; 34 Fla. L. Weekly D 339



February 11, 2009, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 11, 2009.
Review denied by Fijnje v. State, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1243 (Fla., July 14, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County; Manuel A. Lopez, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Hillsborough County Circuit Court (Florida) entered a judgment that granted a motion to suppress in favor of the first defendant and second defendant after they were charged with trafficking in cannabis, and the second defendant was also charged with possession of cannabis. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: A detective applied for a warrant to search the first defendant's apartment. In support, the detective filed her affidavit stating she had "reason to believe" that marijuana "is now being kept" at his apartment. She described contacts involving a confidential informant (CI) and the first defendant. The CI eventually negotiated a cannabis purchase and was informed that the first defendant's supplier, later identified as the second defendant, would be arriving at the first defendant's apartment in 10 minutes with the cannabis. A judge then issued a search warrant and the warrant was executed. After the first and second defendants were charged with trafficking in and possession of cannabis, the trial court suppressed the evidence that was found. The appellate court found that the trial court should have applied the Grubbs totality-of-the-circumstances approach to determining probable cause and that the search warrant affidavit showed probable cause existed to believe the cannabis would be at the first defendant's apartment when the warrant was executed, meaning the right to be free from unreasonable searches under U.S. Const. amend. IV and Art. I, § 12, Fla. Const. was not violated.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment granting suppression and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

1423 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Rosado v. DaimlerChrysler Fin. Servs. Trust


Case No. 2D07-3690


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


1 So. 3d 1200; 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 967; 34 Fla. L. Weekly D 300



February 6, 2009, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 26, 2009.
Review granted by Rosado v. Daimlerchrysler Fin. Servs. Trust, 2011 Fla. LEXIS 2733 (Fla., Nov. 9, 2011)
Approved by, Certified question answered by Rosado v. Daimlerchrysler Fin. Servs. Trust, 2013 Fla. LEXIS 566 (Fla., Apr. 4, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Polk County; Roger A. Alcott, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver sued appellees, a lessee, an attorney, an operator, and a lessor, claiming that the lessor was vicariously liable for the operator's negligent operation of the car under Florida's dangerous instrumentality doctrine because it failed to comply with the insurance requirements of § 324.021(9)(b)(1), Fla. Stat. (2002). The Circuit Court for Polk County (Florida) granted summary judgment in favor of the lessor. The driver appealed.


OVERVIEW: The driver allegedly sustained serious injuries when a car the operator was driving collided with the driver's car. The operator's car was owned by the lessor, and leased to the lessee, a law firm. The insurance policy which the lessee had on the vehicle lapsed for nonpayment the day before the accident. The issue on appeal was whether the Graves Amendment, 49 U.S.C.S. § 30106, limited the lessor's liability. The appellate court concluded that the plain language of § 324.021(9)(b)(2), Fla. Stat. (2002), merely gave the leading company the option to have insurance in place to avoid liability in Florida under the dangerous instrumentality doctrine. Because § 324.021(9)(b)(2) did not compel the lessor to have certain insurance standards, § 324.021(9)(b)(2) did not impose liability for a failure to meet those optional standards. Thus, the appellate court upheld the trial court's ruling. However, the court certified to the supreme court a question of great public important: Does the Graves Amendment, 49 U.S.C.S. § 30106, preempt § 324.021(9)(b)(1), Fla. Stat. (2002)?


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. A question of great public importance was certified to the supreme court.


 

1424 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


L.B.B. v. State


Case No. 2D07-3804


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


998 So. 2d 1217; 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 653; 34 Fla. L. Weekly D 261



January 30, 2009, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 17, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County; Denise A. Pomponio, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed, challenging a decision of the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County, Florida, that denied defendant's dispositive motion to suppress marijuana found incident to his arrest for riding a bicycle without a bell, a violation of Tampa, Fla., City Code § 250186.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that because a person could not be arrested for a bicycle infraction, evidence discovered incident to his arrest for that infraction should have been suppressed. The appellate court agreed. In a decision 14 years earlier, the state supreme court had ruled that under § 901.15(1), Fla. Stat., persons charged with violating municipal ordinances regulating noncriminal conduct could only be detained for the limited purpose of issuing a ticket, summons, or notice to appear. A full arrest under such ordinances violated U.S. Const. amend. IV and Art. I, § 2, Fla. Const. The officer who arrested defendant in the instant case was charged with knowledge of that earlier decision, even though the City had failed to amend its ordinance to remove its improper penalties.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed and remanded for defendant's discharge.

 

1425 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Deen v. Wilson


Case Nos. 5D08-3489, 5D08-3490, 5D08-3491, and 5D08-3989


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


1 So. 3d 1179; 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 2229; 34 Fla. L. Weekly D 254



January 30, 2009, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 18, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Petition for Certiorari Review of Order from the Circuit Court for Brevard County, David Dugan, James H. Earp, and George W. Maxwell, III, Judges.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In four consolidated cases, the Circuit Court for Brevard County (Florida) appointed petitioner regional counsel to represent four respondents in post-conviction proceedings, and denied the regional counsel's motions to withdraw in each case. The regional counsel sought a writ of certiorari or alternatively, a writ of prohibition.


OVERVIEW: The regional counsel argued that the statutory duties of his office did not encompass post-conviction proceedings. The appellate court agreed. The authority of Office of Criminal Conflict and Civil Regional Counsel (Regional Counsel) to represent criminal defendants in post-conviction proceedings was not set forth as an assigned duty in § 27.511(5), Fla. Stat. (2008). When the general provision of § 27.40, Fla. Stat. was read in pari materia with the more specific statute, § 27.511(5), Fla. Stat., it was clear that post-conviction collateral proceedings were not within the realm of the regional counsel's duties of representation. There was no absolute constitutional right to post-conviction counsel. If a trial court determined that appointment of post-conviction counsel was necessary in a particular Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 proceeding, there was no specific provision for the appointment of the regional counsel under § 27.511, Fla. Stat. The appointments constituted a departure from the essential requirements of law for which certiorari relief was available.


OUTCOME: The petitions for writs of certiorari were granted and the orders of appointment were quashed.

 

1426 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Browning v. Angelfish Swim Sch., Inc.


No. 3D08-1827


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


1 So. 3d 355; 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 553; 34 Fla. L. Weekly D 234



January 28, 2009, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 13, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Mary Barzee Flores, Judge. Lower Tribunal No. 03-13413.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Florida Secretary of State, sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Florida, which certified a class of corporate plaintiffs that asserted that late annual report and reinstatement fees paid to the Secretary by them violated the Excessive Punishments section, Art. I, § 17, Fla. Const. Appellees were the two corporations named as class representatives.


OVERVIEW: Discovery revealed that over 249,000 Florida corporations had paid a $400 late annual report fee between 1997 and 2007 and that over 97,000 had paid a $600 reinstatement fee. The first three elements of Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.220(a) were unquestionably present--the class was numerous, the claims of the putative class members involved common issues of law and fact, and the claims of the proposed class representatives were typical of those of the class as a whole. The adequacy of appellees as class representatives was the issue. Corporation one had indicated the ability to pay for a mailing to putative class members, but was unfamiliar with what other costs might be involved. Corporation two had no assets or money. The case was one of first impression. The Secretary would defend the lawsuit vigorously and thoroughly. Regardless of whether appellees sought a full disgorgement of the more than $150 million in fees collected or simply amounts considered as "excessive," the proceedings were likely to be protracted. As the fees were entitled to presumptive validity under Art. I, § 18, Fla. Const., the likelihood of shifting any of the costs of the case to the Secretary was very low.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the certification order on the "adequacy" requirement imposed by Rule 1.220(a)(4). The order was otherwise affirmed. On remand, the trial court was to require the filing of a second amended complaint that, inter alia, clarified the nature of the monetary relief sought. The trial court was then to require appellees to demonstrate their financial capacity to participate in the costs likely to be incurred.


 

1427 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Haddock v. Carmody


CASE NO. 1D08-241


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


1 So. 3d 1133; 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 354; 34 Fla. L. Weekly D 207



January 21, 2009, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 6, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An appeal from the Circuit Court for Nassau County. Brian J. Davis, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Nassau County Property Appraiser (appraiser) appealed a judgment entered by the Circuit Court for Nassau County (Florida) holding that § 196.061, Fla. Stat. was unconstitutional as applied to appellee condominium owners, and ordering the appraiser to grant the owners a homestead tax exemption for the years 2003, 2004, and 2005.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that § 196.061 (2005) was not unconstitutional as applied to the owners as under former art. VII, § 6, Fla. Const., the Florida legislature could establish the procedures for claiming a homestead tax exemption. Section 196.061 properly established how rental property was to be treated under the homestead exemption law. Under § 196.061, the owners rented their entire dwelling, notwithstanding the fact that they reserved two locked closets for personal storage. The claim that reserving the locked closets meant that the entire dwelling was not rented was rejected as it was grounded in a decontextualized literalism that overemphasized the word "entire" and ignored its context. Adherence to such a literal interpretation would produce an unreasonable result. The trial court was instructed that it had to address the provision stating that an abandonment of a homestead after January 1 of any year was not to affect the homestead exemption for tax purposes for that particular year so long as the provision was not used for two consecutive years.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed. The case was remanded with instructions for the trial court to enter an order consistent with the opinion.

1429 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Ellis v. Hunter


Case No. 5D08-162


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


3 So. 3d 373; 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 1974; 34 Fla. L. Weekly D 165



January 16, 2009, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 4, 2009.
Review denied by Hunter v. Ellis, 10 So. 3d 632, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 660 (Fla., Apr. 29, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
9.160 Appeal from the County Court for Brevard County, Oscar A. Hotusing, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The County Court for Brevard County (Florida), where an entire cash bond posted by a person other than a licensed bail bondsman was withheld, ruled that § 903.286, Fla. Stat. (2007) was constitutional. It also ruled, however, that the statute only allowed sums owed in a particular case for which the bond was posted to be withheld. The county court certified questions of constitutionality of the statute and statutory application.


OVERVIEW: The criminal defendant was charged with DUI. Another individual, who was not a bail bondsman, posted a cash bond on his behalf. That other individual signed a bond form stating that the clerk of the court was required to withhold sufficient funds to pay "any" unpaid amounts due. The criminal defendant pled guilty; the trial court then assessed fines, court costs, and fees. However, the clerk of the court withheld the balance of the cash bond to cover outstanding amounts owed on the criminal defendant's three other criminal cases. That left nothing to remit. The trial court certified the questions to the appellate court about whether the relevant statute allowing bond amounts to be withheld, § 903.286, Fla. Stat. (2007), was constitutional and whether cash bond amounts could be applied to multiple cases. The appellate court found that the statute did not violate constitutional guarantees of procedural due process, equal protection, proper takings, single subject, or excessive bail. It also determined that the statute expressly stated that cash on the bond could be withheld on "any" amounts due and did not limit the amount to the immediately relevant case.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's finding that the statute was constitutional. It reversed the trial court's finding that the cash bond could only be used to pay for outstanding amounts due in the criminal matter at issue rather than all of the outstanding amounts due regarding a particular defendant's cases.

St. Johns River Water Mgmt. Dist. v. Koontz


Case No. 5D06-1116


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


5 So. 3d 8; 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 91; 34 Fla. L. Weekly D 123



January 9, 2009, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Release for Publication April 8, 2009.
Motion granted by, Question certified by St. Johns River Water Mgmt. Dist. v. Koontz, 5 So. 3d 8, 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 2267 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., 2009)
Rehearing denied by St. Johns River Water Mgmt. Dist. v. Koontz, 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 8179 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Mar. 20, 2009)
Rehearing denied by, Rehearing, en banc, denied by St. Johns River Water Mgmt. Dist. v. Koontz, 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 21362 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Mar. 20, 2009)
Review granted by St. Johns River Water Mgmt. Dist. v. Koontz, 15 So. 3d 581, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1639 (Fla., 2009)
Quashed by, Remanded by St. Johns River Water Mgmt. Dist. v. Koontz, 77 So. 3d 1220, 2011 Fla. LEXIS 2617 (Fla., 2011)
Remanded by St. Johns River Water Mgmt. Dist. v. Koontz, 129 So. 3d 1069, 2013 Fla. LEXIS 2357 (Fla., 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, Joseph P. Baker, Judge.
St. Johns River Water Mgmt. Dist. v. Koontz, 908 So. 2d 518, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 9774 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee owner of property sued appellant water management district (district), alleging inverse condemnation of his property resulting from an improper "exaction" by the district. The Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida) awarded damages to the owner. The district appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owner had sought permits needed to develop his property. The district replied that it would approve the permits only if the owner agreed to satisfy certain conditions, one of which was the performance of "off-site" mitigation involving property a considerable distance from the owner's property. The owner claimed that the conditions were unreasonable and rejected the offer. The district then denied the permits. The district argued that the lower court never had subject matter jurisdiction because § 373.617(2), Fla. Stat. expressly limited the scope of circuit court review to cases in which a constitutional taking was proven. The district argued that the owner's claim was really a challenge to the merits of the permit denial, which, it argued, may only have been pursued in an administrative proceeding, and that no exaction occurred because nothing was exacted from the owner. The appellate court disagreed. An exaction claim was cognizable when, as here, the land owner refused to agree to an improper request from the government resulting in a permit denial. Any requirement that a developer provide or do something as a condition to receiving approval was an exaction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1431 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


O'Brien v. State Farm Fire & Cas. Co.


CASE NO. 1D08-0175


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


999 So. 2d 1081; 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 79; 34 Fla. L. Weekly D 110



January 8, 2009, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An appeal from the Circuit Court for Duval County. Lance Day, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an insurance coverage dispute, the Circuit Court for Duval County (Florida) entered summary judgment in favor of appellee insurers. It held that under § 627.727(2), Fla. Stat. (2003), appellant insured had no uninsured (UM) or underinsured motorist coverage under his personal liability umbrella policy because he had rejected such coverage at the time he applied for the policy. The insured appealed.


OVERVIEW: The insured rejected UM coverage in 1992. The insured never sought to rescind his 1992 rejection and never communicated with the insurers on the subject. The court stated that § 627.727(2) required only that an issuer of a non-primary policy notify an applicant of the availability of UM coverage, which the insurers had done. It rejected the insured's argument that he was entitled to UM coverage because changes had been made to the policy from time to time, including the addition of new vehicles that had not been previously registered in Florida. Unlike the case relied upon by the insured, the case here involved the same umbrella policy initially issued in Florida in 1992 to the same named insured, bearing the same policy number and providing coverage in the same amount. Next, the unambiguous language in § 627.727(2) trumped any and all canons of interpretation, and the 1984 amendments to the statute treated excess policies differently from primary policies. Finally, the failure of the rejection form to track the language of § 627.727(1), which did not apply to excess policies such as the umbrella policy at issue here, did not render the 1992 rejection form ambiguous or deficient.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

Kovaleski v. State


No. 4D06-1168


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


1 So. 3d 254; 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 42; 34 Fla. L. Weekly D 79



January 5, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Kovaleski v. State, 65 So. 3d 516, 2011 Fla. LEXIS 1838 (Fla., 2011)
Approved by Kovaleski v. State, 2012 Fla. LEXIS 2138 (Fla., Oct. 25, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Indian River County; Dan L. Vaughn, Judge; L.T. Case No. 98-278 CFA.
Kovaleski v. State, 854 So. 2d 282, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 13973 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Indian River County, (Florida) that convicted him of two counts of lewd and lascivious acts involving a minor male; defendant claimed, inter alia, that the trial court erred in allowing the victim to be cross-examined about a prior false accusation of sexual misconduct, and in partially closing the courtroom during the minor's testimony.


OVERVIEW: After defendant's first trial, his convictions were reversed and remanded for a new trial because the trial court improperly closed the courtroom during the testimony of the minor without having a hearing to determine if it was necessary. During the cross-examination of the minor in defendant's retrial, defendant's counsel asked if he had ever made an accusation about someone else having sex with him and later withdrawn it. The appellate court found, inter alia, that a proffer was necessary since the record was silent as to whether the minor had ever made such an accusation or withdrawn it. It was not clear if such evidence would have been admissible. Accordingly, the issue was not preserved. Defendant's right to a public trial was not violated since section 918.16, Florida Statutes (2001) allowed partial closure during the limited time in which the minor testified about the sex offense. Because defendant attempted to solicit the murder of the prosecutor and the victim while he was awaiting retrial, his vindictive argument was without merit.


OUTCOME: The convictions and closure were affirmed, and the matter was remanded for resentencing; conflict was certified on a sentencing issue involving credit for time served where there were multiple sentences.

 

1433 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Scotts Co. v. Linda


No. 3D08-345


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


2 So. 3d 1013; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 19361; 34 Fla. L. Weekly D 18



December 24, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 12, 2009.
Rehearing denied by Scotts Co. v. Linda, 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 6703 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., Mar. 12, 2009)
Review denied by Linda v. Scotts Co., 17 So. 3d 292, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1310 (Fla., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, David C. Miller, Judge. Lower Tribunal No. 04-8937.
Scotts Co. v. Hacienda Loma Linda, 942 So. 2d 900, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 9088 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a company and its employee, sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County (Florida), which reinstated a lawsuit filed by appellee, a Panamanian corporation, that had previously been dismissed for forum non conveniens.


OVERVIEW: The employee allegedly met the corporation's president at a trade show in Florida and recommended the use of one of the company's products for the corporation's orchids. The product allegedly destroyed thousands of the corporation's orchids in Panama. The corporation's president maintained a home office in Miami, and the corporation initially filed its lawsuit for damages there. After the action was dismissed for forum non conveniens, Panama had enacted a law to block transfers based on forum non conveniens. A Panamanian court declined jurisdiction, and the case was reinstated in Florida, but subsequently, the Panamanian law was found unconstitutional. An appeal in Panama was pending. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. Based on the decision in Kinney Systems, Inc. v. Continental Insurance Co., 674 So.2d 86 (Fla. 1996), the case should have remained in Panama as the injury occurred there and the damages were suffered by a Panamanian corporation. The court noted that the corporation's appeal in Panama was not in good faith but, on its face, an intentional effort to obtain an affirmance of the dismissal of the case in Panama as further support for reinstatement in Florida.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of reinstatement and remanded the case to the trial court for dismissal. That dismissal was not to include a retention of jurisdiction in the event the Panamanian court dismissed the action on grounds of preemption or a blocking statute. The court was to retain jurisdiction under Florida Rule of Civil Procedure 1.061(h) to enforce the stipulations in Rule 1.061 and in the instant opinion.

Ibarrondo v. State


Case No. 5D08-813


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


1 So. 3d 226; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 20619; 34 Fla. L. Weekly D 71



December 24, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected.

Released for Publication January 15, 2009.
Review denied by Ibarrondo v. State, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1617 (Fla., Sept. 22, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Osceola County, Jeffords D. Miller, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Circuit Court for Osceola County (Florida) convicted defendant of driving under the influence (DUI) with three prior convictions for that offense, and driving while license suspended with two prior convictions for that offense. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court committed error by refusing to strike a juror for cause. The juror had opined rather steadfastly that he would give more credibility to a police officer than to defendant or to other witnesses. The appellate court found that, while the juror was rehabilitated to some extent by the prosecution, upon examination by the defense, he restated his partiality for police officers. The trial court erred in seating that person as a juror, and accordingly, a reversal was required. The trial court's admission into evidence of the court file in of one of defendant's prior DUI convictions and the publishing of information in that file to the jury was an affront to fairness and was reversible. The rational connection test was satisfied by section 316.193(12), Florida Statues (2007), and, as applied to defendant, was constitutional. As the driving record, uncontested, was sufficient evidence for the jury to find beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was the person convicted of the prior offenses enumerated in the record, the trial court did not err in denying his motion for judgment of acquittal.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial. A question was certified to the Supreme Court of Florida.

 

1435 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Grosso v. State


No. 4D07-4718


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


2 So. 3d 362; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 19373; 34 Fla. L. Weekly D 24



December 24, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Michael L. Gates, Judge; L.T. Case No. 06-11956 CF 10 A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order by the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), that modified his probation to include electronic monitoring more than 60 days after the probationary sentence was imposed; defendant challenged the modification on double jeopardy and jurisdictional grounds.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was placed on probation for unlawful sexual activity involving a minor victim, he pleaded no contest to his failure to register as required by § 775.21(8)(a), Fla. Stat., and was placed on five years of sexual offender probation. Approximately 11 months later, the trial court granted the Department of Corrections' motion to add electronic monitoring as a condition of defendant's probation. The appellate court found, inter alia, that pursuant to § 948.30, Fla. Stat., the trial court was required to impose electronic monitoring as a mandatory condition of probation because of defendant's prior convictions for violations of ch. 794 and § 800.04, 948.30(3) Fla. Stat. However, because the Department was not seeking to modify the probation order, but to add electronic monitoring, pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(c), the trial court had only 60 days after sentencing to modify the order to include the condition.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed, and the matter was remanded with directions to strike electronic monitoring as a condition of defendant's probation.

 

1436 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Kountze v. Kountze


Case No. 2D07-4881


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


996 So. 2d 246; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 18618; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 2830



December 12, 2008, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from nonfinal order of the Circuit Court for Collier County; Cynthia A. Ellis, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Collier County (Florida) denied appellant foreign state resident's motion to dismiss the complaint filed by appellee cousin for lack of personal jurisdiction after the cousin sued the foreign state resident for taping a phone conversation without the cousin's permission in violation of the Florida Security of Communications Act, § 934.03, Fla. Stat. (2002). The foreign state resident appealed.


OVERVIEW: The foreign state resident and the cousin were first cousins. The foreign state resident lived in Nebraska. The cousin lived in Colorado. Both of them were board members of a Nebraska charitable foundation. They were apparently on opposite sides of a dispute. The cousin went to Florida to visit his father. The cousin in Florida called the foreign state resident in Nebraska. During the call, the foreign state resident placed his wireless phone handset near a tape recorder and recorded the conversation without the cousin's consent. Later, the foreign state resident played part of the recording to his wife. The cousin eventually sued for violation of the Florida Security of Communications Act, § 934.03, Fla. Stat. (2002) for the recording of the phone conversation without the cousin's permission. The trial court denied the foreign state resident's motion to dismiss for lack of personal jurisdiction, based on Koch. The appellate court rejected the reasoning in Koch and held that the long-arm statute, § 48.193(1)(b), Fla. Stat. (2002), did not provide a basis for personal jurisdiction over the foreign state resident because he did not engage in any actions inside Florida.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

1440 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Amorin v. Gordon


No. 4D08-1376


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


996 So. 2d 913; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 18061; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 2764



December 3, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Amorin v. Gordon, 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 18219 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Jan. 14, 2009)
Review denied by Gordon v. Amorin, 16 So. 3d 132, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 883 (Fla., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal of a non-final order from the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Indian River County; Robert A. Hawley, Judge; L.T. Case No. 20040655 CA10.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee personal representative brought a negligence action against appellants, a sub-subcontractor and his driver ("first driver"). The Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Indian River County (Florida) entered partial summary judgment denying appellants workers' compensation immunity under § 440.10(1)(e), Fla. Stat. (2004) and granted appellee's cross-motion for summary judgment. Appellants challenged the trial court's decision.


OVERVIEW: Appellee's decedent was killed when his dump truck and the first driver's truck collided. Both the first driver and the decedent were working for sub-subcontractors on a road construction project, and both worked for the same general contractor. The court stated that under § 440.10, the general contractor was the statutory employer of appellants. Because the subcontractor and the sub-subcontractor both failed to obtain workers' compensation, the general contractor was responsible for providing such coverage to appellants, and its policy provided for just that. Thus, because appellants were covered by the general contractor's policy and because appellee did not assert that the major contributing cause of the accident was the first driver's gross negligence, appellants were entitled to horizontal immunity. Next, § 440.10(1)(e) did not violate Fla. Const. art. I, § 21 by depriving appellee of the common law right to sue. Had appellee been able to show that the first driver was grossly negligent, she could have sued appellants in tort; thus, the right to sue had not been completely abolished. Moreover, the decedent's survivors had been beneficiaries of workers' compensation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the partial summary judgment for appellee. It directed the trial court to enter summary judgment for appellants.

Duval County Sch. Bd. v. State Bd. of Educ.


CASE NO. 1D07-6041


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


998 So. 2d 641; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 18030; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 2743



December 2, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 6, 2009.
Related proceeding at Sch. Bd. v. State Bd. of Educ. of Fla., 1 So. 3d 205, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 18036 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Dec. 2, 2008)
Related proceeding at Dist. Sch. Bd. v. State Bd. of Educ., 998 So. 2d 648, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 18039 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Dec. 2, 2008)

Related proceeding at Sch. Bd. of Broward County v. State Bd. of Educ., 998 So. 2d 645, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 18024 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Dec. 2, 2008)
Related proceeding at St. Lucie County Sch. Bd. v. State Bd. of Educ., 998 So. 2d 645, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 18034 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist. 2008)
Related proceeding at Sch. Bd. v. Fla. State Bd. of Educ., 998 So. 2d 646, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 18031 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Dec. 2, 2008)
Related proceeding at Sch. Bd. v. State Bd. of Educ., 998 So. 2d 647, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 18025 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Dec. 2, 2008)
Related proceeding at Sch. Bd. of Volusia County v. State, 998 So. 2d 646, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 18038 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2008)
Related proceeding at Sch. Bd. of Martin County v. State Bd. of Educ., 998 So. 2d 649, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 18026 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Dec. 2, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An appeal from an order of the Department of Education.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee State Board of Education (Florida) entered a decision pursuant to § 1002.335, Fla. Stat. (2006) that allowed three school boards to retain their exclusive power to authorize charter schools in their respective districts, but denied the resolutions of 28 other schools boards to retain that power. Appellant school boards appealed and challenged the constitutionality of § 1002.335, Fla. Stat. (2006).


OVERVIEW: The Florida legislature enacted § 1002.335, Fla. Stat. (2006), which established the "Florida Schools of Excellence Commission" to authorize charter schools throughout Florida. Under § 1002.335, Fla. Stat. (2006), the district school boards could exercise that exclusive authority only if the State Board of Education granted them such power. Multiple school boards sought to retain that exclusive authority. After conducting hearings, the State Board of Education allowed only three school boards to retain their exclusive authority; the requests of the remaining school boards were denied. Several school boards then challenged the constitutionality of § 1002.335, Fla. Stat. (2006). The appellate court found that the statute totally and fatally conflicted with Art. IX, § 4, Fla. Const., which gave the school boards the power to operate public education, because the statute allowed the commission to operate charter schools as a public education alternative. The appellate court also found that it did not matter that only a few schools would be operated as charter schools as an allegedly small constitutional violation was not less important than an larger constitutional violation.


OUTCOME: The appellate court found that the statute was facially unconstitutional.
