Oquendo v. State


No. 4D08-651


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


2 So. 3d 1001; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 17849; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 2721



November 26, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at Oquendo v. State, 117 So. 3d 1105, 2013 Fla. App. LEXIS 9791 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2013)
Post-conviction relief denied at Oquendo v. State, 195 So. 3d 389, 2015 Fla. App. LEXIS 8099 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2015)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Magistrate's recommendation at Oquendo v. Jones, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 14802 (S.D. Fla., Feb. 1, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal of order denying rule 3.850 motion from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Peter Weinstein, Judge; L.T. Case No. 97-895 CF10C.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the summary denial of his Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion by the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida). The trial court in this case found that defendant had violated the terms of his plea agreement. Defendant listed more than twelve claims that attacked the voluntariness of his plea and raised other matters.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to drug-related crimes. As part of the plea, he entered into a substantial assistance agreement with the State and agreed to work with a detective in making drug-related arrests. A tape recording of defendant agreeing to the terms of the substantial assistance agreement was created. A factual dispute existed as to whether defendant provided assistance or not, but he admitted that he fled and changed his name. The appellate court held that most of the claims were conclusorily alleged and did not merit relief. The State did not attach any records regarding what transpired when the plea was entered, such as a transcript of a plea hearing or a written plea form. Thus, the appellate court could not determine whether the terms discussed in the taped substantial assistance agreement were incorporated into the plea that defendant entered before the court. In addition, the tape offered to refute defendant's claims was not authenticated. While the person on the tape appeared to have understood what was occurring and declined the assistance of an interpreter, the tape alone did not refute defendant's claims regarding what occurred when he entered his plea.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed. On remand, if records regarding the plea agreement could not be obtained, then an evidentiary hearing might be required to establish what transpired at the plea hearing and to permit defendant an opportunity to prove any of his facially sufficient claims. In addition, defendant was to have a reasonable opportunity to amend any insufficiently-pleaded claims.

 

1457 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Drake v. Walton County


CASE NO. 1D07-3202


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 17597; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 2710



November 21, 2008, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:

NOT FINAL UNTIL TIME EXPIRES TO FILE MOTION FOR REHEARING AND DISPOSITION THEREOF IF FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, Rehearing, en banc, denied by, Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at, Remanded by Cozette Drake v. Walton County, 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 3236 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Apr. 14, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
An appeal from the Circuit Court for Walton County. W. Howard Laporte, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the successor trustee of two trusts, sought review of a final judgment of the Circuit Court for Walton County, Florida, entered in favor of appellee county on claims that included inverse condemnation. That claim involved the county's diversion of water across a portion of property originally purchased by the trustee's deceased parents.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court affirmed as to all issues except the inverse condemnation claim. Before the parents purchased the property in 1988, a ditch draining a lake's outflow had been stabilized and did not discharge water across the property. That drainage was not changed until the county acted in 1995 to alleviate flooding across a neighbor's property caused by a hurricane. Efforts to restabilize the water flow failed. The continued flow, caused by the county, not the hurricane, constituted a taking. The fact that water flowed across the property prior to 1988 was not legally relevant. The county could not choose to act and protect the property of one owner by diverting floodwater onto the trust property without compensation to the trustee. By allowing the water to flow long after the emergency had passed, the county had conferred a public benefit on other property owners rather than preventing a public harm. Further, while § 252.43(6), Fla. Stat. allowed the county to act in an emergency, that did not preclude the trustee, as an innocent property owner from initiating her takings claim. The statute could not restrict the rights granted to the trustee under Art. X, § 6, Fla. Const.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the final judgment and remanded the matter with directions that judgment be entered for the trustee on her inverse condemnation claim and that a determination of the value of the taking be made.

 

1458 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Allen


Case No. 5D07-4418


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


994 So. 2d 1192; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 17280; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 2653



November 14, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 8, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, Bob Leblanc, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed an order by the Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida) which granted the motion of defendant to suppress certain evidence seized during an investigatory stop because his clothing did not match an informant's written description.


OVERVIEW: The police received information from a reliable confidential informant that he had just purchased crack cocaine in a parking lot which was in a high crime area. The informant gave a verbal description of two men. The officers subsequently saw defendant and two other persons who allegedly matched the verbal description. When the individuals saw the officers, they began to walk away hurriedly. The individual with defendant threw an item that turned out to be crack cocaine under a parked truck. The officers caught up with defendant they discovered him holding several pieces of crack cocaine. The officers did not see the informant's written description until after the arrest. Neither defendant, nor his companion were the person who actually sold the contraband to the informant. The appellate court held that, under the circumstances, the written description was not relevant to the legal determination before it. For constitutional purposes the court could only evaluate the information in the possession of the officers at the time of the stop. The investigatory stop was valid as the officers had a reasonable suspicion to believe that defendant was involved in criminal activity.


OUTCOME: The suppression order was reversed and the matter was remanded for further proceedings.

 

1459 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Montas


Case No. 5D07-3962


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


993 So. 2d 1127; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 16563; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 2560



October 31, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 24, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the County Court for Orange County, Wayne Shoemaker, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with wearing a uniform and insignia of rank in violation of § 250.43, Fla. Stat. (2007). The County Court for Orange County (Florida) held that the statute was unconstitutionally overbroad and violated the Due Process Clause. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: A Transportation Security Administration agent at an airport saw defendant, wearing a U.S. Army uniform, standing in a lane used by military and security personnel. He became suspicious when he noticed that defendant's hair was longer than allowed in the military. Defendant admitted that he was not in the Army. The court rejected the State's argument that defendant's conduct was not protected by the First Amendment. The court could conceive of situations where a person might wear part of a military uniform to communicate a message, such as to express support for the troops or to protest military action. Thus, the court had to determine whether the statute was supported by a compelling governmental interest and was narrowly drawn to protect that interest. While the state had a compelling interest in ensuring that the public was not deceived by people impersonating members of the military, the statute had no element of specific intent to deceive. Without such an element, it criminalized both innocent, protected conduct and unprotected conduct, and was on that basis both overbroad and a violation of due process. There was no way to read the statute more narrowly without rewriting it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1460 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Petion


Case No. 2D07-1549


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


992 So. 2d 889; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 19286; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 2505



October 24, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 18, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Sarasota County; Frederick A. DeFuria, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed an order by the Circuit Court for Sarasota County (Florida) which granted defendant's motion to suppress physical evidence, primarily powder cocaine, which was found in a secret compartment inside a car he was driving as a result of a traffic stop. The trial court concluded that, while defendant initially consented to a search, he withdrew his consent by nonverbal communication.


OVERVIEW: An officer stopped defendant as his windows were heavily tinted and the tag light was inoperable. Defendant consented to a search of the car, including any containers and compartments. An officer found an "after-market compartment" in the right rear passenger area. It took two officers approximately an hour to open the secret compartment. Inside they found more than 270 grams of powder cocaine. Defendant argued, inter alia, that he had withdrawn consent to search after the deputies found the compartment, but before they opened it. He also argued that the destructive nature of the search, forcing open the secret compartment, was beyond the scope of his consent. The trial court also based its decision on the officer's failure to use an available videorecorder to record the consent. Accepting the trial court's findings of fact, the appellate court concluded that the State established that defendant took no action that an objectively reasonable police officer would interpret as a withdrawal of his consent to search, including the consent to search the secret compartment. Also, an officer was not required to record a roadside consent to fulfill the requirements of the Fourth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the matter was remanded for further proceedings.

 

1461 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Harvey v. State


Case No. 2D08-4399


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


32 So. 3d 61; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 16313; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 2447



October 22, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 22, 2010.
Review dismissed by Harvey v. Balkwill, 1 So. 3d 172, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 2495 (Fla., Dec. 31, 2008)
Writ denied by Harvey v. Balkwill, 3 So. 3d 316, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 231 (Fla., Jan. 30, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Sarasota County; Robert B. Bennett, Jr., Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a case involving appellant father's child support obligation pursuant to a November 2007 dissolution order, the father appealed the order of the Circuit Court for Sarasota County (Florida), which found him guilty of indirect criminal contempt pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.840 and sentenced him to 90 days in the county jail.


OVERVIEW: Because criminal contempt was a crime in the ordinary sense, imposition of criminal contempt sanctions required that a contemnor be afforded the same constitutional due process protections afforded to criminal defendants. These rights included the right not to incriminate oneself. The appellate court concluded that the trial court erred in the indirect criminal contempt proceeding when it allowed itself to be persuaded by the argument of the former wife's attorney that the right not to be compelled to incriminate oneself did not apply in such a proceeding. Thus, the trial court erred in compelling the father to testify against himself and the error was not harmless because when the father's testimony was removed from consideration, the remaining evidence was insufficient to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that he willfully violated a prior court order. Essentially, the only competent evidence before the court was the father's child support payment record and the former wife's testimony that the father was not assisting her financially.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's order and remanded the case for a new hearing. The trial court was directed to enter an order releasing the father to the bail status to which he was admitted as of the show-cause hearing or, if he was not admitted to bail, an order releasing him from confinement.

Amisub North Ridge Hosp., Inc. v. Sonaglia


No. 4D08-2448


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


995 So. 2d 999; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 16318; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 2477



October 22, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at, Review denied by Amisub North Ridge Hosp., Inc. v. Sonaglia, 13 So. 3d 57, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 995 (Fla., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Petition for writ of certiorari to the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Carol-Lisa Phillips, Judge; L.T. Case No. 06-019500(25).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner hospital sought certiorari review of an order of the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), which directed that the hospital produce peer review materials pursuant to Art. X, § 25, Fla. Const. in respondent doctor's action against defendant doctor that alleged both defamation and tortious interference with an advantageous business relationship.


OVERVIEW: Respondent claimed that defendant tried to take patients away from her and that when respondent tried to get her patients back, defendant defamed her to get her thrown off the hospital's medical staff. A former patient of respondent's filed an affidavit requesting that any hospital records pertaining to any adverse medical incident involving the patient be turned over to her and respondent's attorney; she claimed that after a successful surgery performed by respondent, defendant removed her as a patient of respondent's and listed her as one of defendant's patients. The hospital refused to produce peer review materials. The court denied the petition. Art. X, § 25 had removed any barrier to a patient's discovery of adverse medical incident information, including peer review protections previously provided by § 381.028, Fla. Stat. (2005), which had been declared unconstitutional. Art. X, § 25 only required that a patient request the materials and did not require that the information be sought for any type of proper purpose and be relevant to a medical malpractice action. Once the information was obtained, the patient was not limited as to whom the patient could reveal the information.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition for certiorari.

New Testament Baptist Church Inc. v. State

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, the State of Florida, Department of Transportation, brought an eminent domain proceeding against appellant church in the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida). The trial court granted summary judgment to the Department and the county on the church's counterclaim. The church appealed.

1464 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


W.M. v. State


Case No. 5D07-3762


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


992 So. 2d 383; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 15416; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 2384



October 10, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 29, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, Lawrence R. Kirkwood, Judge.
McKinney v. State, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 12484 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Aug. 22, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On a motion for rehearing, appellant psychiatric patient appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Orange County, Florida, subjecting her to six months of additional involuntary mental health treatment pursuant to § 394.467(6), Fla. Stat. (2007). Appellee was the State of Florida.


OVERVIEW: Police found the patient in an agitated state at an airport and took her to a hospital for an involuntary mental health evaluation under the Baker Act, § 394.463, Fla. Stat. (2007). At the hospital's request, the circuit court committed her for three weeks of inpatient treatment at the hospital under Florida's Mental Health Act, § 394.467, Fla. Stat. (2007). When she did not respond to treatment, the circuit court committed her for six additional months of involuntary inpatient psychiatric treatment at a state-run mental health facility under § 394.467(6), Fla. Stat. (2007). The patient argued that the circuit court lacked jurisdiction to order the additional treatment. On appeal, the court held that because the initial period was for short-term treatment at a receiving facility, the circuit court retained concurrent jurisdiction to order further treatment. The court rejected the patient's argument that, under § 394.467(7), Fla. Stat. (2007), any hearing for continued treatment was required to be administrative. The legislature intended to give the circuit court jurisdiction for short-term treatment up to six months, while long-term treatment required administrative hearings.


OUTCOME: The court granted the patient's motion for rehearing, withdrew its prior opinion and substituted a new opinion using the patient's initials to maintain her confidentiality, and affirmed the decision of the circuit court. The court ordered that access to the patient's file be restricted and that the file be treated as confidential.

1466 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Sch. Bd. v. Carralero


No. 3D08-1101


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


992 So. 2d 353; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 15129; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 2329



October 1, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 31, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
A Non-final Appeal from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Thomas S. Wilson, Judge. Lower Tribunal No. 08-18026.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee employee sued appellant school board, challenging the school board's action in barring the employee from school property pursuant to §§ 1012.465, 1012.467, Fla. Stat., because of his nolo contendere plea to child abuse. The Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County (Florida) enjoined the school board from barring the employee, and then denied the school board's motion to dissolve the injunction. The school board appealed.


OVERVIEW: After the employee was barred from school property, his employment with a third party was terminated. The employee argued that §§ 1012.465, 1012.467, Fla. Stat., were unconstitutional as applied to him, claiming that they retroactively converted his nolo contendere plea into a conviction thereby depriving him of "his vested rights" to come onto the school board's property. In identifying the employee's vested right, the trial court referred to the employee's "loss of a job" and the employee's right to come on the school board's property. However, the appellate court found that the school board neither terminated the employee's employment nor demanded that his employment be terminated. And, neither the order under review, nor the employee, cited a basis for claiming a vested right to go onto school grounds. Rather, it had always been left to the school board's discretion whether to allow a workman such as the employee to enter onto school property. Because the employee failed to demonstrate that the school board's actions divested him of a right of present enjoyment, or a present fixed right of future enjoyment, he did meet the requirements necessary for issuance of an injunction.


OUTCOME: The order denying the school board's motion to dissolve the temporary injunction was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Jomolla v. State


Nos. 3D07-2857 & 3D06-3093


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


990 So. 2d 1234; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 14650; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 2268



September 24, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at Jomolla v. State, 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 13933 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., Sept. 16, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeals from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Leon Firtel, Judge. Lower Tribunal No. F02-35178.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant of battery evidencing prejudice. The trial court sentenced defendant as a habitual violent offender to seven years imprisonment with a mandatory minimum of five years under §§ 784.03, 775.085, and 775.084(4), Fla. Stat. (2002). The Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County (Florida) issued its denial of defendant's Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(b) motion to correct a sentencing error. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was white, attacked the victim, who was African American, at a convenience store. While the appellate court concluded that the trial court erred in instructing the jury as to both forms of battery listed in § 784.03, Fla. Stat., where the information only charged that defendant committed battery by actually and intentionally touching or striking the victim, the appellate court also found the error did not amount to fundamental error, requiring a new trial, because defendant admitted to striking the victim and thus, the erroneous in instruction did not concern a disputed jury issue. The admission of an officer's testimony that defendant called him a racial slur was not erroneous, because the comment was made shortly after the charged incident and was relevant to the issue of defendant's motivation in striking the victim. The appellate court further concluded that § 775.085, Fla. Stat., was not unconstitutional on its face or as applied to defendant. Finally, the appellate court concluded that the Miranda form used was legally sufficient, as held by the court in a prior action.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Childers v. Dep't of Mgmt. Servs., Div. of Ret.


No. 4D07-4230


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


989 So. 2d 716; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 12681; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 2056



August 27, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 12, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the State of Florida, Department of Management Services, Division of Retirement; L.T. Case No. 07-2128.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee State of Florida, Department of Management Services, Division of Retirement entered a final order forfeiting appellant former employee's pension. The former employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The former employee was convicted for bribery and receipt of unlawful compensation or reward for official behavior. Based on this, his pension was forfeited. He challenged the forfeiture of the full amount of his pension, and argued that § 112.3173, Fla. Stat. was unconstitutional because, as applied, it violated his constitutional protections against excessive fines, double jeopardy, and ex-post facto laws. The employee suggested that the forfeiture should have applied only to that part of the pension that accrued during his tenure as a county commissioner and not to part that accrued while he served as a teacher and legislator. The appellate court held that the forfeiture was not a fine because the employee was not ordered to pay anything to the government. The Double Jeopardy Clause was not violated by the forfeiture. There was no second prosecution. The employee was not receiving multiple punishments for the same offense. Because § 112.3173(3), Fla. Stat. (2003) was enacted before the employee committed the crimes for which he was convicted, § 112.3173 did not reach back in time and did not violate the proscription against ex post facto laws.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

1469 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


McKinney v. State


Case No. 5D07-3762


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 12484; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 2036



August 22, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing granted by, Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at W.M. v. State, 992 So. 2d 383, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 15416 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Oct. 10, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, Lawrence R. Kirkwood, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee State brought a petition for involuntary inpatient placement to request involuntary psychiatric care for appellant patient. After an initial three week placement, the Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida) ordered six additional months of treatment. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: The patient argued that the trial court lacked jurisdiction to order the continued treatment. The appellate court found, based on a full reading § 394.467, Fla. Stat., that the procedure followed by the trial court was proper. Because the initial three week treatment period was short-term treatment at a receiving facility, the trial court retained jurisdiction to order further treatment. The initial treatment ordered for the patient was at a hospital which fit the statutory definition of a "receiving facility." Thus, when the administrator of this receiving facility filed a petition for continued involuntary placement, the receiving facility administrator was not required to file with the Division of Administrative Hearings under Fla. Admin. Code Ann. R. 65E-5.300, which, consistent with § 394.467(7)(b), Fla. Stat., only required "treatment facility" administrators to have done so. More importantly, because the treatment ordered was short-term, the trial court properly exercised jurisdiction to order further treatment. However, once long-term treatment was ordered, a petition for continued treatment was required to have been addressed in an administrative hearing under § 394.467.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Colgate-Palmolive Co. v. Fla. Dep't of Revenue


CASE NO. 1D07-1051


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


988 So. 2d 1212; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 15295; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 2009



August 20, 2008, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An appeal from the Department of Revenue. Jim Zingale, Executive Director.
Colgate-Palmolive Co. v. Fla. Dep't of Revenue, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 8101 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., June 2, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee Department of Revenue (Florida) entered a decision that found Florida's limitation pursuant to § 220.13(1), Fla. Stat. (2004) of net operating loss carryovers under I.R.C. § 172 did not improperly discriminate against foreign corporate dividends. Appellant taxpayer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer, a corporation making and selling products nationally and worldwide, sued and claimed that Florida's treatment of domestic versus foreign dividends for tax purposes discriminated because losses created by domestic dividend deductions could always be carried over while the foreign tax credit, calculated through the payment of foreign dividends, could not. The taxpayer based its discrimination claim on the foreign Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, and the Equal Protection Clause, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, 1, and asserted that the limit under § 220.13(1), Fla. Stat. (2004) on net loss carryovers pursuant to I.R.C. § 172 discriminated against foreign corporate dividends. The department found against it. The appellate court then determined that Florida's taxing scheme did not facially discriminate against foreign corporate dividends because Florida went "above and beyond" the federal governments treatment of foreign dividends by offering corporations the ability to carry over net operating losses resulting from the deduction of foreign taxes paid and the possible deduction of other significant foreign dividends based on those same excluded foreign source dividends.


OUTCOME: The appellate court denied the taxpayer's motion for rehearing and affirmed the department's decision.

Denhart v. State


Case No. 5D07-13


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


987 So. 2d 1257; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 12136; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 1990



August 15, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 4, 2008.
Review denied by Denhart v. State, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 22 (Fla., Jan. 5, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Marion County, Hale R. Stancil, Judge.
Denhart v. State, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 7814 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., May 30, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Circuit Court for Marion County (Florida) convicted defendant of promoting a sexual performance by a child, § 827.071, Fla. Stat. (2005). Defendant was then adjudicated a sexual predator. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that § 827.071 required a showing that the child victim made contact with one of the designated sexual areas of another person and that there was no evidence to that effect. The appellate court disagreed. Section 827.071(3), Fla. Stat., as written, defined sexual conduct broadly enough to cover contact by one party with the designated sexual areas of another party regardless of whether the child victim made the contact or received the contact. The trial court did not err in issuing a jury instruction regarding the fact that defendant's ignorance of the victim's age, the victim's misrepresentation of her age, or defendant's bona fide belief of the victim's age, was not a defense. The trial court did not err in admitting photos of defendant's house because the photos were relevant to corroborate the testimony presented by the State's witnesses concerning the fact that the crime took place inside defendant's home and to refute a claim that the photos of the child victim were altered by use of computer software. Defendant was properly adjudicated a sexual predator. There was no due process violation in applying § 775.21, Fla. Stat. (2007) in this situation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Morton v. State


CASE NO. 1D07-1623


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


988 So. 2d 698; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 11884; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 1961



August 8, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 26, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. Kathleen F. Dekker, Judge.
Harris v. State, 987 So. 2d 807, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 11883 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Aug. 8, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida), which convicted him upon a jury verdict of felony hazing in violation of § 1006.63(2), Fla. Stat. (2005).


OVERVIEW: The statute criminalized hazing as a rite of initiation into student organizations and made it a felony to participate in hazing activities that resulted in "serious bodily injury." Defendant challenged the constitutionality of § 1006.63(2), arguing that the statute was facially void for vagueness because it did not specify what constituted "serious bodily injury." The court, however, rejected defendant's facial challenge because the statute was not vague in light of the facts of the case, which showed that defendant participated in a two-day caning ritual during which the victim sustained 150 cane strikes to his buttocks. The victim's physician testified that he sustained a hematoma that required surgical removal. The court also rejected defendant's challenge to the sufficiency of the evidence. The court, however, found that defendant was entitled to a new trial because of an erroneous jury instruction that impermissibly narrowed the range of findings jurors could have made in order to acquit. The instruction on the definition of "serious bodily injury" effectively allowed the jury to convict if they found that the victim's injuries were anything more than "slight."


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction, and it remanded the case for a new trial.

Scheible v. Joseph L. Morse Geriatric Ctr., Inc.


No. 4D07-3064


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


988 So. 2d 1130; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 11606; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 1873



July 30, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 15, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; David F. Crow, Judge; L.T. Case No. CL 97-7021 AO.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant personal representative of decedent's estate sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), in her favor and against appellee nursing home as to a breach of contract action in regard to resuscitative measures being taken contrary to the decedent's expressed will and from the trial court's order denying her motion for prejudgment interest.


OVERVIEW: The decedent was admitted to the nursing home at the age of 89. At the time, she had an admitting diagnosis of senile dementia and a seizure disorder. The nursing home signed a living will/advance directive that stated there were to be no life-prolonging treatments or resuscitative measures taken if she had a terminal condition or was in the process of dying. The nursing home staff found the decedent unresponsive, but breathing, in her bed. They called 911. EMS intubated the decedent and took her to the hospital. During transport, she was placed in physical restraints. She was subsequently extubated and died several days later of cardiopulmonary arrest. The appellate court held that the immediate wrong suffered was akin to wrongful prolongation of life. The trial court was correct that prejudgment interest depended on the nature of the damages claimed. Thus, the fact that the estate recovered under a breach of contract theory should not automatically entitle it to prejudgment interest if the nature of damages was inappropriate for such interest. Although the estate's action was technically for breach of contract, the damages sought involved unliquidated personal injury damages.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Brookins v. Ford Credit Titling Trust


No. 4D07-2010


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 10881; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 1780



July 16, 2008, Decided


NOTICE:

NOT FINAL UNTIL DISPOSITION OF TIMELY FILED MOTION FOR REHEARING.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing granted by, En banc, Opinion withdrawn by Brookins v. Ford Credit Titling Trust, 993 So. 2d 178, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 16968 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Oct. 31, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Dorian K. Damoorgian, Judge; L.T. Case No. 06-3446 (02).
Brookins v. Ford Credit Titling Trust, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 10278 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., July 9, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant accident victim sued appellee, the long-term lessor of a motor vehicle, in the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), for injuries sustained in an accident involving a leased vehicle. The trial court granted summary judgment to the lessor. The victim appealed.


OVERVIEW: The lessee, who rented a motor vehicle from the lessor, failed to maintain the liability insurance specified in the lease. The victim's contentions that the lessor did not have a special policy of insurance explicitly listing the vehicle involved in the accident with the victim and that the lessee was the driver of the vehicle were accepted. However, the lessor maintained a blanket policy of liability insurance covering its fleet of leased automobiles. On appeal, the court found that the Graves Amendment, 49 U.S.C.S. § 30106, did not preempt state laws imposing financial responsibility on commercial or business entities leasing motor vehicles when the entities failed to meet financial responsibility or liability insurance requirements imposed by state law. Furthermore, the lessor satisfied the requirements of Florida law to avoid the imposition of liability for the injuries caused in the accident because the lessor's insurance policy satisfied the requirements of Florida law pursuant to § 324.021(9)(b)(1), Fla. Stat. (2007).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment, and certified conflict with the contrary decision on the same point of law in other cases.

Ogborn v. Zingale


CASE NO. 1D07-1831


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


988 So. 2d 56; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 11079; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 1763



July 11, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 29, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. Thomas H. Bateman, III, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant subscribers brought a class action complaint against appellee director, alleging that the Communications Services Tax statute, § 202.12, Fla. Stat., was facially unconstitutional. The Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida) granted the director's motion to dismiss. The subscribers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The subscribers alleged that § 202.12, Fla. Stat. was facially unconstitutional under the Commerce Clause to the extent that it imposed a sales tax on satellite television service, an out-of-state service, in an amount greater than that imposed on cable television service, an in-state service. The director asserted that the subscribers' challenge was an as-applied challenge and that, as they failed to timely file suit within 180 days of receiving notice that their refund request had been denied, the action was time-barred pursuant to § 202.23, Fla. Stat. The subscribers acknowledged that dismissal was appropriate if their constitutional challenge were treated as an as-applied challenge because the suit would have been time-barred. Similarly, the director acknowledged that a refund request would have been unnecessary if the subscribers' constitutional challenge were treated as a facial challenge. The appellate court found that the subscribers alleged that the higher sales tax, on its face, was unconstitutional in every instance of satellite television service in Florida. Thus, contrary to the trial court's ruling, the subscribers' challenge was facial in nature.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

1476 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Brookins v. Ford Credit Titling Trust


No. 4D07-2010


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 10278; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 1728



July 9, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at Brookins v. Ford Credit Titling Trust, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 10881 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., July 16, 2008)
Released for Publication November 21, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Dorian K. Damoorgian, Judge; L.T. Case No. 06-3446 (02).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant accident victim sued appellee, the long-term lessor of a motor vehicle, in the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), for injuries in an accident involving a leased vehicle. The trial court granted summary judgment to the lessor. The victim appealed.


OVERVIEW: The lessee of a motor vehicle failed to maintain the liability insurance specified in the lease. The victim's contentions that the lessor did not have a special policy of insurance explicitly listing the leased vehicle and that the lessee was the driver were accepted. However, the lessor did maintain a blanket policy of liability insurance covering its fleet of leased automobiles. On appeal, the court found that (1) the lessor of a vehicle, according to the Florida common law, could be held vicariously liable under the dangerous instrumentality doctrine for the negligent operation of the vehicle by a lessee or a lessee's agent; (2) Florida's common law was augmented by the enactment of § 324.021, Fla. Stat.; and (3) the Graves Amendment, 49 U.S.C.S. § 30106, did not to preempt state laws imposing financial responsibility on commercial or business entities leasing motor vehicles when the entities failed to meet financial responsibility or liability insurance requirements imposed by state law. Accordingly, the trial court properly granted summary judgment to the lessor because the lessor's liability insurance satisfied the requirements of § 324.021(9)(b)(1), Fla. Stat. (2007).


OUTCOME: The summary judgment was affirmed. Conflict was certified with a contrary decision on the same point of law.

 

1477 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wooding


No. 3D01-1168


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT

1478 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Tribbitt v. State


Case No. 2D07-1524


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


984 So. 2d 624; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 8998; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 1584



June 18, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 14, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Polk County; J. Dale Durrance, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury and sentenced in the Circuit Court for Polk County (Florida) for attempted robbery with a deadly weapon, in violation of § 812.13(2)(a), Fla. Stat. (2005), armed robbery with a firearm, and fleeing or attempting to elude. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim testified that, during the attempted robbery, she saw something in defendant's hand, but could not make out what it was. Defendant pushed her against a counter, and she felt something hard on her left shoulder blade. The victim did not otherwise describe what was in defendant's hand. A woman, who worked with the victim, testified that when a man standing over the victim saw her, he ran out of the store. The woman did not observe a firearm or any other weapon. Other witnesses testified as to defendant's use of a firearm in a second crime committed soon after the attempted robbery. Defendant testified that he carried a stick taped to a glove during his encounter with the victim. He said that he used the item to just point, and denied having a firearm. On appeal, the court found that, although the evidence was insufficient to establish that defendant used a weapon, as defined by § 790.001(13), Fla. Stat. (2005), during his attempted robbery of the victim, the jury found and the record supported that defendant attempted to rob the victim. Thus, defendant was to be convicted and resentenced for the lesser offense of attempted robbery pursuant to § 924.34, Fla. Stat. (2005).


OUTCOME: The conviction for attempted robbery with a deadly weapon was reversed and remanded for entry of an amended judgment reflecting a conviction for attempted robbery and for resentencing. The remaining convictions and sentences were affirmed without discussion.

 

1479 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Orange County v. Expedia, Inc.


Case No. 5D07-2787


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


985 So. 2d 622; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 8479; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 1549



June 13, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 30, 2008.
Review denied by Expedia, Inc. v. Orange County, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 2442 (Fla., Dec. 22, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, Cynthia Z. Mackinnon, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a county and a county comptroller, sought review of a final order by the Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida) which dismissed with prejudice their amended complaint for declaratory relief that sought a judgment that the Tourist Development Tax (TDT) imposed on appellee internet travel companies was due on the difference between the wholesale price and the retail price they received for the rooms when they resold them.


OVERVIEW: The appeal revolved around whether a taxing agency could obtain a declaratory judgment when in doubt as to the meaning or application of a tax statute or ordinance without the need to first exhaust the full panoply of administrative remedies associated with tax collection lawsuits. The internet travel companies negotiated with hotels for a discounted or wholesale price, from which they purchased room nights and then re-sold them at a marked up rate. The county and comptroller alleged that under the TDT, the travel companies were "dealers" because they received the consideration paid by the hotel guests for the right to occupy the hotel accommodations and as such, were required to collect and remit the TDT on the total consideration paid for the room by the guest. The appellate court held that the complaint alleged a present and practical need for declaratory relief. The claim was not abstract and the county was not bringing the action to challenge the laws governing TDT. As to exhausting remedies, it was illogical to require the parties to submit to the cumbersome, expensive process associated with a tax collection action when such process may prove to be entirely unnecessary.


OUTCOME: The order dismissing the complaint was reversed. The matter was remanded.

 

1480 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Kia Motors Am. Corp. v. Butler


No. 3D05-1145


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


985 So. 2d 1133; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 8457; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 1529



June 11, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 18, 2008.
Review denied by Butler v. Kia Motors Am. Corp., 2008 Fla. LEXIS 2404 (Fla., Dec. 16, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal of a non-final order from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Peter R. Lopez, Judge. Lower Tribunal No. 03-25467.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee car buyer filed a class action suit against appellant auto manufacturer, alleging defects in a model of car, and asserting claims under a federal statute, the Florida Deceptive and Unfair Trade Practices Act, and for breach of warranties. The Miami-Dade County Circuit Court (Florida) certified a class consisting of all persons who bought or leased such a car in Florida in the four years before suit was filed. The manufacturer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The buyer alleged the model of car she bought had a design defect that caused premature wear of the brakes. The appellate court held that class certification was improper, as she failed to satisfy the commonality and superiority requirements of Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.220(b)(3). Proof of deficiencies in her car would not advance the cause of other class members, as (1) there had been design and component changes to the model during the years at issue, and (2) without individual inquiry, there was no way to determine whether the need for a particular repair was due to a defect or other factors. Class members whose cars were satisfactory could not be compensated, as she requested. Nor did common legal questions predominate. The claim under the Florida Deceptive and Unfair Trade Practices Act, §§ 501.201-.213, Fla. Stat. (2003), failed on the causation and actual damages elements. For the same reasons, the claims of breach of implied and express warranties and violation of the Magnuson Moss Warranty Improvement Act, 15 U.S.C.S. § 2301-2312, were flawed. As individual inquiry and many mini-trials would be needed to identify the class, the buyer did not establish the superiority requirement.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's order with the direction that the class be decertified.


 

1481 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Colgate-Palmolive Co. v. Fla. Dep't of Revenue


CASE NO. 1D07-1051


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 8101; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 1435



June 2, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 5, 2008.
Rehearing denied by, Corrected by Colgate - Palmolive Co. v. Fla. Dep't of Revenue, 988 So. 2d 1212, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 15295 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Aug. 20, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
An appeal from the Department of Revenue. Jim Zingale, Executive Director.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged taxes assessed by appellee Florida Department of Revenue, contending that § 220.13(1), Fla. Stat. (2004), by which Florida limited net operating loss carryovers to federal net losses under I.R.C. § 172, discriminated against foreign corporate dividends in violation of the foreign Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, and the Equal Protection Clause, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer's foreign subsidiaries generated most of its sales. As it used the federal deduction method, under § 220.13, Florida treated its carryover losses in a similar method as the U.S. system. The taxpayer asserted that, as losses created by domestic dividend deductions could always be carried over while the foreign tax credit, calculated through the payment of foreign dividends, could not be carried over, § 220.13(1) discriminated between domestic and foreign dividends. The appellate court disagreed. Florida's treatment of foreign dividends under § 220.13(1) was more generous than the U.S. government's, as it offered corporations (1) the subtraction of all foreign source dividends from its income calculation, and (2) the ability to offset taxes owed to Florida through to the use of the foreign tax credit. No disparate treatment of the dividends existed, as Florida did not include foreign source dividends in its income calculation, but offered a corporation the ability to carry over net operating losses resulting from the deduction of foreign taxes paid and the possible deduction of other significant foreign dividends based on those same excluded foreign source dividends.


OUTCOME: The Department's ruling was affirmed.

Denhart v. State


Case No. 5D07-13


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 7814; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 1422



May 30, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at, Rehearing denied by Denhart v. State, 987 So. 2d 1257, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 12136 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Aug. 15, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Marion County, Hale R. Stancil, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Circuit Court for Marion County (Florida) of promoting a sexual performance by a child, in violation of § 827.071, Fla. Stat. (2005). The trial court adjudicated defendant to be a sexual predator pursuant to § 775.21, Fla. Stat. (2007). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant engaged in sexual conduct with a seventeen-year-old female, was involved in photographing those activities, and distributed the photographs to others. On appeal, the court found that (1) a photograph showing defendant making contact with the child's breast was sufficient to establish a prima facie case under § 827.071(3), Fla. Stat.; (2) the trial court did not abuse its discretion by agreeing to issue a special jury instruction stating that defendant's ignorance of the victim's age, the victim's misrepresentation of her age, or defendant's bona fide belief of the victim's age, was not a defense to the crime charged; (3) defendant failed to sustain his burden of proving that the trial court abused its discretion in concluding that photographs of defendant's home were relevant to corroborate testimony concerning the fact that the crime took place inside defendant's home and to refute a claim that the photos of the victim were altered; and (4) pursuant to the provisions of the Florida Sexual Predators Act, § 775.21, Fla. Stat. (2007), a person who was convicted of violating one of the statute's enumerated offenses was to be designated as being a sexual predator.


OUTCOME: The judgment and sentence were affirmed.

 

1483 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Lamore v. State


CASE NO. 5D07-2271


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


983 So. 2d 665; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 7815; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 1419



May 30, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 18, 2008. As Corrected June 25, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Marion County, Brian Lambert, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Circuit Court for Marion County (Florida) of driving under the influence of alcohol (DUI), § 316.193(2)(b)(3) Fla. Stat. (2006), and driving while driver's license permanently revoked (DWLR), § 322.341, Fla. Stat. (2006). The trial court sentenced defendant. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that his convictions and sentences were to be reversed because: (1) both the DUI and the DWLR statutes violated the Due Process Clauses of both the United States and Florida Constitutions; (2) the evidence was legally insufficient to sustain a DWLR conviction; (3) the State of Florida presented speculative and unfairly prejudicial testimony through cross-examination of the defense witness; and (4) the State made an unfairly prejudicial and legally erroneous argument to the jury in closing. On appeal, the court found that because defendant's challenges to the application of the statutes to the facts were not raised below, they were not preserved. Similarly, his contention that the statutes violated substantive due process was not preserved for review. Moreover, his sufficiency of the evidence argument was not preserved for appellate review, as the defense made no motion for judgment of acquittal challenging the sufficiency of the evidence. His objection to the cross-examination was also not preserved for appeal. Finally, as no objection was raised below, the court examined the prosecutor's comments and found nothing approaching fundamental error.


OUTCOME: The convictions and sentences were affirmed.

 

1484 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Beckett v. Dep't of Fin. Servs.


CASE NO. 1D07-2831


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


982 So. 2d 94; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 8133; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 1343



May 12, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 28, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An appeal from an order of the Department of Financial Services.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to §§ 626.611 and 626.621(6), Fla. Stat. (2004), appellee Florida Department of Financial Services suspended appellant insurance agent's insurance license for 12 months. The agent appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Department alleged the agent sold ancillary insurance products to customers without their informed consent (known as "sliding"), which was grounds to suspend or revoke her license under §§ 626.611 and 626.621(6), Fla. Stat. Three customers testified they left the agent's office believing they had purchased only the insurance they requested and did not realize they had purchased additional, optional coverage. An administrative law judge (ALJ) ruled (1) the agent engaged in sliding, an unfair or deceptive practice under § 626.9541(1)(z)3, Fla. Stat. (2004); (2) the Department did not prove her lack of trustworthiness to engage in the insurance business under § 626.611(7), Fla. Stat.; and (3) it did not prove she had engaged in fraudulent practices under § 626.611(9). He recommended a 60-day suspension. The Department accepted the ALJ's first ruling, but reversed the second and third rulings. It concluded that as the agent engaged in intentional wrongdoing, she violated § 626.611(7) and (9). The appellate court held that sliding was not a per se demonstration of unfitness under § 626.611(7), and that the ALJ reasonably found the agent had not engaged in fraud under § 626.611(9).


OUTCOME: The Department's reversal of the ALJ's finding that the Department failed to prove violations of § 626.611(7) and (9) was reversed and the case was remanded to the Department for reconsideration of the appropriate penalty. The Department's ruling was otherwise affirmed.


 

1485 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. State


No. 4D07-3443


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


980 So. 2d 624; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 8089; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 1252



May 7, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 23, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Indian River County; Dan L. Vaughn, Judge; L.T. Case No. 312007CF000068A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to felony criminal mischief and was sentenced as a habitual felony offender by the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Indian River County, Florida. He appealed his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that Huss v. State precluded the use of a prior conviction for misdemeanor criminal mischief as an enhancement under § 806.13(1)(b)4, Fla. Stat. (1999), because § 806.13(1)(b)4 was not added to the statute until after he had committed that offense. The appellate court noted that a law that increased the penalty for an offense committed after the law was enacted, based on a conviction occurring prior to the law's enactment, was not an unconstitutional ex post facto law. Unlike the statute involved in Huss, § 806.13(1)(b)4 did not add an element to the qualifying offense. Section 806.13(1)(b)4 provided only that if a person had one or more previous convictions for criminal mischief under 806.13(1)(b), the offense under §§ 806.13(1) or 806.13(2) for which the person was charged would be reclassified as a felony of the third degree. Therefore, under § 806.13(1)(b)4, the instant post-amendment offense was permissively enhanced by the pre-amendment convictions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Carrin v. State


CASE NO. 1D03-2084


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


980 So. 2d 604; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 6938



May 5, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 21, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. Richard L. Hood, Judge.
Carrin v. State, 978 So. 2d 115, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 369 (Fla., 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury in the Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida) convicted defendant of aggravated assault on a law enforcement officer, the instant court reversed the same and remanded the case with directions to enter a judgment for culpable negligence. The case was then sent to the Supreme Court of Florida, which remanded the case to the instant court to consider whether § 924.34, Fla. Stat. (2001) violated defendant's right to a jury trial.


OVERVIEW: On a prior appeal, defendant claimed that he was entitled to a new trial on the charge of culpable negligence. The State conceded that the evidence was insufficient to support a conviction for aggravated assault on a law enforcement officer and that this conviction had to be reversed. However, the State argued that a new trial was not necessary and that the instant court should direct the trial court to enter a judgment and sentence for the lesser-included offense of culpable negligence pursuant to § 924.34, Fla. Stat. (2001). As a result, the instant court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded with directions to enter judgment for culpable negligence.


OUTCOME: A new trial was ordered.

LaMorte v. State


Case No. 2D06-4346


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


984 So. 2d 548; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 6188; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 1225



May 2, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 17, 2008.
Rehearing denied by LaMorte v. State, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 14709 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., July 1, 2008)
Review denied by Lamorte v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 2548 (Fla., Dec. 9, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Sarasota County; Andrew D. Owens, Jr., Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the Circuit Court for Sarasota County (Florida), defendant pleaded no contest to sexual battery by a person in custodial authority, attempted sexual activity with a child by a person in custodial authority, and lewd, lascivious, or indecent act upon or in the presence of a child under 16 years of age. He appealed from the denial of his motion to dismiss based on the statute of limitations of § 775.15(3)(b), Fla. Stat. (Supp. 1990-1991).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a high school teacher and a swim team coach. The offenses involved students, one of whom was also on the swim team. The court rejected defendant's argument that § 775.15(3)(b), which extended the statute of limitations for misconduct in office by a public employee, was unconstitutionally vague. First, the legislature's act of rewriting the statute in 1974 clearly indicated that it did not intend to restrict the extension only to public office holders. The legislature specifically included the word "employee" and referenced "employment." Next, the fact that the statute did not define "public officer or employee" or "misconduct in office" did not make it unconstitutionally vague. The term "public officer or employee" was clear on its face and needed no definition. The meaning of "misconduct in office" was also not ambiguous. "Misconduct in office" by teachers was defined by Fla. Admin. Code Ann. R. 6B-4.009(3) as a violation of the Code of Ethics and the Principles of Professional Conduct that was so serious as to impair the individual's effectiveness in the school system. It was not necessary to rely on case law for a definition of the term "misconduct in office."


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Gonzalez v. State


Case No. 2D06-1619


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


982 So. 2d 77; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 6136; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 1183



April 30, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 21, 2008.
Review denied by Gonzalez v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1678 (Fla., Sept. 10, 2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Gonzalez v. Fla., 2008 U.S. LEXIS 8602 (U.S., Dec. 1, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Polk County; Dennis P. Maloney, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Polk County Circuit Court (Florida) denied defendant's motion to empanel a 12-person jury to hear his case. He was convicted of second-degree murder and was sentenced to life imprisonment as a prison releasee reoffender pursuant to § 775.082(3)(a), -(9)(a)(1), Fla. Stat. (2005). He appealed his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Art. I, § 22, Fla. Const., required a jury of at least six in criminal cases. Section 913.10, Fla. Stat. (2006), required a jury of 12 in capital cases, but provided for juries of six in all other criminal cases. Defendant sought an evidentiary hearing on his motion to present testimony and documentary evidence supporting his argument that a jury of six was inferior in its functioning to a jury of 12. The appellate court held that since the U.S. Supreme Court had ruled that the six members provided for by Florida law did not violate a defendant's Sixth Amendment rights, no purpose would have been served by an evidentiary hearing. Neither Florida nor federal law provided any relief for defendant.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment and sentence.
