State v. Ngo Lanh Nguyen


Case Nos. 5D07-2163 and 5D07-2181


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


980 So. 2d 1189; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 5914; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 1160



April 25, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 14, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, Tim Shea, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged, in each of two separate cases, with the felony of practicing a health care profession without a license, § 456.065(2)(d)1, Fla. Stat. (2005), and the misdemeanor of holding oneself out as a massage therapist without a license, § 480.047(1)(a), Fla. Stat. (2005). The Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida) granted defendant's motion and dismissed the felony counts in each case. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victims alleged that, in addition to offering instructions in martial arts, defendant offered "energy sessions" which were, in reality, massage sessions. The victims further alleged that defendant acted improperly during these massage sessions. Defendant argued that the specific misdemeanor statute governing massage therapists, § 480.047(1)(a), Fla. Stat. (2005), controlled over the more general felony statute covering health care professionals, § 456.065(2)(d)1., Fla. Stat. (2005). The appellate court held that the trial court erred in dismissing the felony counts because § 456.065(2)(d), Fla. Stat. (2005) was unambiguous and expressly authorized the State to prosecute an individual under both ch. 456, Fla. Stat., and ch. 480, Fla. Stat. A statute which authorized prosecution of a particular criminal act as a felony was not rendered unconstitutional, as applied, even though that criminal act may also have constituted a misdemeanor.


OUTCOME: The trial court's dismissal orders were reversed and the cases were remanded for reinstatement of the felony counts on each information.

 

1490 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brocca


No. 3D02-2652


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


979 So. 2d 430; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 5891; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 1156



April 23, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 9, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Marc Schumacher, Judge. Lower Tribunal No. 00-16352.
State v. Brocca, 955 So. 2d 532, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 575 (Fla., 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with the sexual battery of a mentally disabled adult. The State sought to introduce the adult's statements to his mother. The trial court held the statements were inadmissible because § 90.803(24), Fla. Stat. (2001), was unconstitutional. The intermediate appellate court certified the question to the Florida Supreme Court, which quashed its decision and remanded the case for reconsideration in light of State v. Hosty.


OVERVIEW: In Hosty, the high court held that in determining whether to admit hearsay statements of a mentally disabled adult under § 90.803(24), the courts should consider, inter alia, the spontaneity of the statement, how it was elicited, the ability of the declarant to distinguish between reality and fantasy; the motive or lack thereof to fabricate the statement; the possibility of any improper influence on the declarant; and the mental state of the declarant when the abuse was reported. The intermediate appellate court held that the declarant's private conversation with his mother was nontestimonial within the meaning of Crawford. To admit the statements under § 90.803(24), the State had to establish a proper factual predicate, and the declarant had to either testify or be determined to be unavailable. The trial court had to make specific findings on the record indicating the basis for determining the reliability of the declarant's statements. The declarant's statements to the state attorney interviewer were testimonial and could not be admitted unless the declarant (1) testified at trial, or (2) was determined to be unavailable, and defendant had an opportunity for cross-examination.


OUTCOME: The intermediate appellate court reversed the trial court's order finding that § 90.803(24) was unconstitutional and remanded the case to the trial court to conduct appropriate inquiries as to the admissibility of declarants statements, including whether the declarant would testify at trial.

 

1491 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Fla. Hometown Democracy, Inc. PAC v. Browning


CASE NO. 1D07-6024


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


980 So. 2d 547; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 6286; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 1099



April 23, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 9, 2008.
Motion granted by Save Our Constitution, Inc. v. Fla. Hometown Democracy, Inc., 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1255 (Fla., July 3, 2008)
Affirmed by, Stay vacated by Browning v. Fla. Hometown Democracy, Inc., 13 So. 3d 57, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1006 (Fla., 2009)
Affirmed by Browning v. Fla. Hometown Democracy, 2010 Fla. LEXIS 217 (Fla., Feb. 18, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. Charles A. Francis, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a citizens group and another, sued appellees, the Florida Department of State and the Florida Secretary of State, seeking a judgment declaring that ch. 2007-30, § 25, Laws of Fla., and emergency implementing rules enacted by the Department, were unconstitutional. The Leon County Circuit Court (Florida) granted appellees summary judgment. Appellants sought review.


OVERVIEW: The appellants contended that the challenged statute and its implementing rules violated the citizen initiative provisions of art. XI, § 3, Fla. Const. The appellate court agreed. Statutes and administrative rules regulating the citizen initiative process were valid only when their sole goal was to ensure ballot integrity; the challenged statute and rules failed that test. The statute and implementing rules asserted regulatory authority over the citizen initiative process by interjecting the concept of petition signature revocation. Inter alia, they prescribed procedures through which an elector's signature on a citizen initiative petition form could be revoked, provided that an elector who revoked his signature on a petition form could not thereafter sign a new petition in support of the same initiative, and that signatures that were revoked would not be counted towards the requisite number of verified signatures need to submit a proposed constitutional amendment to the electorate. As the statute and rules burdened the initiative process with requirements that were not prescribed by the Florida Constitution, they were invalid.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed and the case was remanded with directions that judgment be entered for appellants.

 

1492 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


BDO Siedman, LLP v. Banco Espirito Santo Int'l, Ltd.


No. 3D07-2472 Consolidated: 3D07-2746


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


998 So. 2d 1; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 5507; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 1036



April 16, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 4, 2009.
Review denied by Banco Espirito Santo Int'l, Ltd. v. BDO Seidman, LLP, 996 So. 2d 211, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 2251 (Fla., 2008)
Motion denied by BDO Seidman, LLP v. Banco Espirito Santo Int'l, Ltd., 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 2858 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., Apr. 8, 2009)
Motion granted by, Motion denied by, Remanded by BDO Seidman, LLP v. Banco Espirito Santo Int'l. Ltd., 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 11242 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., Aug. 12, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeals from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Jose M. Rodriguez, Judge. Lower Tribunal No. 04-14009.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant judgment debtor filed a motion to quash a notice of taking deposition subpoena duces tecum in aid of execution filed by appellee judgment creditor, on grounds that the debtor had posted a bond to stay execution pursuant to § 45.045(1), Fla. Stat. (2007). The Miami-Dade County Circuit Court (Florida) denied the motion. The debtor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The debtor claimed the trial court erred in allowing the creditor to proceed with discovery in aid of execution after the debtor posted a bond to stay execution. The creditor argued the trial court did not err, because § 45.045 unconstitutionally infringed on the Florida Supreme Court's rule-making authority over procedural matters; Fla. R. App. P. 9.310(a)-(b)(1) already dealt with the procedures for issuing such bonds. The appellate court held that the trial court erred in not applying § 45.045(1), Fla. Stat., to preclude the discovery in aid of execution at issue. Fla. R. App. P. 9.310(a) authorized modifications to its terms as "provided by general law." That modification came by way of § 45.045(1), Fla. Stat. The $ 50 million bond cap provided in § 45.045(1) concerned substantive rights to property and to appeal and was not an impermissible intrusion on the procedural practices of the courts.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed and the case was remanded with instructions that the trial court grant the debtor's motion to quash.

 

1493 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Progressive Auto Pro Ins. Co. v. One Stop Med., Inc.


Nos. 4D06-2157, 4D06-2697, 4D06-2698, 4D06-2699, 4D06-2700, 4D06-2701, 4D06-2702, 4D06-2703, 4D06-2705, 4D06-2706, 4D06-2707, 4D06-2708


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


985 So. 2d 10; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 5522; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 1174



April 16, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 25, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Consolidated appeals from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Jay Spechler and Kathleen D. Ireland, Judges; L.T. Case Nos. 02-18567 COCE49, 02-21446 COCE49, 05-250-27 COCE49, 02-25139 COCE49, 02-18569 COCE49, 02-25136 COCE49, 02-21424 COCE49, 02-20979 COCE49, 02-25025 COCE49, 02-028COCE49, 03-4525 COCE49, 03-4533 COCE49.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In separate suits, appellee medical providers sued appellant insurers under § 627.736(5)(b)5, Fla. Stat. (2003), seeking a Consumer Price Index (CPI) increase in sums payable as personal injury protection (PIP) benefits on magnetic resonance imaging (MRI) scans they provided the insureds. The Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County, Florida, granted the providers summary judgment; the insurers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The first provider claimed that under § 627.736(5)(b)5, Fla. Stat. (2001), it was entitled to a CPI adjustment to the Medicare Part B fee schedule for an MRI it provided to an insurer in 2002 based on the 2001 CPI figures. The trial held that under the 2003 amendment to § 627.736(5)(b)5, the MRI inflation adjustment had to be made based on the 2001 CPI. The appellate court agreed. The second provider sought a judgment declaring that the CPI adjustments were annual and cumulative under § 627.736(5)(b)5, and compounded from August 1st, 2002, to the date the MRI scans commenced. The trial court held the 2003 amendment to § 627.736(5)(b)5 required applying cumulative and compounding inflation adjustments for 2001, 2002, and succeeding years, so that the fee schedule amount for the year in question reflected the combined prior year's increases from 2001 through August 1st of the year in which the MRI scan was performed. Again, the appellate court agreed. This construction did not result in an unconstitutional retroactive application of § 627.736(5)(b)5. Rather, it involved application of a statute that became effective October 1, 2003 to an MRI scan performed later in May 2005.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1494 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Graham v. State


CASE NO. 1D06-3190


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


982 So. 2d 43; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 5230; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 1001



April 10, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 3, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Graham v. State, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 8917 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., May 16, 2008)
Review denied by Graham v. State, 990 So. 2d 1058, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 2074 (Fla., 2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari granted by, Motion granted by Graham v. Florida, 129 S. Ct. 2157, 173 L. Ed. 2d 1155, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 3327 (U.S., 2009)
Reversed by, Remanded by Graham v. Fla., 2010 U.S. LEXIS 3881 (U.S., May 17, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An appeal from the Circuit Court for Duval County. Lance M. Day, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile pled guilty to armed burglary with assault or battery and attempted armed robbery, in return for the trial court's withholding adjudication and three years' probation, conditioned on his serving a year in a pre-trial detention facility. Later, the Duval County Circuit Court (Florida) found he had violated his probation and sentenced him to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant violated probation when he and his accomplices broke into a victim's home, he held the victim at gunpoint, and his accomplices robbed the home. He confessed to two or three similar robberies. He was 19 when sentenced. The appellate court held that imposing a life sentence on a juvenile had never, in state or federal courts, been considered per se unlawful. Thus, such a sentence had not become so unique as to be "unusual" under the Eighth Amendment. U.S. courts, not international courts, interpreted the Eighth Amendment. As the International Covenant on Civil and Political Rights was ratified subject to a declaration of non-execution, appellant had no judicially enforceable right directly arising out of a challenge to the treaty as it would be interpreted by its signatory nations. The life sentence was not grossly disproportionate as applied. After receiving probation--an extremely lenient sentence for a life felony--appellant committed at least two armed robberies and confessed to an additional three. The trial court properly balanced the unlikely possibility of his rehabilitation with the safety of society and did not abuse its discretion in imposing a life sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1495 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Sloban v. Fla. Bd. of Pharm.


CASE NO. 1D07-0346


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


982 So. 2d 26; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 4782; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 927



April 3, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 5, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Sloban v. Fla. Bd. of Pharm., 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 9391 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., May 19, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An appeal from the Department of Health. Rebecca R. Poston, R. Ph., Executive Director, Florida Board of Pharmacy.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former pharmacist filed a petition to compel appellee, the Florida Board of Pharmacy, to adopt a rule under § 120.54, Fla. Stat. (2006), allowing his reapplication for licensure The Board denied his petition, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Board permanently revoked appellant's pharmacy after his criminal convictions for federal offenses related to the practice of pharmacy. The Board denied his request to reapply because it had not adopted rules permitting a formerly licensed pharmacist to apply for relicensure. Appellant argued that § 456.072(6), Fla. Stat. (2006), which authorized the Board to adopt reapplication rules, had to be read to require the Board to do so. The appellate court held that as § 456.072(6) granted the Board unfettered discretion to decide whether formerly licensed pharmacists could reapply for licensure, it was an unconstitutional delegation of legislative authority, in violation of the separation of powers provision, art. II, § 3, Fla. Const. The unconstitutional portion was not severable from the remainder of § 456.072(6), Fla. Stat. The context in which "may" was used in § 456.072(6)--"the Board may establish by rule"--did not permit the court to construe it as "shall." Therefore, the constitutionality of § 456.072(6) could not be salvaged, and, consequently, the Board had no authority to enact rules providing for reapplication for pharmacy licenses.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the Board's order denying appellant's petition to initiate rulemaking.

 

1496 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Reaves v. State


CASE NO. 1D07-1205


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


979 So. 2d 1066; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 4673; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 901



March 31, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 16, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An appeal from the Circuit Court for Escambia County. Nickolas P. Geeker, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to racing on a highway (§ 316.19(2)(a), Fla. Stat. (2005)) and vehicular homicide (§ 782.071(1), Fla. Stat. (2005)). He appealed, contending the Escambia County Circuit Court (Florida) erred by denying his motion to withdraw his plea to vehicular homicide, and that § 316.19(2)(a), Fla. Stat., was vague and facially unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and another driver began to drag race at a high rate of speed. The other driver's car struck a median, spun, and hit two trees; his passenger died. Defendant argued he was entitled under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.170(f) to withdraw his guilty plea to vehicular homicide because the charge was not supported by the element of causation. He argued that as the passenger voluntarily participated in the race, she caused her own death; in the alternative, the other driver was the cause as he refused to slow down and merge as he approached the median. The appellate court disagreed. There was no evidence the passenger played an active role in the race, or even acquiesced in the other driver's decision to race. It was foreseeable that the other driver would accelerate and try to pass defendant, as they were engaged in a high speed race. As defendant intended to outdistance the other car and be the first to arrive at a given destination, this conduct, combined with the fact that he refused to let the other car pass, was clearly "racing" as defined by § 316.19, and was expressly prohibited by § 316.191(2)(a). Thus, § 316.191(2)(a) was facially valid, not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Mulligan v. City of Hollywood


No. 4D02-3626


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 3876; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 783



March 19, 2008, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:

NOT FINAL UNTIL DISPOSITION OF TIMELY FILED MOTION FOR REHEARING.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at, Vacated by, in part, Remanded by, On rehearing at Mulligan v. City of Hollywood, 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 570 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Jan. 28, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Thomas M. Lynch IV, Judge; L.T. Case No. 00-1887 CACE 11.
City of Hollywood v. Mulligan, 934 So. 2d 1238, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1476 (Fla., 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sued appellee city, alleging its impoundment ordinance, Hollywood, Fla., Ordinance § 101.46, was invalid on various grounds. The trial court upheld the ordinance. Appellant sought review; the instant court reversed, finding the ordinance was preempted by the Florida Contraband Forfeiture Act. The Florida Supreme Court reversed this ruling and remanded to the instant court to address appellant's other challenges to the ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Section 101.46 authorized the impoundment of vehicles used in the commission of certain misdemeanors. Appellant argued § 101.46 violated due process and the separation of powers. It relegated the issue of the propriety of an impoundment to a municipal agency without affording the aggrieved person a right to trial by jury in a court. The ordinance created a police court exercising judicial powers in violation of the Florida Constitution's separation of powers provision. It did not insure that a neutral magistrate presided over an impoundment case and it minimized the quantum of evidence necessary to sustain impoundment. It provided no criteria to apply to fix the amount of the "administrative fee" to impose for return of the impounded vehicle. The instant court held that so much of § 101.46 as provided for administrative hearings before city officials on whether there was probable cause to impound a vehicle and the amount of any fee to obtain a return of it was unconstitutional as violating the separation of powers, Art. II, § 3, Fla. Const., and due process.


OUTCOME: The instant court held that the challenged portions of the ordinance were unconstitutional.

 

1499 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Sutton v. Fla. Parole Comm'n


No. 4D07-3653


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


975 So. 2d 1256; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 3397; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 747



March 12, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 1, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Sutton v. Fla. Parole Comm., 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 5315 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Apr. 1, 2008)
Review denied by Fla. Parole Comm'n v. Sutton, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1896 (Fla., Sept. 17, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Krista Marx, Judge; L.T. Case No. 1991CF003456AO2.
Sutton v. State, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 16736 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Oct. 24, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant offender was given early release and committed to civil confinement pending a final Florida's Jimmy Ryce Act (JRA) determination. Appellee Florida Parole Commission (FPC) terminated his early release. The JRA action was dismissed, but he did not receive credit for time served while under JRA detention. The Palm Beach County Circuit Court (Florida) denied his Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(a) motion to correct an illegal sentence. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: After the offender had been confined in a JRA facility for more than four years, the State Attorney dismissed the JRA case and the FPC revoked his conditional release. The State moved the offender back to his prison without counting against his sentence the four-year long JRA hold. The offender never appealed the FPC's revocation or the Florida Department of Corrections' (DOC's) refusal to credit the JRA confinement. The appellate court held that under Rule 3.800(a), the motion court lacked jurisdiction to grant relief at this point. The failure of the DOC to credit unforfeited gain time did not make the sentence allowing credit for prison time illegal; the prisoner's remedy was not under Rule 3.800, as his sentence was legal when imposed. His remedy for the unlawful administration of his sentence, which he did not pursue, had been within the DOC, whose decision would have been subject to judicial review by appropriate writ. However, he was entitled to JRA credit, since there was no meaningful distinction between incarceration in jail and state-enforced confinement in a mental hospital. The appellate court presumed that the DOC and FPC would follow the law that it had announced.


OUTCOME: Any habeas corpus claim for immediate release being premature, the offender's appeal was affirmed.

Dep't of Highway Safety & Motor Vehicles v. Johnson


Case No. 5D06-2931


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


980 So. 2d 1118; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 3144; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 696



March 7, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 23, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Dep't of Highway Safety & Motor Vehicles v. Johnson, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 8944 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., May 6, 2008)
Review denied by Johnson v. Dep't of Highway Safety & Motor Vehicles, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1980 (Fla., Oct. 14, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, Reginald K. Whitehead, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Florida Department of Highway Safety and Motor Vehicles denied appellee applicant's request for license reinstatement, ruling that under § 322.271, Fla. Stat., his four convictions for driving under the influence (DUI) precluded reinstatement. He filed a declaratory judgment action. The Orange County Circuit Court (Florida) granted him summary judgment, ruling that amended § 322.271(4) was void ab initio. The Department appealed.


OVERVIEW: Former § 322.271, Fla. Stat. (1997), was amended by ch. 98, § 223, Laws of Fla., to delete a provision that allowed a person with four DUI convictions to apply for reinstatement of his or her driving privileges. The state high court held that ch. 98, § 223, was unconstitutional for violating the single subject rule, art. III, § 6, Fla. Const. The legislature then enacted ch. 03, § 25, Laws of Fla., to cure this defect. The trial court held that ch. 03, § 25, did not cure the single subject defect. Therefore, the version of § 322.271, Fla. Stat., in effect before enactment of ch. 98, § 223, Laws of Fla., applied, and the applicant was entitled to seek reinstatement. The appellate court disagreed. The single subject rule violation contained in ch. 98, § 223, was cured by the enactment of ch. 03, § 25, Laws of Fla. Accordingly, the amended version of § 322.271(4), Fla. Stat., became operative on the effective date of ch. 03, § 25, Laws of Fla., and the applicant had a window period, which closed on that date, to obtain reinstatement of his license from the Department.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

Sch. Bd. v. Academies of Excellence, Inc.


Case No. 5D06-1054


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


974 So. 2d 1186; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 5177; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 569



February 22, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 12, 2008.
Review dismissed by Sch. Bd. v. Academies of Excellence, Inc., 981 So. 2d 1200, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 656 (Fla., Apr. 7, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Administrative Appeal from the Department of Education.
Sch. Bd. v. Academies of Excellence, Inc., 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 18808 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Nov. 30, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to § 1002.33, Fla. Stat. (2005), appellee school filed a charter school application. Appellant district school board denied the application. The school appealed. The Florida Charter School Appeal Commission reversed the board's ruling. The board appealed; the Florida Department of Education affirmed. The board sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The board's witnesses testified that the school's application failed to set a goal of attaining an A, B, C, or D grade; that its standard that students who scored at or above the 25th percentile on norm referenced tests demonstrated acceptable performance was lower than the State's standard; and that the application lacked evidence of sound financial planning. The board denied the application on these grounds. The Commission ruled that the board had established that the application was deficient in the area of student assessment/accountability, but that this was not good cause for denial. The Department affirmed. The appellate court held that neither § 1002.33(6)(a), Fla. Stat., nor the Florida charter schools standard application required a charter school to include a school grade. The school had rebutted the board's claim that it was statutorily deficient in the finance/class size requirement. The Department's authority under § 1002.33(6)(c) to approve or deny a charter school application did not violate the authority of district school boards under Art. IX, § 1(a), Fla. Const., to control public schools, as only those boards were authorized to open and supervise charter schools.


OUTCOME: The decision of the Department was affirmed.

Steil v. State


No. 4D06-3296


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


974 So. 2d 589; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 2186; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 549



February 20, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 7, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Indian River County; Dan Vaughn, Judge; L.T. Case No. 05-435.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Indian River County (Florida) that convicted him of aggravated fleeing or eluding an officer under § 316.1935(3), Fla. Stat. (2005); defendant claimed that there was no proof that he was driving at high speed or in a manner demonstrating a wanton disregard for the safety of persons or property.


OVERVIEW: Three police officers in a restaurant went outside after hearing there was going to be a fight in the parking lot. One of the officers held out his hand and yelled "stop" to defendant, who made eye contact with the officer, but did not stop his vehicle as he was leaving the parking lot. Another officer followed defendant and observed him drive 15 to 20 miles an hour over the 35-mile an hour speed limit and run several stop signs. The appellate court found that because the pursuing officer testified that he did not have lights and sirens on while chasing defendant, there was insufficient evidence of high speed or wanton disregard to support the conviction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the matter was remanded to reduce defendant's conviction to simple fleeing or eluding.

Dep't of Revenue ex rel. Jackson v. Nesbitt


Nos. 4D06-4322, 4D06-4323 & 4D07-574


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


975 So. 2d 549; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 1383; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 432



February 6, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 25, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Dep't of Revenue v. Nesbitt, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 4505 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Mar. 25, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Consolidated appeals from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Jack Tuter & Carol-Lisa Phillips, Judges; L.T. Case Nos. 00-14170 4291 & 03-17471 3890.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a paternity and child support action, the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), granted appellee father's motion to determine child support arrearages, payment thereon, and to set aside writ and passport release. Thus, appellant, the Department of Revenue, who had filed the instant action on behalf of the two mothers involved, sought further review, and the cases were consolidated for appeal.


OVERVIEW: The Department of Revenue (DOR) argued that the trial court lacked the authority to lift federally mandated restrictions on the father's passport because the record reflected that his combined delinquency in the consolidated appeals was $ 37,313, which exceeded the $ 2,500 threshold established by federal law. The Court of Appeals agreed. Specifically, pursuant to § 409.2564(10), Fla. Stat. (2006), the DOR had the authority to certify to the Secretary of Health and Human Services that an individual had child support arrearages and might be eligible for passport restrictions. Second, Florida case law held that the trial court was prohibited from interfering with, and lacked the authority enter into, the decision-making process of a state agency. Further, the DOR had not deemed the arrangements created by the trial court to be acceptable.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

In re Doe 07-B


CASE NO. 1D07-4991


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


973 So. 2d 627; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 818; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 357



January 28, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 13, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. John E. Crusoe, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a Georgia juvenile, sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida) in which the circuit court ruled that it did not have jurisdiction to consider appellant's Parental Notice of Abortion Act, § 390.01114(4)(a), Fla. Stat. (2007), petition for judicial waiver of parental notification of the termination of a pregnancy.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court determined that it did not have jurisdiction because the minor did not reside within the jurisdiction of the court. Appellant argued that the circuit court erred as a matter of law in holding that it lacked jurisdiction to hear the petition. Appellant asserted that when a minor was a nonresident of the state, Florida law compelled a conclusion that she might file a petition for judicial waiver in any circuit court in the state. The appellate court agreed. Contrary to the circuit court's ruling, § 390.01114(4)(a) was a venue statute, not a jurisdictional statute. As the statute was silent on the venue in which an out-of-state party was to file a petition, no specific venue was preferred, and the circuit court's decision was error. However, based on the time limits set forth in the Act, a remand for a new hearing before the circuit court was not authorized. As a result, the appellate court, before issuing its written opinion, had directed that the circuit court immediately issue an order granting the petition.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the circuit court's dismissal of the petition and remanded with directions that the circuit court forthwith enter an order granting the petition and directing the clerk of the circuit court to place a certificate to that effect in the file and provide appellant with a certified copy of that certificate.

 

1508 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Malone v. State


No. 4D07-1113


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


973 So. 2d 1220; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 700; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 278



January 23, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 4, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Malone v. State, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 3658 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Mar. 4, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, St. Lucie County; James W. McCann, Judge; L.T. Case No. 562006CF001865A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the sentence she was given after she entered an open plea in the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, St. Lucie County (Florida), on one count of grand theft of property valued at more than $ 100,000 and one count of fraudulently obtaining property valued at more than $ 50,000.


OVERVIEW: Defendant stole money from her employer by misusing a corporate credit card. Although her prison sentence was authorized by the criminal punishment code, defendant argued that she was unconstitutionally being imprisoned because of her inability to pay restitution. A co-employee, who also stole from the employer, was given probation after making full restitution of the amount he had taken. The appellate court affirmed. Direct appeal of a sentence was limited by § 921.002(1)(h), Fla. Stat. Further, assuming that the holding in the case defendant relied on to support her direct appeal was correct, the appellate court agreed with the State's arguments that defendant's case was distinguishable. Unlike the co-defendants in the case defendant relied on, defendant and her co-employee were not co-defendants; their thefts were done individually. Further, defendant was charged with a higher degree of felony than the co-employee. Finally, the charges against the co-employee were not dropped upon the payment of restitution; he simply received a different sentence based upon his plea. The appellate court found no constitutional violation that would make defendant's sentence appealable.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence was affirmed.

 

1509 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


In re Petition of Doe


Case No. 2D07-5975


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


973 So. 2d 548; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 728; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 319



January 23, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 14, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County; Raul C. Palomino, Jr., Acting Circuit Judge.
In re Petition of Doe, 973 So. 2d 548, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 80 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., Jan. 4, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant minor appealed a judgment by the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County (Florida) that denied her motion for a rehearing en banc of her petition for a judicial waiver of the parental notice of the termination of her pregnancy.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court was evenly divided concerning the disposition of the motion. Therefore, pursuant to Fla. R. App. P. 9.331(a), the panel decision denying the motion stood, and the motion for rehearing en banc was denied. Thereafter, one of the judges withdrew his vote in favor of the motion, and voted to deny it.


OUTCOME: The motion was denied.

 

1510 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



City of Miami v. Wellman


No. 3D01-3050


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


976 So. 2d 22; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 744; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 296



January 23, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 27, 2008.
Rehearing denied by City of Miami v. Wellman, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 5456 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., Mar. 27, 2008)
Review denied by City of Miami v. Wellman, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1660 (Fla., Sept. 10, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeals from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Celeste H. Muir, Judge. Lower Tribunal Nos. 99-19523; 99-28417.
City of Miami v. Wellman, 944 So. 2d 251, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2592 (Fla., 2006)
City of Miami v. Wellman, 875 So. 2d 635, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 894 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city appealed, and appellee vehicle owner's cross-appealed, from an order of the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County (Florida), which granted the vehicle owners' motions for injunctive relief, rejecting many of the vehicle owners' arguments, but finding that Miami-Dade County, Fla., Code §§ 42-120-124 (1997) was unconstitutional as applied.


OVERVIEW: The court found that the city's vehicle impoundment ordinance was unconstitutional for three reasons: (1) it failed to provide adequate notice; (2) it applied an incorrect standard of proof; and (3) it failed to satisfy due process requirements by not providing an innocent owner defense. The ordinances did not clearly require that notice be promptly given to owners who were not at the scene of the impoundment. Additionally, the ordinance did not require any notice to lessors, renters, and lienors. Also, the ordinance was constitutionally infirm because it called for a preponderance of the evidence standard of proof. Deprivation of property and the assessment of fines called for the higher standard. Impoundment was analogous to a forfeiture, which required the government to prove, by no less than clear and convincing evidence, that the property being forfeited was used in the commission of a crime. Finally, although mindful that impoundment was not equivalent to forfeiture, the court did not believe that an ordinance that did not allow for an innocent owner to be immune from loss of property and additional monetary penalties could satisfy due process.


OUTCOME: The order granting injunctive relief was affirmed.


 

1511 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Lykes v. State


Case No. 5D07-2079


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


972 So. 2d 292; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 506; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 265



January 18, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 6, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, Marc L. Lubet, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed after being convicted in the Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida) of fleeing to elude a law enforcement officer at a high speed or with wanton disregard for the safety of persons or property in violation of § 316.1935(3)(a), Fla. Stat. (2006).


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the jury instruction was fundamentally flawed as it might have deprived him of a unanimous jury verdict. Among other things, the jury instruction required the State to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that during the course of the fleeing or attempting to flee, defendant drove at a high speed or in any manner demonstrating a wanton disregard for the safety of persons or property. Defendant contended if some of the jurors concluded that he fled at a high speed, while others believed that he endangered persons or property while fleeing, he was deprived of a unanimous verdict. The appellate court disagreed. There were two ways to prove defendant guilty under § 316.1935(3)(a). Defendant was found guilty under a general verdict. While the general verdict could have rested on a theory of liability without adequate evidentiary support, reversal was not warranted because there was an alternative theory of guilt for which the evidence was sufficient.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Abrams v. State


Nos. 4D06-2326, 4D06-2327 and 4D06-2328


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


971 So. 2d 1033; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 471; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 228



January 16, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 1, 2008.
Review denied by Abrams v. State, 984 So. 2d 1250, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1023 (Fla., 2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Abrams v. Fla., 2008 U.S. LEXIS 7461 (U.S., Oct. 14, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Consolidated appeals from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Jeffrey Levenson and Paul L. Backman, Judges; L.T. Case Nos. 94-7430 CF10A, 94-5492 CF10A and 05-12519 CF10A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), of committing lewd or lascivious battery under § 800.04(4)(a), Fla. Stat. (2004) and lewd or lascivious conduct under § 800.04(6), Fla. Stat. (2004). The court sentenced defendant, in accordance with the Florida Dangerous Sexual Felony Offender Act, § 794.0115, Fla. Stat. (2004), to two concurrent life terms. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the Florida Dangerous Sexual Felony Offender (DSFO) Act was unconstitutional on its face because it provided no statutory notice, no separate hearing, and no standard of proof. On appeal, the court found that, as the DSFO Act was passed prior to defendant's commission of his second offenses, he was on notice of the increased penalty attached to his criminal conduct. He also had notice and an opportunity to be heard on his sentence as the sentencing hearing provided for in Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.720 satisfied defendant's due process opportunity to be heard on his DSFO sentence. Moreover, Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.713 required the disclosure of prior convictions to defendant in advance of the sentencing hearing. Although the DSFO Act did not provide a standard of proof, there was no impediment to its constitutionality for this omission. Finally, there was clearly competent substantial evidence to support the sentencing. However, defendant's conviction for lewd or lascivious conduct under § 800.04(6), Fla. Stat., did not qualify him for sentencing pursuant to the DSFO Act.


OUTCOME: The sentence for the lewd or lascivious conduct count was reversed, and the case was remanded for resentencing. The conviction and sentence on the lewd or lascivious battery count was affirmed.

C.B. v. Dep't of Children & Family Servs. (In the Interest of J.B.)


Case Nos. 2D06-4205, 2D06-5532 CONSOLIDATED


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


990 So. 2d 520; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 71; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 159



January 4, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 1, 2008.
Rehearing denied by C.B. v. State Dep't of Children & Family Servs., 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 17381 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., Mar. 14, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County; Jack Espinosa, Jr., Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee agency filed a petition for the involuntary termination of appellant mother's parental rights. The mother did not appear at the adjudicatory hearing. The Circuit Court for Hillsborough County (Florida) ordered entry of a consent by nonappearance on the mother's behalf and rendered a judgment terminating her parental rights as to her child. The mother moved to set aside the judgment, which the trial court denied. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother claimed that she did not attend the adjudicatory hearing due to the financial hardships she faced in traveling from New Hampshire, in addition to demands of her job, new child, and ill father in New Hampshire. The appellate court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in terminating the mother's parental rights as to her child, pursuant to § 39.801(3)(d), Fla. Stat. (2005), or refusing to set aside the consent. The trial court found that the mother's testimony lacked credibility based on its inconsistencies and contradictions. It concluded that the mother did not make a reasonable effort to be present at the hearing because she did not attempt to contact her attorney or the trial court to explain her circumstances or otherwise attempt to arrange for transportation and alternative care for her father. The findings were supported by the mother's own testimony at the hearing regarding her lack of preparation and her testimony that she actually forgot about the important court date. The trial judge made credibility determinations based upon his observations of the mother's demeanor and his assessment of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Gallo v. Celebration Pointe Townhomes, Inc.


No. 4D07-496


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


972 So. 2d 992; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 37; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 127



January 2, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 21, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Gallo v. Celebration Point, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 2745 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Feb. 21, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Barry E. Goldstein, Judge; L.T. Case No. 06-7044 CACE11.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mobile home owner filed suit against appellee mobile home park owner in the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), for a declaratory judgment that the mobile home park owner did not act in good faith in accordance with § 723.021, Fla. Stat. (2005). The circuit court dismissed the complaint. The mobile home owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mobile home park owner sent notices of eviction to all of the mobile home park residents. The mobile home park owner sought rezoning of the mobile home park property to construct townhomes, but the rezoning was not commenced prior to the sending of the notices of eviction. The mobile home owner claimed that the mobile home park owner did not act in good faith in accordance with § 723.021, Fla. Stat., because the eviction notice required the mobile home owner to abandon her mobile home prior to the rezoning and a finding by a governmental body that other suitable facilities existed for the mobile home owners, which she alleged was required by § 723.083, Fla. Stat. (2005). On appeal, the court found that, because the Florida Legislature, pursuant to § 723.061(3), Fla. Stat. (2005), expressly rendered § 723.083, Fla. Stat., inapplicable to change of use evictions, the trial court correctly determined that the statutory obligation which the mobile home owner asserted that the mobile home park owner violated did not exist. The mobile home park owner had no obligation under § 723.083, Fla. Stat., to await the results of the rezoning decision before sending its notice of eviction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Kodsy v. Dep't of Fin. Servs.


No. 4D07-54


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


972 So. 2d 999; 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 42; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 128



January 2, 2008, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Department of Financial Services of the State of Florida; L.T. Case No. 87200-06-AG.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant contractor petitioned for review of an immediate final order by appellee, the Department of Financial Services of the State of Florida, which, pursuant to § 120.569(2)(n), Fla. Stat. (2006), ordered the contractor to cease and desist from analyzing insurance policies or counseling or advising or giving opinions as to insurance policies or otherwise acting as a general lines insurance agent without being properly licensed and appointed.


OVERVIEW: The contractor was a Florida licensed building contractor who operated a mold remediation company. He was not and never was a Florida licensed insurance agent. The immediate final order (IFO) found that the contractor was engaging in the unlicensed and illegal business of analyzing homeowner's insurance policies and counseling, advising, and giving opinions relative to homeowner's insurance. According to the IFO, the contractor analyzed four homeowners' insurance policies and advised the homeowners that his services were covered under their policies. As a result of that assurance, the homeowners hired the contractor. However, the insurance companies would not pay the contractor. When the homeowners did not pay their bills, the contractor filed a claim of lien against their properties. On appeal, the court found that the Department issued a facially deficient IFO which failed to demonstrate that the complained of behavior would continue, and that an emergency order without a hearing was necessary.

Brumit v. State


No. 4D06-4999


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


971 So. 2d 205; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 20690; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 168



December 31, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 18, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Petition for writ of habeas corpus to the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Paul L. Backman and Ana I. Gardiner, Judges; L.T. Case No. 00-12574 CF10A.
Brumit v. State, 843 So. 2d 978, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 6183 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the denial of her writ of habeas corpus by the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida). After the appellate court had determined that a co-defendant could not be tried for a lesser-included offense of child abuse where the conviction was based on an all or nothing verdict for aggravated child abuse, defendant sought collateral relief in her own case.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged, along with co-defendant with one count of aggravated child abuse in violation of § 827.03(2)(b), Fla. Stat. Neither side asked to have the jury instructed on any lesser included offenses and the jury was instructed to find them either guilty of aggravated child abuse as charged, or not guilty. Both were found guilty as charged. Upon appeal, the appellate court directed the trial court on remand to enter judgment against defendant for child abuse under § 827.03(1), which the trial court did. No direct appeal was taken from the new conviction and sentence. The appellate court determined, in regard to co-defendant's appeal, that because the jury was not instructed on the lesser included offense of simple child abuse at the original trial, retrying him for simple child abuse would violate his right to be protected from double jeopardy. The appellate court held the previous jury determination that defendant was guilty of aggravated child abuse, i.e., that she maliciously punished the child, could not be deemed to include a jury finding that she was guilty of every element of the permissive lesser included offense of child abuse.


OUTCOME: The petition was granted. The trial court was directed to vacate defendant's conviction.

Siplin v. State


CASE NO. 5D06-4071


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


972 So. 2d 982; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 20549; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 82



December 28, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 18, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Siplin v. State, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 2772 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Jan. 31, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, Julie H. O'Kane, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial in the Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida), defendant, a state senator, was convicted of grand theft under § 812.014(2)(c)(2), Fla. Stat. and of using the services of a state employee during working hours in furtherance of a political campaign under § 106.15(3), Fla. Stat. (2004). He appealed.


OVERVIEW: With regard to the theft charge, the State alleged that the State had paid one of its employees to work for three months as a legislative aide when she was in fact working for defendant's re-election campaign. No witness testified that defendant knew that the aide was continuing to receive her state salary. The court held that the circumstantial evidence was insufficient to prove that defendant knew that the aide was receiving a state paycheck. Even if defendant had been negligent in allowing the aide to handle her own payroll submissions, a criminal conviction for theft could not stand based upon negligence in handling office procedures. Next, although § 106.15 would be overbroad under the First Amendment and in violation of substantive due process under the Fourteenth Amendment and Art. I, § 9, Fla. Const. if it could be read not to include a guilty knowledge or mens rea requirement, criminal statutes were generally read to include such a requirement. The jury, however, had not been instructed on mens rea as requested. This error was not harmless, as a key witness's testimony was contradicted by other evidence as well as by testimony that the witness was biased against defendant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed both convictions and remanded with directions that defendant be acquitted on the felony charge. On remand, the State could retry defendant on the charge under § 106.15(3), Fla. Stat.

Miller v. State


Case No. 5D07-10


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


971 So. 2d 951; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 20543; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 79



December 28, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 16, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, Alicia Latimore, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the denial by the Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida) of his motion to dismiss an information charging him with failure to report at a driver's license office in violation of § 943.0435(9) and (3), Fla. Stat. (2006). Defendant argued that the statute violated his right to equal protection by requiring him to register as a result of an offense he committed in West Virginia, while exempting Florida sex offenders.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of a sex crime in West Virginia and was required to register as a sex offender there. Following a move to Florida, he was advised by law enforcement of his registration obligation. After several months passed he was charged with failing to report as a sex offender in violation of § 943.0435(9) and (3). After the denial of his motion to dismiss, he pled no contest to the charge. The appellate court held the statute did not treat him differently from similarly-situated persons. § 943.0435(1)(a)1. and 2., Fla. Stat. did not treat in-state and out-of-state sexual offenders differently. As he was required to register in West Virginia, he was subject to § 943.0435(1)(a)2. when he remained in Florida for more than five days. He was treated the same as other similarly-situated sex offenders, moving into Florida or already living in Florida, who were required to register in other states. Thus, he did not show that § 943.0435 treated him differently from any other similarly-situated sexual offender, or that it intentionally discriminated against him. § 943.0435, Fla. Stat. did not offend equal protection.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Langello v. State


Case No. 2D06-2419


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


970 So. 2d 491; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 20094; 33 Fla. L. Weekly D 3

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Pinellas County; Nancy Moate Ley, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Pinellas County (Florida) convicted defendant, on his plea of nolo contendere, of carrying a concealed firearm and possession of marijuana, but defendant reserved his right to appeal the denial of his motion to suppress the evidence found in his car as a result of a traffic stop for a broken tag light. Thus, defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that § 316.221(2), Fla. Stat. (2004) required only a single operational light on a vehicle and that the officer erroneously focused on whether both tag lights were functioning instead of on whether the tag was clearly legible. (2004), as it failed to show that defendant's car was not equipped as required by law, and it made no attempt to establish that the car was unsafe.


OUTCOME: The order denying suppression was reversed, and the case was remanded with directions to the circuit court to discharge defendant.

Bechina v. Enter. Leasing Co.


No. 3D07-1225


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


972 So. 2d 925; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 19704; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 2935



December 12, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 20, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Jon I. Gordon, Judge. Lower Tribunal No. 05-25024.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a personal injury action alleging vicarious liability, the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County (Florida) granted final summary judgment to appellee car rental agency (agency) on their defense of the federal Graves Amendment, 49 U.S.C.S. § 30106, as a complete bar to the claim asserted. Thus, appellants, the alleged injured parties, sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The alleged injured parties first asserted that the trial court misinterpreted a provision of the Graves Amendment that limited the preemptive reach of the statute and preserved certain vicarious liability provisions under preexisting Florida statutory and common law. Second, they claimed that the Graves Amendment was unconstitutional. But, the appeals court disagreed with both claims, as the instant court previously upheld the preemptive language of the Graves Amendment, as applied to § 324.021(9)(b)(2), Fla. Stat. (2005). As a result, the Graves Amendment abrogated the agency's vicarious liability in this case. Second, the instant court declined to follow other reported cases that concluded that the Graves Amendment was outside of the Congressional powers created by the Commerce Clause of the United States Constitution and, therefore, unconstitutional, opting instead to hold that motor vehicle leasing transactions unquestionably affected the channels of interstate commerce, the instrumentalities of interstate commerce, and intrastate activities substantially related to interstate commerce. Thus, the court could not strike a Congressional enactment for local interests.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Taylor v. State


No. 4D06-4478


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


969 So. 2d 583; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 19206; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 2874



December 5, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 21, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; William Berger, Judge; L.T. Case No. 06-1486 CFA02.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), convicted defendant of selling cocaine within 1,000 feet of a place of worship. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying him the first and rebuttal closing arguments during his October 19, 2006, trial. He asserted that § 918.19, Fla. Stat. violated the separation of powers provided in Art. II, § 3, Fla. Const. The appellate court found that, although the legislature's repeal of the portion of Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.250 relating to first and last closing arguments was effective, having been passed by a two-thirds majority of each house, its attempt to substitute a different procedure was not. The trial occurred after adoption of the statute, but before the promulgation by the Supreme Court of Florida of Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.381, which amended Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.250. Thus, the case involved a repealed Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.250, without a replacement rule. In such a situation, the common law applied. No intolerable hiatus resulted because the common law supplied the order of closing arguments. Further, the later adoption of the amended rule undermined the position that a "hiatus" was created, as both the amended rule and the common law conformed precisely to § 918.19, Fla. Stat. The trial court properly decided the order of final arguments.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

Sch. Bd. v. Academies of Excellence, Inc.


Case No. 5D06-1054


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


2 So. 3d 280; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 18808; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 2846



November 30, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, Rehearing, en banc, denied by, Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at Sch. Bd. v. Academies of Excellence, Inc., 974 So. 2d 1186, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 5177 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Feb. 22, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Administrative Appeal from the Department of Education.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee academy filed an application with appellant school board for permission to open a charter elementary school. The school board denied the application. The Charter School Appeals Commission reversed the denial of the application. The school board appealed. The State of Florida, Department of Education (State Board), issued a written order upholding the findings and recommendations of the Commission. The school board appealed.


OVERVIEW: The school board claimed that the State Board deviated from the record and improperly created its own record, that the State Board failed to include a fact-based justification for its decision, that the application was unsound in student assessment/accountability and finance/class size requirements, and that the Florida Constitution was violated. On appeal, the court found that (1) the school board failed to preserve the record issues; (2) the failure of the State Board to include a fact-based justification for its decision was not reversible error under § 1002.33 Fla. Stat. (2005); (3) competent substantial evidence supported the Commission's conclusion that the school board did not have good cause to deny the application pursuant to § 1002.33(6)(a) (2005); (4) the Commission had sufficient evidence to properly conclude that, although the application was statutorily deficient, such a deficiency was not good cause for denial of the application when the academy recognized the problem and was willing to correct it; and (5) § 1002.33, Fla. Stat. did not violate the provisions of Art. IX, § 1(a), Fla. Const.; Art. IX, § 4(b), Fla. Const.; and Art. IX, § 2, Fla. Const.


OUTCOME: The final order of the State Board to grant the application was affirmed.

Singleton v. Eli B. Inv. Corp.


No. 4D06-3582


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


968 So. 2d 702; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 18740; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 2833



November 28, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 14, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Robert L. Andrews, Judge; L.T. Case No. 05-18783 CACE 09.
Singleton v. Eli B. Inv. Corp., 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 14283 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Sept. 12, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee purchaser filed a complaint in the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), to quiet title pursuant to a tax deed. Appellant property owners filed an answer, affirmative defenses, and a counterclaim to vacate and set aside the tax deed sale. The trial court granted purchaser's motion for summary final judgment quieting title. The owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owners, whose property was sold because of unpaid ad valorem taxes, acknowledged that their home address was listed correctly in the county's records, but asserted (1) that they were not notified by certified mail, return receipt requested, or by regular mail; (2) that the clerk of court had actual knowledge that they were not notified because the notices, sealed and unopened, were still in the tax deed file; and (3) that the sheriff failed to notify them by posting a copy of the notice in a conspicuous place at their home or otherwise failed to notify them of the tax deed sale. They further asserted that § 197.522, Fla. Stat., which governed notice to an owner when application for tax deed was made, was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court found that the notice of the impending tax deed sale was inadequate and that it failed to comport with constitutional due process requirements.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order of summary final judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded for further evidentiary proceedings.

 

1527 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Richardson v. State


CASE NO. 1D06-6382


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


969 So. 2d 535; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 18684; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 2799



November 26, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 12, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An appeal from the Circuit Court for Alachua County. David A. Glant, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted twice for possession of cocaine and twice for sale of cocaine within 1,000 feet of a place of worship by the Circuit Court for Alachua County (Florida). Defendant contended his right not to be convicted more than once for the same offense was twice violated.


OVERVIEW: An informant gave defendant $ 100 in exchange for about five or six rocks of crack cocaine. An undercover deputy sheriff then came over and purchased additional cocaine. The sale to the informant took about 10 seconds. The second transaction occurred approximately 15 seconds later. The appellate court held that although defendant sold cocaine to two different individuals, both the confidential informant and the undercover agent were acting in concert and as agents of the same buyer. While defendant's two convictions for sale of cocaine in violation of § 893.13(1)(e), Fla. Stat. (2004) indisputably contained identical legal elements, the two convictions arose from two factually separate and distinct sales of cocaine, sales which could be punished separately without violating double jeopardy prohibitions. Defendant had time to pause, reflect, and intentionally commit an additional crime after his sale to the informant was fait accompli. Having completed one sale, he agreed to sell a separate quantity to the deputy sheriff for a separate, additional sum of money. The two physically distinct sales constituted separate criminal acts that could be separately punished.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentences and one of his convictions for possession of cocaine were reversed and remanded for resentencing. The remaining conviction for possession of cocaine and both convictions for sale of cocaine were affirmed.

Fernandez v. Dep't of Revenue


No. 3D07-779


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


971 So. 2d 875; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 18550; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 2763



November 21, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 7, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the State of Florida, Department of Revenue. Lower Tribunal No. 130600002387, CSE No. 1188793942.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant "putative father" sought review of a final administrative child support order entered against him by the Florida Department of Revenue, Child Support Enforcement Program (DOR). The putative father argued, inter alia, that the administrative judge who heard the child support matter lost jurisdiction when the putative father filed an answer disputing paternity and requested DNA testing to determine whether he was the child's father.


OVERVIEW: The DOR commenced an administrative proceeding against the putative father alleging that his paternity had been legally established by affidavit or voluntary acknowledgment as to a minor child. The putative father filed an answer denying the allegations which included an unsworn response requesting DNA tests. The answer did not request a hearing. The putative father did not respond to a proposed support order, and a final administrative child support order was entered. The putative father was designated as the father of the child on the child's Florida birth certificate. At the time he answered the administrative notice, Florida's separate statute on disestablishment of paternity, § 742.18, Fla. Stat., was not yet effective. Both § 742.18 and § 742.10(4), Fla. Stat. (2007), provided that a father who acknowledged paternity remained responsible for child support until he established good cause or prevailed in his own action in circuit court to disestablish paternity and terminate the payment obligations. Neither of those circumstances occurred. The paternity statutes afforded him a remedy to disestablish paternity and terminate his child support obligations.


OUTCOME: The order of the DOR was affirmed but without prejudice to the putative father's right to commence an action to disestablish paternity.

Smith v. State


No. 4D05-4622


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


968 So. 2d 108; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 18573; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 2779



November 21, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 7, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Charles M. Greene, Judge; L.T. Case No. 04-5303CF10A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged in the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), with lewd or lascivious molestation in violation of § 800.04(5)(a), Fla. Stat., and lewd or lascivious conduct in violation of §§ 800.04(6)(a) and 800.04(6)(b), Fla. Stat. (2004). Following his conviction, defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant went to a police station for questioning. He acknowledged receiving Miranda warnings. His mother was present during the interview. The interview was digitally recorded and entered into evidence at trial. Additionally, the trial was set over a year after a public defender was appointed. The case was continued or reset three times before substitute counsel filed an appearance and two times afterwards. The trial judge scheduled jury selection on 24-hours notice, four days before a Monday trial date that was set six weeks before. Defendant alleged due process violations under Fla. Const. art. I, § 9. On appeal, the court found that the trial court gave defense counsel sufficient notice before requiring him to begin his part of the voir dire. After two continuances and three months on the case, counsel had sufficient time to have prepared for jury selection. Further, there was no due process violation in the trial judge simply overruling defense counsel's objection and failing to hold a voluntariness hearing outside the jury's presence prior to admission of the DVD as counsel merely made a perfunctory objection as to voluntariness before the DVD was admitted into evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Browning v. Sarasota Alliance for Fair Elections, Inc.


Case No. 2D06-4339


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


968 So. 2d 637; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 17235; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 2573



October 31, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Sarasota Alliance for Fair Elections, Inc. v. Browning, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 2263 (Fla., Nov. 29, 2007)
Approved by, in part, Quashed by, in part Sarasota Alliance for Fair Elections, Inc. v. Browning, 2010 Fla. LEXIS 218 (Fla., Feb. 11, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Sarasota County; Robert B. Bennett, Jr., Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Sarasota County Circuit Court (Florida) entered a final judgment in a declaratory action, which upheld the constitutionality of an amendment to the Sarasota County charter that had been sponsored by appellee political action committee and set forth detailed election requirements to be implemented in a specific county in the future. Appellant government representatives appealed.


OVERVIEW: The political action committee sponsored an amendment to the Sarasota County charter that detailed election requirements to be implemented in the county in the future. The government representatives filed a complaint seeking a declaration of the constitutionality of the proposed amendment because they believed that the amendment was preempted by state law or conflicted with state law. The trial court ordered that the amendment be placed on the ballot for an upcoming general election. The electorate then approved the proposed amendment, which would become effective over a year thereafter. The trial court entered a final judgment in the declaratory action which upheld the constitutionality to the proposed amendment. On appeal, the appellate court found that the Florida Election Code, § 97.011 et seq., Fla. Stat. (Election Code) was so pervasive that the proposed amendment was impliedly preempted because the Election Code almost completely occupied the election law field in Florida that there was not room for conflicting county law on the subject. It also found that public policy reasons, such as uniformity, dictated that the proposed amendment be found unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed and the case was remanded to the trial court with directions to vacate the trial court's final judgment. Also, the appellate court certified the question to the state supreme court, as a matter of great public importance, whether the state's election law was sufficiently pervasive and whether public policy sufficiently strong, to preclude local laws regarding certain, specified voting matters.

K.C. Cromwell, Inc. v. Pollard


Case No. 2D06-1010


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT

October 12, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 13, 2008.
Reversed by, Remanded by Pollard v. K.C. Cromwell, Inc., 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1415 (Fla., Sept. 3, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Manatee County; Marc B. Gilner, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Manatee County (Florida) entered a final judgment in the amount of $ 160,000 in favor of appellee day laborer, and against appellant temp agency, finding that the agency violated § 448.24(1)(b), Fla. Stat. (2000-2003). The agency thus appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that the Manatee County Area Transit System rate of $ 1 for each one-way trip was the prevailing rate for public transportation in the Manatee County geographic area. Thus, it concluded that in order to comply with § 448.24(1)(b), Fla. Stat. (2000-2003), $ 1 was the maximum amount the agency could have deducted from the day laborer's pay, and found that the agency violated the statute on 160 occasions. Hence, in accordance with § 448.25, Fla. Stat., the trial court awarded the day laborer damages in the amount of $ 1,000 for each violation. On appeal from that order, the agency asserted that the final judgment should be reversed because the version of § 448.24(1)(b), Fla. Stat. in effect from 2000 through 2003 was unconstitutionally vague. The appeals court agreed, based on a prior decision rendered by the Fourth District Court of Appeal on markedly similar facts.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

Crapo v. HCA, Inc.


CASE NO. 1D06-5640


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


968 So. 2d 54; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 15954; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 2413



October 10, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 6, 2007.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An appeal from the circuit court for Alachua County. Toby S. Monaco, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a county property appraiser, sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Alachua County (Florida), which dismissed with prejudice his complaint under § 195.027(3), Fla. Stat. (2006) and Fla. Admin. Code Ann. R. 12D-1.005 for a subpoena duces tecum to compel appellee property owner to produce financial records relating to the owner's tangible personal property in the county.


OVERVIEW: The appraiser alleged that the owner declined a written request to produce documents which were necessary for an accurate determination by the appraiser of the owner's property as of a particular date. Accordingly, he sought issuance of a writ of subpoena duces tecum in order to compel the owner's production of the requested financial records. The trial court granted the owner's motion to dismiss the complaint, finding that the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction under either § 195.027(3), Fla. Stat. (2006) or Fla. Admin. Stat. (2006). The complaint sufficiently stated a cause of action. The owner's claim that the records were not necessary for an accurate value determination was not properly raised in a dismissal motion, which was determined based on the allegations in the complaint.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

Tampa Serv. Co. v. Hartigan


No. 4D05-4822


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


966 So. 2d 465; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 15921; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 2422



October 10, 2007, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal of a non-final order from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; J. Leonard Fleet, Judge; L.T. Case No. CACE 04-09206 (08).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant labor pool company sought review of a non-final order from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), which granted class certification pursuant to Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.220(b)(2) and (3) to appellee worker in his action, alleging that the company violated § 338.24(1)(b), Fla. Stat. (2003) of Florida's Labor Pool Act.


OVERVIEW: The worker filed suit against the company, alleging that it violated § 338.24(1)(b) by charging its workers in a particular county more than the prevailing rate for public transportation to and from its hiring halls and work sites. He sought injunctive relief and monetary damages. The trial court granted his request for class certification, finding that he satisfied Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.220(a)(1)-(4) and that injunctive relief might be appropriate. Accordingly, it was clear that the action was maintainable under those sections. The court found no abuse of discretion in the trial court's determination that the worker was suitable to serve as the designated class representative.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.
