Post-Newsweek Stations Orlando, Inc. v. Guetzloe


Case No. 5D07-430 & 5D07-526


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


968 So. 2d 608; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 15709; 35 Media L. Rep. 2357; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 2397



October 4, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 6, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Post-Newsweek Stations Orlando, Inc. v. Guetzloe, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 20084 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Nov. 19, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Non Final Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, Rom W. Powell, Senior Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a television station broadcaster, challenged a temporary injunction entered by the Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida) that prohibited it from broadcasting the contents of documents obtained from a storage unit leased by appellee.


OVERVIEW: Appellant came into possession of eighty boxes of appellee's records after they were sold at auction by the owner of a storage facility due to appellee's alleged failure to pay rent. Appellee alleged that the records remained his private property because the storage facility's determination that he had failed to pay was erroneous. The injunction entered by the trial court prohibited only the publication of the contents of medical records of appellee and his family and communications between appellee and his attorneys. Appellee conceded that the injunction operated as a prior restraint on the First Amendment rights of appellant and was therefore presumed unconstitutional. The appellate court held that there were hypothetical situations when publication of sensitive medical records or attorney-client communications might make an actionable invasion of privacy likely; the appellate court could not conclude that the publication of any such records would necessarily meet this threshold merely because of their nature. Speculation could not suffice to rebut the heavy presumption against a prior restraint. Thus, the trial court erred in entering the injunction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

Rehearing, en banc, denied by, Question certified by Wright v. Frankel, 970 So. 2d 504, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 20684 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2007)
Review denied by Wright v. Frankel, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1095 (Fla., June 2, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Consolidated appeals from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Amy L. Smith, Judge; L.T. Case No. 502006CA006094XXXXMB.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fifteenth Judicial Circuit Court, Palm Beach County (Florida), entered a judgment that determined that the doctrine of laches barred a mandamus action brought by appellant petition committee to compel appellee city to place an initiative for ordinances requiring voter approval for the relocation of two city buildings on the ballot. The petition committee appealed.


OVERVIEW: Citizens and registered voters disagreed with the city's decision to relocate the city hall and the city library. As a result, they formed a petition committee, which gathered signatures on initiative petitions for ordinances requiring voter approval for the relocations. When the city refused to place their proposed initiative on the ballot, the petition committee sought mandamus relief in the trial court to compel the city to place the initiative on the ballot. OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed and the case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Deonarine v. State


Nos. 4D05-2926 and 4D06-671


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


967 So. 2d 333; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 15569; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 2363



October 3, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 29, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Deonarine v. State, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 17813 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Oct. 29, 2007)
Review denied by Deonarine v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 353 (Fla., Feb. 25, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Consolidated appeals from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Richard I. Wennet, Judge; L.T. Case Nos. 01-8126CF10A02 and 01-5383CF10B02.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted and sentenced in the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), for counts of trafficking in a Schedule II drug over 28 grams, trafficking of a Schedule II drug over 4 grams but less than 14 grams, delivery of a Schedule IV drug, racketeering, Medicaid fraud, insurance fraud, and fraudulent insurance claim. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a physician who prescribed prescription drugs for a patient who became the physician's employee. The physician claimed that there was insufficient evidence of drug weight to support the trafficking counts and that the State of Florida was not permitted to have added together the multiple prescriptions over time which the physician wrote for the employee to reach the requisite weight to support the trafficking charges. On appeal, the court found that the prescriptions issued over a three-month period of time did not allow for the aggregation of the amounts of the prescribed controlled substances to support defendant's conviction for trafficking in a Schedule II drug over 28 grams. However, evidence of two prescriptions presented by the employee to a pharmacist at the same time was sufficient to support defendant's conviction for trafficking of a Schedule II drug over 4 grams but less than 14 grams. Finally, defendant's medical practice was an enterprise under § 895.02(3), Fla. Stat., and the multiple convictions of delivery, the trafficking charge, and the Medicaid fraud convictions were sufficient to satisfy the racketeering element of § 895.03(3), Fla. Stat. (2001).


OUTCOME: The conviction on the count for trafficking of a Schedule II drug over 28 grams was reversed, and the case was remanded to allow entry of a lesser included crime of delivery. The judgment was affirmed in all other respects.

Magee v. Magee (In re Estate of Magee)


Case No. 2D06-3692


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


988 So. 2d 1; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 15163; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 2307



September 26, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 11, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Magee v. Magee, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 21691 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., Nov. 30, 2007)
Review denied by Magee v. Magee, 977 So. 2d 576, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 301 (Fla., 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Pinellas County; George W. Greer, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee widow filed a petition for administration of the decedent's estate and a notice of her intent to seek the elective share. Appellant daughter objected to the election. The probate court entered a final order determining the widow's right as a surviving spouse to an elective share of the decedent's estate. The daughter appealed.


OVERVIEW: The daughter asserted that Florida's elective share statutes, §§ 732.201 to 732.2155, Fla. Stat. (2002), violated the Due Process Clause of the United States Constitution. She also argued that the elective share statutes violated Art. I, § 2, Fla. Const. On appeal, the court rejected the daughter's assertion that Florida's elective share statutes violated the Due Process Clause of the United States Constitution. Additionally, the State of Florida had a strong public policy concerning the protection of the surviving spouse of a marriage in existence at the time of the decedent's death. The provisions of the elective share statute thus served a legitimate legislative purpose. Furthermore, the statutes were rationally related to that purpose in that they sought to provide any surviving spouse who had not waived such protections a minority share in the assets of the decedent in the event that spouse did not receive as much through testamentary dispositions. Thus, Florida's elective share statutes were constitutional under Art. I, § 2, Fla. Const.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

Williams v. State


Case No. 2D06-2918


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


966 So. 2d 985; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 14547; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 2261



September 19, 2007, Opinion Filed

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1]

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an Anders appeal, defendant challenged the judgment and sentence entered by the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County (Florida) after defendant pled guilty to violating probation. Defendant was originally adjudicated guilty in 1992 on four counts of attempted sexual battery and one count of committing a lewd and lascivious act, all involving a victim under 12 years of age. Friends of the Great Southern, Inc. v. City Of Hollywood


No. 4D06-3365


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


964 So. 2d 827; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 14558; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 2254



September 19, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 5, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Richard D. Eade, Judge; L.T. Case No. 05-16383 05.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a corporation and individuals, sought review of a judgment entered by the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), which held that Hollywood, Fla., Land Development Code § 5.6.F.5.d was constitutional based on a grant of summary judgment to appellee city.


OVERVIEW: The city commission had approved, under § 5.6.F.5.d, a certificate of appropriateness for the partial demolition of a hotel, which was a contributing structure in the city's historic business district, and the proposed construction of a 19-story condominium, retail, and parking garage complex. Appellant sought a declaratory judgment to determine whether the criteria in § 5.6.F.5.d(1)-(8) were unconstitutionally vague and whether the city commission properly applied those criteria. The trial court found that § 5.6.F.5.d was constitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed. Because the language in § 5.6.F.5.d stating that the city commission "shall consider" the eight criteria was mandatory, the court held that the city commission did not have the discretion to consider factors outside the criteria provided. As the criteria enumerated in § 5.6.F.5.d were objective and sufficiently detailed, the provision was properly found to be constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1541 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Pinellas County v. City of Largo


Case No. 2D06-4826


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


964 So. 2d 847; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 14572; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 2220



September 19, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 5, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Pinellas County; Bruce Boyer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Summary judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee cities filed suit seeking to invalidate three ordinances by which appellant charter county attempted to create an exclusive method of voluntary municipal annexation. The Circuit Court for Pinellas County, Florida, granted the cities summary judgment on grounds the ordinances violated § 171.044(4), Fla. Stat. (2005) of the Florida Municipal Annexation or Contraction Act, §§ 171.011-.094, Fla. Stat. The county appealed.


OVERVIEW: The county adopted an ordinance that provided the exclusive method for voluntary annexation, delineating areas eligible for municipal annexation. The trial court held that a charter county could not adopt an exclusive method of voluntary municipal annexation under § 171.044(4). The appellate court disagreed. Under the plain language of § 171.044(4), a county could provide for such a method. It rejected the cities' argument that the legislature expressly or impliedly preempted Florida counties' authority to do so. However, § 171.044's voluntary annexation provisions did not apply to municipalities in counties with charters that provided for an exclusive method of municipal annexation. Thus, under § 171.044(4), the method of annexation had to be set forth in the charter; a charter county could not delineate the process in an ordinance. A charter county's exclusive method of voluntary municipal annexation was ineffective where, as here, it was not set forth in the charter and approved by the voters.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Shields v. Schuman


No. 4D07-1858


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


964 So. 2d 813; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 14608; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 2266



September 19, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 5, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Petition for writ of certiorari to the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Barry E. Goldstein, Judge. L.T. Case No. CACE 06-013334 (11).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner minority shareholder sued respondents, two owners of an office park and a buyer, seeking to enjoin a sale of an office park. The Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), created a cloud on the title and ordered the minority shareholder to post a bond of $ 8.5 million as a condition of maintaining his suit. The minority shareholder filed a petition for a writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court noted that the trial court was reluctant to require a bond as there was no pending lis pendens. After the buyer cited Maplewood Phase One Homeowner's Ass'n, Inc. v. Cecil and Archive America, Inc. v. Variety Children's Hospital, the bond was ordered. The cases were distinguishable in that they both involved existing liens that the courts permitted to be transferred to bonds. The buyer cited no authority that would authorize requiring a bond to be posted in order to maintain a lawsuit under these circumstances. The order requiring a bond, which was not related to a lis pendens, violated the minority shareholder's constitutional right of access to the courts under Fla. Const. art. I, § 21.


OUTCOME: Certiorari review was granted. The order requiring the bond was quashed.

 

1543 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


G.S. v. T.B.


CASE NO. 1D06-5264


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


969 So. 2d 1049; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 14239; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 2149



September 12, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by G.S. v. T.B., 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 20977 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Dec. 17, 2007)
Review granted by G.S. v. T.B., 975 So. 2d 1134, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 2527 (Fla., 2007)
Quashed by, Remanded by G.S. v. T.B., 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1243 (Fla., May 22, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An appeal from the Circuit Court for Duval County. L. Haldane Taylor, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant maternal grandparents sought to adopt their grandchildren. Appellee paternal grandparents resisted the request. The Circuit Court for Duval County (Florida) denied the petition. The maternal grandparents appealed.


OVERVIEW: The maternal grandparents sought reversal, alleging that the trial court abused its discretion by not entering a final judgment of adoption of the children after finding that the maternal grandparents were fit and proper persons to rear the children. The appellate court disagreed. The legislature vested broad discretion in the trial courts of Florida to determine the best interest of children sought to be adopted, and did not limit the traditional trial court's discretion. Ch. 63, Fla. Stat. did not require a trial court to enter a final judgment of adoption upon a determination that the persons seeking adoption were fit to rear the child, to the exclusion of other factors that impacted the child's best interest and might have dictated, in the discretion of the trial court, a disposition other than adoption. Here the trial court heard extensive testimony relating to the children's best interest and concluded their best interest compelled that the adoption should be denied. This was not an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1544 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wells


No. 4D06-3425


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


965 So. 2d 834; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 14264; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 2159



September 12, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 28, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Robert S. Zack, Judge; L.T. Case No. 05-035262 TC10A.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part; Reversed and Remanded in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with racing on highway under § 316.191, Fla. Stat. (2005) and filed a motion to dismiss challenging the constitutionality of the statute. The Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida) granted the motion and found § 316.191 unconstitutional on both vagueness and overbreadth grounds. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: An officer saw defendant driving his car at a high rate of speed. Another vehicle was following behind defendant's vehicle at a high rate of speed. The vehicles were not driving side by side. The vehicles, among other things, were weaving through traffic. The trial court found that § 316.191, Fla. Stat. on its face and as applied was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. The appellate court agreed that the statute was vague. The definition of "racing," in part as the use of one or more vehicles in an attempt to outgain or outdistance another motor vehicle, encompassed passing, accelerating from a stop, and countless other legal maneuvers which drivers employed in their daily lives. By failing to include an element of competition, the definition of "race," encompassed an endless range of otherwise legal conduct, primarily based on the "outgain and outdistance" term, including passing and accelerating from a stop so as to make the scope of proscribed conduct vague. However, the trial court erred by finding § 316.191 unconstitutional on overbreadth grounds. Overbreadth was not implicated because the statute did not affect a fundamental constitutional right.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment finding that § 316.191, Fla. Stat. (2005) was overbroad was reversed and the case was remanded in part for the trial court to strike the overbreadth findings. Otherwise, the judgment was affirmed.

Singleton v. Eli B. Inv. Corp.


No. 4D06-3582


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 14283; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 2183

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Robert L. Andrews, Judge; L.T. Case No. 05-18783 CACE 09.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, the purchaser of property at a tax sale, filed a complaint against appellants, the owners of the property, seeking to quiet title pursuant to the tax deed. The Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), entered summary judgment in favor of the purchaser. The owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owners asserted that they did not receive notice of the tax deed sale. The owners' affidavits in opposition to summary judgment specifically asserted that they were not notified by certified mail, return receipt requested, or by regular mail, that the clerk of court had actual knowledge that they were not notified because the notices, sealed and unopened, were still in the tax deed file, and that the sheriff failed to notify them by posting a copy of the notice in a conspicuous place at their home or otherwise notify them of the tax deed sale. The appellate court found that more efforts to provide notice to the owners were required in this case.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Smith v. Fisher


No. 4D06-4922


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


965 So. 2d 205; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 13886; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 2122



September 5, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 25, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Smith v. Fisher, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 17372 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Oct. 25, 2007)
Review denied by Smith v. Fisher, 980 So. 2d 490, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 606 (Fla., 2008)
Related proceeding at Smith v. Hernandez, 20 So. 3d 905, 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 14076 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2009)
Related proceeding at Smith v. Fisher, 116 So. 3d 1263, 2013 Fla. LEXIS 1027 (Fla., 2013)
Related proceeding at Smith v. Bondi, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 80526 (N.D. Fla., May 20, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Martin County; Robert R. Makemson, Judge; L.T. Case No. 03-196 CA.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate brought a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 case against appellee doctor based on the quality of cream prescribed for the inmate's "itching condition." The Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Martin County (Florida), found the inmate a vexatious litigant and ordered him to furnish security pursuant to § 68.093(3)(b) Fla. Stat. The inmate failed to furnish security, and the case was dismissed. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued that § 68.093, Fla. Stat. violated Art. I, § 21, Fla. Const. The appellate court found a difference of opinion between the inmate and a prison medical staff member as to treatment for the inmate's itching skin condition did not give rise to an Eighth Amendment violation. The $ 600 security required was reasonable on its face, far less than is typically incurred in a civil rights case to cover a defendant's anticipated, reasonable expenses of litigation, including attorney's fees and taxable costs. Section 68.093, Fla. Stat. satisfied the second Kluger test. The compelling state interest behind § 68.093, Fla. Stat. was to prevent vexatious litigation from interfering with the business of the court system, and the provision remedied the problem of meritless litigation in the most effective way and did not restrict the vexatious litigant's rights more than absolutely necessary. The statute subjected the vexatious litigant's case to close, up-front scrutiny, but had no effect on a case that was likely meritorious.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Phantom of Brevard, Inc. v. Brevard County


Case No. 5D06-3408


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


966 So. 2d 423; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 13431; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 2084



August 31, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 5, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Phantom of Brevard, Inc. v. Brevard County, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 18161 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Oct. 18, 2007)
Review granted by Phantom of Brevard, Inc. v. Brevard County, 982 So. 2d 685, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 750 (Fla., 2008)
Quashed by, in part Phantom of Brevard, Inc. v. Brevard County, 3 So. 3d 309, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 2431 (Fla., 2008)
Modified by, in part Phantom of Brevard, Inc. v. Brevard County, 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 3993 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Apr. 9, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Brevard County, T. Mitchell Barlow, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation brought an action against appellee county, seeking a judgment declaring Brevard County, Fla., Ordinance 05-60, as amended by Brevard County, Fla., Ordinance 06-18, to be unconstitutional. The Circuit Court for Brevard County (Florida) entered final summary judgment in favor of the county. The corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: The corporation argued that Brevard County, Fla., Ordinance 05-60, as amended by Brevard County, Fla., Ordinance 06-18, violated Art. VIII, § 1(g), Fla. Const. The corporation asserted that ch. 791, Fla. Stat. preempted local fireworks regulation. The appellate court disagreed. Contrary to the corporation's argument, the language of § 791.001, Fla. Stat. (2006) was insufficient to support the preemption argument. Neither ch. 791, Fla. Stat. nor the corresponding legislative history created any distinct line to neatly separate enforcement from regulation. If the legislature had a preemptive purpose, it did not make that purpose clear. Local governments, therefore, were free to exercise their lawmaking powers to facilitate enforcement, so long as the local ordinance was not inconsistent with general law. Nevertheless, Brevard County, Fla., Ordinance 05-60 § 8 invaded the exclusive province of the state legislature and judiciary. Brevard County, Fla., Ordinance 05-60 § 10 was in direct conflict with § 791.001, Fla. Stat., and Brevard County, Fla., Ordinance 05-60 § 13 improperly failed to account for permissible uses of fireworks, including ceremonial and military uses.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded with direction to the trial court to remand to sever Brevard County, Fla., Ordinance 05-60 §§ 8, 10, 13. The trial court was also directed to determine whether Brevard County, Fla., Ordinance 05-60 § 7 was valid. Otherwise, the judgment was affirmed.

Parker v. State


CASE NO. 1D04-1939


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


973 So. 2d 1167; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 13934; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 2093



August 31, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 20, 2007.

Rereleased for Publication March 5, 2008.
Review denied by Parker v. State, 1 So. 3d 173, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 535 (Fla., 2009)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by Parker v. State, 2011 Fla. App. LEXIS 10902 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., July 12, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. Thomas H. Bateman, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: At resentencing, the Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida) sentenced defendant as a prison releasee reoffender. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the State adduced only hearsay to prove the date of his prison release. At the resentencing hearing, the State relied on a "Certification of Records." The appellate court found that this document was sufficient. The affidavit attached to the records satisfied the requirements of § 90.902(11), Fla. Stat. The appellate court rejected defendant's argument that application of this provision, which became effective after the date of the commission of his offenses, was unconstitutional in violation of the ex post facto provision. Defendant erroneously asserted that prior to enactment of § 90.902(11), Fla. Stat., the State would have been required to present a witness with personal knowledge of his release date from prison. Instead, the State would have been required to present the live testimony of a records custodian. Section 90.902(11), Fla. Stat., in the present context, did not result in a conviction based on less evidence than the law required at the time the offense was committed. The evidence presented to establish his alleged release date from prison did not violate defendant's right of confrontation set forth in the Sixth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Prosper Diagnostic Ctrs. v. Allstate Ins. Co.


No. 4D07-12


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


964 So. 2d 763; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 13401; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 2069



August 29, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 17, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Petition for writ of certiorari to the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Richard D. Eade, Judge; L.T. Case No. 06-233 CACE05.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner health care provider file a petition for a writ of certiorari to quash an order by the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida) that affirmed the county court's grant of final summary judgment in favor of respondent insurer.


OVERVIEW: The insured was referred to the provider for a magnetic resonance image (MRI) following an automobile accident. The provider sought compensation for the MRI, which was actually performed by its lessee, from the insurer pursuant to an assignment of benefits executed in its favor by the insured. The insurer denied payment on the grounds that the amount the provider sought for the insured's MRI was not compensable. The county court granted final summary judgment in favor of the insurer because the provider rendered no professional or technical services at all pertaining to the MRI. The county court also found that the provider's "lease agreement" violated the prohibition against fee splitting and patient brokering in § 817.505(1)(b), Fla. Stat. (2002). The circuit court affirmed. The Court of Appeal found that because the provider neither performed the professional nor the technical components of the MRI itself and contracted the MRI services out to another entity pursuant to a "lease" arrangement, § 817.505(1)(b) was correctly applied. Therefore, the provider was not entitled to certiorari relief.


OUTCOME: The petition was denied.

Kuvin v. City of Coral Gables


No. 3D05-2845


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


62 So. 3d 604; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 13015; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 2009



August 22, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
As Corrected August 24, 2007.

Rothenberg Revised Dissent August 25, 2010.
On rehearing at, En banc, Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at Kuvin v. City of Coral Gables, 45 So. 3d 836, 2010 Fla. App. LEXIS 20776 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Michael A. Genden, Judge. Lower Tribunal No. 03-8911.
Kuvin v. City of Coral Gables, 917 So. 2d 201, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 20876 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a city resident, sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County (Florida), which upheld the validity of Coral Gables, Fla., Zoning Code §§ 8-11 and 8-12 by granting summary judgment to appellee city in the resident's declaratory judgment action, wherein he asserted that the ordinances were constitutionally violative of his personal rights.


OVERVIEW: The city enacted and strictly enforced rigorous restrictions on the design and construction of commercial and residential structures in order to maintain its reputation as a "beautiful city." The resident lived in a rental home with no garage, and he parked his personal pickup truck on the public asphalt in front of the residence. This conduct violated Coral Gables, Fla., Zoning Code §§ 8-11 and 8-12, and the resident was found guilty and fines and costs were assessed against him. He brought his declaratory judgment action, challenging the constitutionality of the ordinances. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the city, finding that the ordinances were constitutional. On appeal, the court held that there was no lawful basis for the restrictions imposed by the ordinances on city residents' freedom. A truck parking ban contained therein was not related to preserving the residential character of neighborhoods, as the ordinances were not restricted to only commercial vehicles. Further, matters of aesthetics were not within the government's concerns. The court concluded that there was no legitimate reason that supported the validity of the ordinances.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the matter with directions to enter a declaratory judgment in favor of the resident, and to vacate the guilty determination against him for his ordinance violations.

Sutton v. State


Case No. 5D07-2175


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


963 So. 2d 858; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 12360; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 1911



August 10, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 29, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: Sutton v. State, 905 So. 2d 148, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 10395 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., 2005)


DISPOSITION:  [**1] PETITION DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate brought a proceeding against respondent State, seeking a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmate had entered an open plea of nolo contendere and was sentenced to, inter alia, 50 years in prison with 30 years suspended, followed by a term of life probation for armed burglary, 30 years in prison with 10 years suspended, followed by 10 years' probation for first-degree felony murder, 5 years in prison for burglary of a conveyance, and 5 years in prison for burglary of a structure. Since his sentencing, the inmate had filed a motion for postconviction relief, a motion to correct sentence, and a petition for writ of prohibition, all of which were denied. The gist of his claim was the same as that raised in prior proceedings, which was premised on his view that the State failed to file a petition for delinquency and treat him as a juvenile. The instant petition was an improper attempt to use habeas review as a mechanism to collaterally attack his judgment and sentence.


OUTCOME: The petition was dismissed. The court also ruled that additional collateral attacks on the inmate's convictions and sentences, if successive and improper, would have resulted in sanctions, including an order barring him from filing additional collateral attacks on those convictions and sentences.

Masztal v. City of Miami


Nos. 3D06-1259, 3D06-920, 3D06-924, 3D06-947, 3D06-1255, 3D06-1055, 3D06-1046


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


971 So. 2d 803; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 12198; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 1881



August 8, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, En banc Masztal v. City of Miami, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 1385 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., Jan. 8, 2008)
Motion granted by Adorno & Yoss, LLC v. City of Miami, 1 So. 3d 171, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 2407 (Fla., 2009)
Related proceeding at Fla. Bar v. Adorno, 48 So. 3d 837, 2010 Fla. LEXIS 1818 (Fla., 2010)
Related proceeding at Matter of Adorno, 88 A.D.3d 1245, 931 N.Y.S.2d 545, 2011 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 7441 (N.Y. App. Div. 3d Dep't, 2011)
Related proceeding at In re Adorno, 2014 Fla. LEXIS 2360 (Fla., July 23, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Peter R. Lopez, Judge. Lower Tribunal No. 98-11208.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizens sued appellee city, challenging a special assessment; appellant property owners intervened. The Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Florida, granted the owners' and the city's motion to set aside a settlement and entered judgment against the citizens for the settlement amount; it reserved jurisdiction to determine prejudgment interest, costs, and attorneys' fees. All parties, as well as the citizens' attorneys, appealed.


OVERVIEW: The citizens filed a class action suit alleging the city improperly imposed a special assessment and seeking a refund of the assessments. Before a class was certified, they settled with the city. They admitted the settlement was a significant windfall as compared to the refund amount they would have received under a class settlement. The city and property owners sought to set aside the settlement. The trial court found that there was an implied class action requiring judicial approval of the individual settlement for fairness and reasonableness; that the citizens and attorneys breached their fiduciary duties to the class; and that the city committed a unilateral mistake in believing the settlement was class-wide, not for individual claims. Therefore, it rescinded the settlement agreement. The appellate court noted that the amount the citizens received bore no relation to the amount they paid in assessments. There was an implied fiduciary relationship between the citizens, their attorneys, and the class. As the settlement prejudiced the class, the citizens and attorneys breached their fiduciary duty to the class by entering into a settlement that benefitted only seven citizens.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

City of Tampa v. Addison


Case No. 2D06-3168


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


979 So. 2d 246; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 14708; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 1866



August 8, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by City of Tampa v. Addison, 980 So. 2d 1070, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 639 (Fla., 2008)
Related proceeding at Addison v. City of Tampa, 2010 Fla. App. LEXIS 4493 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., Apr. 7, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: Addison v. City of Tampa, 887 So. 2d 334, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 16058 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2004)


DISPOSITION:  [**1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a nonfinal order by the Circuit Court (Florida) which certified a bilateral class action brought by appellee attorneys who were members of The Florida Bar and maintained an office within the jurisdiction of the city. The attorneys challenged the constitutionality of the city's occupational license tax as applied to their practicing law in the city. They sought, inter alia, declaratory and injunctive relief.


OVERVIEW: The trial court certified a plaintiff class consisting of all lawyers subject to local occupational license taxes in all municipalities and counties within the State of Florida pursuant to Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.220(b)(2), (3) and a defendant class consisting of all municipalities and counties within Florida that levied such occupational license taxes pursuant to Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.220(b)(1)(A). The appellate court held the trial court properly excluded evidence concerning each attorney's income because it was not relevant to any issue at the hearing on class certification. The enactment of the various occupational license tax ordinances under the authority of the same enabling legislation by all of the members of the proposed defendant class provided the requisite "juridical link" that authorized the certification of the proposed defendant class. It did not appear that the city had any interests that were antagonistic to the interests of the other members of the proposed defendant class. The deposition testimony of one of the class attorneys included competent substantial evidence from which the trial court could find that the city was an adequate representative for the defendant class.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Peninsular Props. Braden River, LLC v. City of Bradenton


Case No. 2D06-5302


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


965 So. 2d 160; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 11693; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 1815



August 1, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 23, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Peninsular Props. Braden River, LLC v. City of Bradenton, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 17610 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., Oct. 5, 2007)
Review denied by City of Bradenton v. Peninsular Props. Braden River, LLC, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 83 (Fla., Jan. 10, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Manatee County; Durand J. Adams, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant developers filed a petition for writ of certiorari seeking to overturn appellee city's rejection of their application for a planned development project. The Circuit Court for Manatee County (Florida) dismissed the petition based on a finding that it was untimely filed. The developers appealed.


OVERVIEW: Although the developers' petition was filed more than 30 days after the city's order denying their application, the developers asserted that the time limit was tolled under the Florida Land Use and Environmental Dispute Resolution Act (Act), § 70.51, Fla. Stat. The trial court found, however, that the Act was unconstitutional. The appellate court ruled that this was error. The trial court found that the Act was an unconstitutional infringement on the rule-making authority of the Supreme Court of Florida under Art. V, § 2(a), Fla. Const. However, there were circumstances where a legislative provision which would have been deemed procedural if viewed in isolation would have nonetheless been upheld against a challenge under Art. V, § 2(a), Fla. Const. because of the connection between that provision and substantive provisions adopted by the legislature. Because the procedural tolling provision of § 70.51(10)(a), Fla. Stat., was intertwined with the remainder of the statute, the trial court erred in finding that section unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded.

Pesci v. State


No. 3D06-234


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


963 So. 2d 780; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 10970; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 1721



July 18, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 26, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Pesci v. State, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 15970 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., Sept. 26, 2007)
Review denied by Pesci v. State, 973 So. 2d 1122, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 2493 (Fla., 2007)
Subsequent civil proceeding at, Dismissed by Pesci v. Budz, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 14987 (M.D. Fla., Feb. 8, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
$80An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Monroe County, Richard G. Payne, Judge. Lower Tribunal No. 01-257.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, the State of Florida, petitioned the Circuit Court for Monroe County (Florida), for the involuntary civil commitment of appellant patient as a sexually violent predator under Florida's Jimmy Ryce Act, §§ 394.910 through 394.932, Fla. Stat. After a trial, the court found that the patient was a sexually violent predator and civilly committed him for treatment. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: The patient challenged the trial court's admission of hearsay evidence regarding an alleged prior offense committed by the patient in another state. The patient attempted to evade prosecution for the alleged prior offense by fleeing to Florida and changing his name. However, he admitted to nearly everything contained in the police reports regarding the incident. On appeal, the appellate court found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion under § 394.9155, Fla. Stat. (2006) in admitting the hearsay evidence regarding the prior offense because (1) the evidence was reliable; and (2) the patient's rights under the Confrontation Clauses of both the United States and Florida Constitutions were not violated as the Confrontation Clauses were limited in application to criminal prosecutions, and were therefore inapplicable to civil commitment proceedings under the Jimmy Ryce Act. Furthermore, based on the substantial unobjected-to evidence that was presented at the trial, any error in the introduction of the objected-to evidence was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Rupp v. Dep't of Health


No. 3D06-1769


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


963 So. 2d 790; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 10978; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 1724



July 18, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 28, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the State of Florida, Department of Health. Lower Tribunal Nos. 04-35830 & 05-3242.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions that judgment be entered in Dr. Rupp's favor.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After appellee, the Florida Department of Health's Board of Medicine (Board), imposed certain penalties against appellant doctor for her failure to report timely an administrative disciplinary action taken against her in the State of Virginia, the doctor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The doctor first contended that the Board's order was invalid because it imposed sanctions on her for failure to take actions that the order acknowledged were impossible to perform. The appeals court agreed. The order specifically found that the doctor was to be punished for failing to comply with the notification requirements of § 458.331(l)(kk), Fla. Stat., which the judge's own order specifically acknowledged could not be done, and despite the fact that the doctor was physically unable to comply. Further, it simply defied logic that the doctor's noncompliance would not be excused when she did not know, nor could she have known, that the action taken against her in Virginia had taken place. Second, the doctor correctly asserted that the Board was required to conduct a de novo review of the record, and, by its own admission, it did not do so. This admitted failure amounted to a material error in procedure which made it impossible for the doctor to obtain a fair hearing. It also violated the doctor's right to due process by refusing her the opportunity to present her case, and resulted in an unjust punishment.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded with instructions that judgment be entered in the doctor's favor.

Liner v. Workers Temp. Staffing, Inc.


No. 4D05-4729


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


962 So. 2d 344; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 10387; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 1628



July 5, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by, Remanded by Liner v. Workers Temp. Staffing, Inc., 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1380 (Fla., July 31, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Leroy H. Moe, Judge; L.T. Case No. 04-07313 (13).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant day laborer appealed an order by the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County, (Florida) that, inter alia, found § 448.24(1)(b) of the Labor Pool Act, §§ 448.20-448.25, Fla. Stat. (2003), was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: The day laborer filed a class-action complaint against appellee employer, alleging that it had violated § 448.24(1)(b), Fla. Stat. (2003) (amended 2006) by overcharging day laborers for transportation between its labor halls and worksites. The day laborer claimed that he was overcharged 50 cents for each trip and that he incurred $ 265 in actual damages. The day laborer sought statutory damages of $ 177,000 under § 448.25(1), Fla. Stat. (2003). The appellate court found, inter alia, that the terms "reasonable amount," "public transportation," and "geographic area," in § 448.24(1)(b), Fla. Stat. (2003) impermissibly delegated basic policy matters to judges and juries for resolution on an ad hoc and subjective basis, with the attendant dangers of arbitrary and discriminatory application. The statute failed to give persons of common intelligence and understanding adequate warning or fair notice of the proscribed conduct. Therefore, the trial court properly found that the section was unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

Abbott v. State


No. 4D06-3100


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


958 So. 2d 1140; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 10014; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 1601



June 27, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Rehearing denied by Abbott v. State, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 12030 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., July 19, 2007)Released for Publication July 19, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, St. Lucie County; Gary L. Sweet, Judge; L.T. Case No. 562004CF004759A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, St. Lucie County (Florida), convicted defendant of two counts of lewd or lascivious molestation of a child under 12 years of age. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the jury instructions were erroneous since they encompassed masturbation or the commission of other lewd acts in the victim's presence, which were not a part of the charged offense or the evidence at trial. Defendant did not object to the challenged instruction at trial, but argued that fundamental error occurred because the jury returned a general verdict, and it was impossible to determine whether the jury convicted him of the charged or uncharged offenses. The appellate court found no fundamental error. The uncharged crimes were never at issue during defendant's trial, and the State never argued or presented evidence that defendant committed those acts. Reversal was not warranted where a general verdict could have rested upon a theory of liability without adequate evidentiary support when there was an alternative theory of guilt for which the evidence was sufficient. Because defendant's claim of ineffective assistance of counsel was not apparent from the record, the appellate court declined to consider this issue.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Lawnwood Med. Ctr., Inc. v. Seeger


CASE NO. 1D06-2016


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


959 So. 2d 1222; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 9569; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 1543



June 21, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 9, 2007.
Affirmed by Lawnwood Med. Ctr. v. Seeger, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1458 (Fla., Aug. 28, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An appeal from the Circuit Court of Leon County. Janet E. Ferris, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The summary final judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action between appellant hospital and appellee doctor, the Circuit Court of Leon County (Florida) invalidated the St. Lucie County Hospital Governance Law, 2003 Fla. Laws ch. 372. The hospital appealed.


OVERVIEW: A contract had been established between the hospital's board of trustees and its medical staff. The appellate court found that 2003 Fla. Laws ch. 372 dramatically altered many of the rights and obligations specified in the contract, thus constituting an "impairment" under Art. I, § 10, Fla. Const. The hospital acknowledged that 2003 Fla. Laws ch. 372 effected an impairment through diminution of the medical staff's contract rights, but argued that the law was valid under a balancing test. But 2003 Fla. Laws ch. 372 was unconstitutional even under this test because the contract impairment was not required to protect the public health, ensure the quality of care at the hospital, or accomplish some other legitimate public purpose. The legislation also unconstitutionally granted a privilege to a private corporation in violation of Art. III, § 11(a)(12). Although 2003 Fla. Laws ch. 372 applied to all hospitals located in St. Lucie County, there were only two hospitals in St. Lucie County and both were controlled by the same private corporation. Thus, the law therefore unconstitutionally granted a substantial privilege to this private corporation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1561 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Fredman v. Fredman


Case No. 2D06-1674


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


960 So. 2d 52; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 9511; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 1504



June 20, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Released for Publication July 25, 2007.
Review denied by Fredman v. Fredman, 968 So. 2d 556, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1932 (Fla., 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Melton v. Fredman, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 2330 (U.S., Mar. 3, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County; Monica L. Sierra, Judge.
Fredman v. Fredman, 917 So. 2d 1038, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 111 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother filed a petition to modify appellee father's visitation because she planned to move to Texas with the parties' two children. The father moved to enjoin her from removing the children from Florida. The Circuit Court for Hillsborough County, Florida, denied the mother's request to relocate. She appealed, contending that the parental relocation statute, former § 61.13(2)(d), Fla. Stat. (2004), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The parties had shared parental responsibility; the mother was the primary residential parent. The appellate court did not address § 61.13001, Fla. Stat., which replaced § 61.13(2)(d). It held that § 61.13(2)(d) did not violate the mother's right to privacy under Fla. Const. art. I, § 23, as the father, who had shared parental responsibility under § 61.046(15), Fla. Stat., had the same fundamental right as she did to decide where the children lived. As § 61.13(2)(d) required the trial court to consider competing interests, with an appropriate focus on the parents' rights, along with the best interest of the child, it did not violate the right to travel of the parent wishing to relocate. The father's choice to move out of state would not deny the mother access to her children. Thus, to the extent that a primary residential parent had to seek permission to relocate, the parties were not similarly situated; therefore, § 61.13(2)(d) did not violate the Equal Protection Clause. The trial court properly held that relocation was not in the children's best interest, as it found that the mother failed to show that the proposed move would improve their school, family, or even home life.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Avante Villa at Jacksonville Beach, Inc. v. Breidert


CASE NO. 1D06-4880


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


958 So. 2d 1031; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 8716; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 1413



June 5, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 21, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari -- Original Jurisdiction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner nursing home sought a writ of certiorari seeking review of an order compelling the discovery of documents it claimed to be privileged, in an underlying suit filed against it by respondent personal representative.


OVERVIEW: Upon a review of the record, the court found that the documents ordered disclosed were not discoverable because nursing homes did not fall within the definition of "health care facility" or "health care provider" as contemplated by Fla. Const. amend. VII, later incorporated as Art. X, § 25, Fla. Const.. Thus, the court did not address the nursing home's preemption claim. As the trial court was required to apply the law of Florida's Constitution as codified and clarified in § 381.028, Fla. Stat. (2005), which excluded nursing homes and skilled nursing facilities, in finding that a nursing home was a health care provider and compelling production of the documents at issue, it departed from the essential requirements of law. Further, the erroneous production of privileged and/or protected documents could not be remedied on appeal. Finally, because this was a question of great public importance, the following question was certified to the Florida Supreme Court: "Whether "nursing homes" or "skilled nursing facilities" fell within the definition of "health care facility" or "health care provider" as contemplated by Fla. Const. amend. VII?


OUTCOME: The writ was granted, and the order compelling discovery was vacated.

 

1563 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Masters v. State


Case No. 5D06-3508


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


958 So. 2d 973; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 7591; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 1304



May 18, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 6, 2007.
Review denied by Masters v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1651 (Fla., Aug. 31, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for St. Johns County, Wendy Berger, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the Circuit Court for St. Johns County (Florida) civilly committed appellant inmate under the Jimmy Ryce Act, §§ 394.910-.930, Fla. Stat. (2002), he appealed, alleging that: (1) the trial court erred in admitting unreliable hearsay evidence against him; and (2) § 394.9155(5), Fla. Stat. (2006) violated Art. V, § 2(a), Fla. Const..


OVERVIEW: The appeals court disagreed with the inmate's claims. First, as the court relied upon the testimony from all three doctors about three disciplinary reports the inmate received, the inmate should have objected to each doctor's testimony, not just one. Having failed to do so, his claim of error in their admission was not preserved. Even if it was preserved, the inmate ignored the fact that the State sought to admit testimony regarding the disciplinary reports under § 90.704, Fla. Stat., which allowed an expert witnesses to testify about facts or data upon which an expert based an opinion, so long as those facts or data were of a type reasonably relied upon by experts in the subject to support the opinion expressed. Moreover, there was ample non-hearsay evidence demonstrating a need to commit the inmate. Finally, the inmate's constitutionality challenge was previously rejected by the Second District Court of Appeals. The Confrontation Clauses of both the United States and Florida Constitutions are expressly limited to criminal prosecutions. As such, the constitutional right of confrontation does not bar the admission of hearsay evidence in civil commitment proceedings.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Lee


Case No. 5D06-2993


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


957 So. 2d 76; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 7151; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 1251



May 11, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 31, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Brevard County, Meryl L. Allawas, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Brevard County (Florida) suppressed the evidence seized upon defendant's arrest after a stop of his vehicle for an inoperable tag light. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: While maintaining that the tag light did not work, the State also argued that the validity of the stop of defendant's vehicle did not depend on whether the light worked; the State claimed the stop was valid if the deputy had a reasonable suspicion that a traffic infraction had occurred. Further, the odor of burnt or burning cannabis detected as the deputy approached defendant provided him with probable cause to search the vehicle. Upon a review of the evidence, the appeals court held that although the trial court concluded that the failure to verify the light's function after stopping the vehicle impaired the accuracy and credibility of the deputy's estimations, it did not matter. The deputy's observation that the light was not working, from forty to fifty feet away, was sufficient to warrant a man of reasonable caution to believe that the taillight was, in fact, inoperable and to stop the vehicle under § 316.221(2), Fla. Stat. (2005), and whether or not the deputy further inspected the vehicle after stopping defendant, it was lawful for him to approach defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded.

Zingale v. Crossings at Fleming Island Cmty. Dev. Dist.


CASE NO. 1D06-2026/1D06-2158 Consolidated


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


960 So. 2d 20; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 7005; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 1209



May 8, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 6, 2007.
Motion granted by Zingale v. Crossings at Fleming, Island, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 21714 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., June 26, 2007)
Rehearing denied by Zingale v. Crossings at Fleming Island, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 12935 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., July 19, 2007)
Review granted by, Sub nomine at Crossings at Fleming Island Cmty. Dev. Dist. v. Echeverri, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 2264 (Fla., Nov. 29, 2007)
Quashed by Crossings at Fleming Island Cmty. Dev. Dist. v. Echeverri, 991 So. 2d 793, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1222 (Fla., 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An appeal from the Circuit Court for Clay County. Marvin Gillman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED in part; REVERSED in part and REMANDED with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee community development district sued appellants, the appraiser and the Florida Department of Revenue, in the Circuit Court for Clay County (Florida), for declaratory and injunctive relief. The court found that properties of the district were exempt from ad valorem taxation for certain tax years, and ruled that the appraiser did not have standing to challenge the constitutionality of a statute. The appraiser and the Department appealed.


OVERVIEW: The district, pursuant to § 189.403(1), Fla. Stat. (1999), was a residential community that owned and operated public recreational facilities, including a golf course, swimming pools, tennis courts, and playgrounds. On appeal, the court found that the properties were used for a proper municipal purpose and were therefore exempt from ad valorem taxation under § 196.199(1), Fla. Stat. (1999). Significantly, the properties were open to the public and were not operated for profit, notwithstanding that they were operated by a management company. Thus, the properties, for exemption purposes, were to be treated the same as parks and recreation opportunities traditionally provided by municipalities, that were explicitly recognized as exempt property. However, the trial court erred by granting an exemption based on the separate and independent ground of disparate treatment because there was not competent substantial evidence to show that the district was treated differently from all, or substantially all, similar properties in the county. Finally, the appraiser had standing, in his defensive procedural posture in the case, to assert that § 189.403(1), Fla. Stat., was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The trial court's ruling that the property was exempt from an ad valorem tax was affirmed. The trial court's denial of the appraiser's affirmative defense on the constitutional issue was reversed and remanded for the trial court to address the defense.

Wheeler v. State


Case No. 2D05-5493


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


956 So. 2d 517; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 6781; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 1193



May 4, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 20, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Wheeler v. State, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 10512 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., June 4, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the Circuit Court for Polk County (Florida) denied defendant's motion to suppress the contraband found in his home, it convicted him of trafficking in methamphetamine, possession of oxycodone, possession of marijuana, possession of drug paraphernalia, resisting an officer without violence, and possession of a firearm. Defendant thus appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's motion to suppress alleged that the evidence seized amounted to the fruits of an illegal search. The appeals court agreed. First, the testimony presented to the trial court failed to show that an emergency existed. Upon arrival, the deputies found nothing to corroborate the report of a crime. There was nothing suspicious about the residence itself, such as an open door, and the deputies did not determine that there were persons inside the residence who refused to answer the door. Despite the fact that an anonymous 911 call had been placed, the officers were faced with no facts which led them to believe that a crime was afoot or that an exigency existed. Likewise, the inevitable discover rule did not apply, as the contraband seized would not have been discovered by any legal means. Moreover, when defendant opened the door to his residence and stepped outside in response to the deputies' knock, his exchange with them was a citizen encounter, which, in the absence of further detail or corroboration, did not provide the deputies with either reasonable suspicion to detain him, or probable cause to arrest him on the reported battery.


OUTCOME: The order denying suppression, as well as defendant's convictions, were reversed and the case was remanded.

Lecroy v. State


No. 4D06-403


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


954 So. 2d 747; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 6651; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 1141



May 2, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Lecroy v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1613 (Fla., Aug. 23, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Edward A. Garrison, Judge; L.T. Case No. 81-000219 CFA02.
Lecroy v. State, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 1786 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Feb. 14, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion for rehearing of his appeal of a judgment by the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County, (Florida) that resentenced him; defendant claimed that he was not represented by counsel at the sentencing proceeding in violation of his constitutional rights.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that the trial court simply conformed the sentence to a pronouncement by the state supreme court. Because the trial court had no jurisdiction to do otherwise, it performed a ministerial act. Therefore, defendant's presence was not required. The order by the supreme court specified the exact sentence to be imposed: life imprisonment without the possibility of parole for 25 years. The trial court had no jurisdiction to vary from that mandate. Thus, the case was akin to those cases where the appellate court remanded for a trial court to conform the written sentence to its oral pronouncement.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

Dep't of Corr. v. Daughtry


Case No. 5D05-3876


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


954 So. 2d 659; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 4961; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 900



April 5, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 23, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Volusia County, Joseph G. Will, Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDER VACATED in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Florida Department of Corrections (DOC), appealed the order of the Seventh Judicial Circuit Court for Volusia County (Florida), which enjoined the DOC from engaging in the practice of automatically violating the probation of every sex offender who failed to give an address acceptable pursuant to § 948.30(1)(b), Fla. Stat. (2005), at the time of a scheduled release from incarceration.


OVERVIEW: Appellee probationer was sentenced to a split sentence of seven years' incarceration to be followed by five years of sex offender probation. After completing the incarceration term, the probationer was arrested immediately upon his release from prison on the ground that he had violated a special condition of his probation. The DOC asserted that it had a statutory obligation to report a compliant residence address for each sex offender releasee. At a bond hearing, the trial court realized that the probationer's "violation" was the inability to supply a compliant address prior to leaving prison and questioned the DOC's basis for conducting a warrantless arrest of the probationer immediately upon the expiration of his prison term. The appellate court concluded that the DOC correctly asserted multiple reasons why the injunctive provisions of the challenged order had to be reversed. First, the DOC was not a party to the proceedings and no notice was given to the DOC that such an order was within the contemplation of the court. Nor had the probationer filed any motion or sought injunctive relief. The provisions of the trial court order directed to the DOC were not authorized.


OUTCOME: The injunctive provisions of the trial court's order were vacated.

Fla. Hometown Democracy, Inc. v. Cobb


CASE NO. 1D06-5059


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


953 So. 2d 666; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 4666; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 852



March 30, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 17, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. Terry P. Lewis, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida) granted summary judgment in favor of appellee, Florida's Secretary of State (Secretary), in a suit filed against her by appellants seeking declaratory and injunctive relief challenging the constitutionality of a legislatively proposed revision to the Florida Constitution known as Senate Joint Resolution (SJR) 2394. Appellants thereafter sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The proposed legislation at issue sought to place time limitations on amendments to the Florida Constitution proposed by citizen's initiatives. On appeal, the court upheld the legislation first finding that appellants failed to explain how the ballot title mischaracterized the proposed revision's main purpose. Second, the language sufficiently apprised voters that it dealt with proposed changes to the constitution. Third, the summary and title adequately apprised the electorate that the proposed amendment would serve to establish a cut-off date, 9 months prior to the general election, for the filing of a citizen's initiative petition. Further, although the Secretary failed to publish the notices as expressly required in all Florida counties, the lack of proper notification in only four out of sixty-seven counties was not fatal to the legislation. Finally, it was apparent that § 101.161(1): (1) applied to all similarly situated persons to appellants; (2) did not intentionally discriminate against appellants alone; and (3) passed a rational basis scrutiny. Accordingly, the statute passed muster under the equal protection clause.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1572 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Companioni v. City of Tampa


Case No. 2D05-688


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


958 So. 2d 404; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 4679; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 840



March 30, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected April 4, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Companioni v. City of Tampa, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 11858 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., May 15, 2007)Released for Publication July 20, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County; Herbert J. Baumann, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant injured person sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County (Florida) which granted appellee city's motion for a new trial in a personal injury action where the jury verdict was in favor of the injured person. The trial court granted the motion on the ground that two jurors were not qualified to serve because they had previously been convicted of felonies and had not had their civil rights restored.


OVERVIEW: The injured person was injured when his motorcycle collided with a city water truck. The trial court qualified the prospective jurors in a central juror assembly room prior to the beginning of the trial. The prospective jurors completed a standard questionnaire. During the voir dire examination, the jurors were not asked any questions about prior felony convictions or their statutory qualifications to serve on a jury. After the verdict, the city moved for a new trial, alleging that two members of the six-person jury failed to disclose prior felony convictions and had not had their civil rights restored. The appellate court accepted, for purposes of analysis, that the jurors concealed their prior felony convictions during the jury qualification proceeding. However, the appellate court held that to the extent the theory that felon jurors had an "inherent bias" had any validity, its applicability was limited to criminal cases. It had no application to civil cases. The city was not entitled to a new trial on account of the jurors' prior felony convictions in the absence of a showing of actual bias or prejudice or that the city did not receive a fair and impartial trial.


OUTCOME: The order granting the city a new trial was reversed. The matter was remanded for the reinstatement of the jury's verdict and the judgment. On remand, the trial court was to conduct further proceedings to dispose of the city's motion for remittitur, its motion to alter or amend the judgment, and the other grounds raised by the city in its motion for new trial.
