T.A. Enters. v. Olarte, Inc.


Nos. 4D05-829 & 4D05-3052


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


951 So. 2d 978; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 3728; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 715



March 14, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 30, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: Consolidated appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Miette K. Burnstein, Judge; L.T. Case No. 01-17597 CACE (21).
T.A. Enters. v. Olarte, Inc., 931 So. 2d 1016, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 8940 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2006)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), awarded damages and attorney's fees to appellee buyer, and against appellant manufacturer, in the buyer's action under Florida's Lemon Law. The manufacturer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The manufacturer challenged the judgment entered, claiming error. The appeals court first held that the trial court erred in awarding the buyer damages because evidence of damages was never presented at the trial de novo. Further, the buyer was not entitled to a new trial on damages. The appeals court also reversed the trial court's award of attorney's fees to the buyer because it failed to plead entitlement to such fees, and no exceptions applied.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded.

 

1574 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Massey v. David


CASE NO. 1D06-3657


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


953 So. 2d 599; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 3653; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 683



March 12, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 27, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Massey v. David, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 7001 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Apr. 11, 2007)
Affirmed by Massey v. David, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 552 (Fla., Apr. 3, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Alachua County. Robert E. Roundtree, Jr., Judge.
Massey v. David, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 2156 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Feb. 15, 2007)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant client sued appellee attorney in the Circuit Court for Alachua County (Florida), for legal malpractice. The jury, in a bifurcated trial, found negligence on the part of the attorney that caused damage to the client. However, the jury awarded no damages to the client. The trial court then rendered a separate judgment awarding costs to the attorney. The client appealed.


OVERVIEW: The client alleged that the trial court erred in awarding the attorney costs for expert witnesses, and erred when it did not enter judgment for the client after the first phase of the trial and award him costs and fees in connection with that phase. On appeal, the court found that § 57.071(2), Fla. Stat. (1999), was an unconstitutional intrusion on the powers of the judiciary, through the Florida Supreme Court under Art. V, § 2(a), Fla. Const., to determine matters of practice and procedure in the Florida Courts. Even if the statute was substantive, it did not apply in the case as it was then restricted to prospective effect. In addition, the client did not show that the trial court abused its discretion as to the amount of the costs which it awarded. Finally, the jury ultimately returned a verdict awarding the client no damages. Thus, the client did not satisfy the third element of his legal malpractice claim as the attorney's actions did not cause the client to suffer any injury. Accordingly, the trial court properly entered a final judgment in favor of the attorney at the conclusion of the proceeding, and the client was not entitled to costs under § 57.041(1), Fla. Stat. (1997).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1575 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bryant


CASE NO. 1D06-2075


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


953 So. 2d 585; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 3289; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 635



March 7, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 3, 2007.
Rehearing denied by State v. Bryant, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 7339 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Apr. 17, 2007)
Review denied by Bryant v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1645 (Fla., Aug. 31, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court of Alachua County. Martha Ann Lott, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order under review is accordingly reversed and this case is remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Alachua County (Florida) dismissed a count of an information charging defendant with using drug paraphernalia to transport cocaine, in violation of § 893.147(4), Fla. Stat. on grounds that said statute was unconstitutional because the statutory term "transport," as used therein, was overbroad and vague. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Upon a review of the record, the appellate court first rejected the trial court's conclusion that the term "transport," as used in § 893.147(4), Fla. Stat., rendered the statute unconstitutionally overbroad. As to this issue, it noted that legislation was overbroad when it was drafted in a manner that could be applied to conduct protected by the First Amendment. Because there was no danger of any such constitutionally-protected conduct being impacted in defendant's case, the statute was not overbroad. Second, the court rejected the trial court's conclusion that the same term made the statute unconstitutionally vague. The word "transport" clearly communicated to both law enforcement officers and members of the general public the concept of conveying a thing from one place to another. Although the use of this term in conjunction with the broad statutory definition of drug paraphernalia meant that § 893.147(4) would likely apply to a significant number of individuals who at some point possess such paraphernalia or certain controlled substances or contraband, there was nothing unconstitutionally vague about the term itself or the manner in which it is used in the statute.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded.

 

1576 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Thompson v. State


CASE NO. 1D06-0420


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


949 So. 2d 1169; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 3044; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 614



March 2, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 20, 2007.
Review granted by Thompson v. State, 959 So. 2d 718, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1247 (Fla., 2007)
Reversed by, Remanded by Thompson v. State, 990 So. 2d 482, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1456 (Fla., 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. Kathleen F. Dekker, Judge.
Thompson v. State, 764 So. 2d 630, 2000 Fla. App. LEXIS 3768 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2000)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida) denied defendant's motion for post-conviction relief. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: While defendant raised numerous grounds for relief, he only raised three of those grounds on appeal. Finding none had merit, the appeals court upheld the trial court's order. First, at the time defendant's sentence became final, Apprendi did not apply. Moreover, Blakely did not apply because the judgment and sentence were already final when Blakely was decided. Second, defendant was unable to demonstrate any prejudice from counsel's alleged deficient performance and failed to show that the aggravating factors relied upon by the court to impose a heightened sentence did not exist. Nor did defendant allege that, assuming the existence of these aggravating factors, the sentence actually imposed was not within the trial court's discretion. Because the sentences were lawful, the mere fact that the trial court imposed such was not evidence of prejudice resulting from his attorney's failure to timely file the motion to disqualify. Third, defendant failed to establish a structural defect. While defendant alleged that the trial judge could have been disqualified by a timely filed motion to disqualify, he did not show that the judge was actually biased.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. The court also certified conflict with Goines and Kleppinger, decisions in the Fourth and Second Districts, respectively, to the extent they interpret the U.S. Supreme Court decision in Lockhart as modifying or supplanting the ineffective assistance of counsel standard set down in Strickland.

 

1577 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


A.J. v. K.A.O.


Case No. 5D06-3451


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


951 So. 2d 30; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 3009; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 613



February 27, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 16, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, George A. Sprinkel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee mother filed a petition to terminate appellant father's parental rights pending a stepparent adoption. The petition alleged that the father had abandoned the children, had willfully refused to pay child support, and had been sentenced to 10 years in federal prison. The Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida) terminated the father's parental rights. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the father argued that ch. 63, Fla. Stat. was unconstitutional on its face because there was no requirement that termination be the least restrictive alternative. The appellate court held that the least restrictive means test applied to ch. 63, Fla. Stat. involuntary termination proceedings as it had been applied to ch. 39. Fla. Stat. involuntary termination proceedings. There was evidence that the father was incarcerated until 2012, at which time the children would be 14 and 16. The children did not have contact with the father. The guardian ad litem testified, based on personally visiting the prison and interviewing numerous people, that requiring the children to visit the father would have been detrimental to them. The trial court also noted a letter in the court file from the school guidance counselor which expressed the same opinion. Furthermore, the children's stepfather had acted in every capacity as their real father and wanted to adopt them. There was ample evidence that termination of the father's parental rights was the least restrictive means of protecting the children.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State Dep't of Highway Safety & Motor Vehicles v. Rendon


No. 3D02-611


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


957 So. 2d 647; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 2366; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 522



February 21, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Released for Publication June 25, 2007.
Rehearing denied by State Dep't of Highway Safety & Motor Vehicles v. Rendon, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 10655 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., June 8, 2007)
Review dismissed by Fla. Dep't of Highway Safety & Motor Vehicles v. Rendon, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1488 (Fla., Aug. 18, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Amy Steele Donner, Judge. Lower Tribunal No. 96-17716.
Rendon v. Fla. Dep't of Hwy. Safety & Motor Vehicles, 541 U.S. 1059, 124 S. Ct. 2387, 158 L. Ed. 2d 960, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 3685 (2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee handicapped drivers filed a class action against appellant state agencies in the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County (Florida), challenging fees imposed by the State of Florida for issuance and renewal of disabled parking permits. The court granted declaratory, injunctive, and monetary relief, ruling that the fees violated 28 C.F.R. § 35.130(f), a regulation under the federal Americans with Disabilities Act. The agencies appealed.


OVERVIEW: The drivers sought to recover fees which they paid that allowed them to park in handicapped spaces. On appeal, the court found that sovereign immunity under the Eleventh Amendment barred an unconsented action against the State of Florida for damages, but did not bar a suit for nonmonetary relief, such as declaratory or injunctive relief. Further, there was no valid barrier to enforcement of 28 C.F.R. § 35.130(f). Thus, the drivers could recover on their claims for declaratory and injunctive relief. Additionally, the State of Florida established a statutory procedure under § 215.26, Fla. Stat. (Supp. 1996) (amended) for obtaining a refund of a tax payment where no tax was due. Accordingly, for tax refunds under § 215.26 the State had consented to be sued, and the immunity under the Eleventh Amendment for monetary relief was thereby waived. However, the record did not reveal which drivers, if any, made application for a refund under § 215.26 within the statutory time limit. Finally, the drivers were entitled to appellate attorney's fees under 42 U.S.C.S. § 12205 for that portion of the appellate proceedings reasonably attributable to the claims for declaratory and injunctive relief.


OUTCOME: The award of declaratory and injunctive relief was affirmed, but the issue of monetary relief was remanded to the trial court regarding only those claimants who timely applied for a refund. Appellate attorney's fees were granted for that portion of the appellate proceedings reasonably attributable to the claims for declaratory and injunctive relief, and the matter was remanded to the trial court to determine the amount of the fees.

City of Gainesville v. Crapo


CASE NO. 1D05-4253


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


953 So. 2d 557; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 1631; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 442



February 12, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 30, 2007.
Rehearing denied by City of Gainesville v. Crapo, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 7023 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Apr. 12, 2007)
Review denied by City of Gainesville v. Crapo, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 2315 (Fla., Nov. 26, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Alachua County. Robert E. Roundtree, Jr., Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city filed an action against appellees, a property appraiser, a tax collector, and the Director of the Florida Department of Revenue, in which the city sought a declaratory judgment that certain property was tax exempt. The Circuit Court for Alachua County (Florida) granted partial summary judgment to both parties. The city appealed. The appraiser and the Director filed a cross-appeal.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that communications towers and certain land were subject to taxation and that a fiber optic network and Internet equipment were exempt under Art. VII, § 3(a), Fla. Const. The court held that the trial court had erred in concluding as a matter of law that the city's use of the fiber optic network and Internet equipment to provide telecommunications services to the public served municipal or public purposes without considering whether the services promoted the goals set forth in § 364.01(3), Fla. Stat. (2002). Next, although the city used the towers for governmental communications, private providers also leased and used spaces on the towers for private business. This contradicted the requirement of Art. VII, § 3(a), Fla. Const. that property be used exclusively by a municipality for municipal or public purposes. Finally, the city argued that the land was being used for the public purposes of providing a buffer between the generating plant and residential development and accommodating future plant retrofitting and/or expansion. The land, however, had been in use for private purposes on both the 2003 and 2004 assessment dates; thus, it was not tax exempt.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's ruling as to the fiber optic network and Internet equipment. It affirmed the trial court's rulings with regard to the communication tower and the land. It remanded the case for further proceedings.

Gonzalez v. State


Case No. 5D05-2834


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


948 So. 2d 892; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 1577; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 436



February 9, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 28, 2007.
Review denied by Gonzalez v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1320 (Fla., July 6, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, Daniel P. Dawson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida) convicted defendant of dealing in stolen property in violation of § 812.019(1), Fla. Stat. (2001). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged on appeal that the trial court erred by denying his motion to declare §§ 812.019(1) (2001) and 812.012(8), Fla. Stat., unconstitutional, and by awarding $ 4,000 in restitution, when the evidence did not support this amount. The appeals court first held that the trial court properly upheld the challenged statutes, as the statutes were not overbroad. A statute's purported overbreadth occurred when that statute criminalized conduct that was otherwise innocent. Because trafficking in any amount of stolen goods was not innocent conduct, the fact that trafficking in a small amount of stolen goods was relatively harmless, as defendant alleged, was of no consequence. Second, defendant's equal protection challenge was rejected. Even if the equal protection clause was implicated, the challenged statutes adequately addressed the State's interest in discouraging and punishing dealing in stolen goods at all levels. Finally, because the restitution amount of $ 4,000 was not supported by the victim's testimony, but instead said testimony supported a loss in the amount of $ 3,125, restitution in that amount should have been ordered.


OUTCOME: The trial court's denial of defendant's motion to declare §§ 812.019(1) (2001) and 812.012(8), Fla. Stat. unconstitutional was affirmed. But, the restitution order in the amount of $ 4,000 was reversed, and the case was remanded. On remand, a corrected restitution award in the amount of $ 3,125 was to be entered.

Imhotep-Nguzo Saba Charter Sch. v. Dep't of Educ.


Nos. 4D05-4634 & 4D05-4635 1


1 We have consolidated these related cases for opinion purposes only.


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


947 So. 2d 1279; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 1414; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 394



February 7, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 23, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from the State of Florida, Department of Education; L.T. Case Nos. 05-1081 FOI and 05-1082 FOI.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Florida Department of Education (Department) affirmed decisions by the Palm Beach County School Board (School Board) to deny charters to appellant schools. The schools appealed.


OVERVIEW: The schools challenged the application and constitutionality of a School Board policy. The appeals court found the challenged policy was valid, affirming the Department's decision. While § 1002.33, Fla. Stat. (2005) was clearly aimed at giving charter schools some measure of academic and administrative freedom, the appeals court did not read this provision to prohibit the School Board from adopting and enforcing policies related to the creation, renewal or termination of the charter schools they sponsor. Such was true because the legislature delegated primary decision-making authority to the school boards over these basic decisions. Second, the "Guiding Principles; Purpose" section of the charter school statute provided sufficient legislative guidance to support the School Board's Policy 2.56. When coupled with the mandatory application requirements, this section saved the legislative delegation from separation of powers problems. Moreover, these statements provided the School Board with sufficient ground to allow it to require an applicant who already owned a school to show that it was an exemplary school before another charter will be granted to the same entity.


OUTCOME: The Department's judgment was affirmed.

 

1583 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


DaimlerChrysler Corp. v. Hurst


No. 3D06-2593


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


949 So. 2d 279; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 1434; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 387



February 7, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 15, 2007.
Review denied by Hurst v. DaimlerChrysler Corp., 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1299 (Fla., July 6, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] A Writ of Certiorari to the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Joseph P. Farina, Chief Judge. Lower Tribunal No. 04-24071.



DISPOSITION: Petition granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner corporation brought a proceeding against respondent personal representative, seeking a writ of certiorari to the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County (Florida) seeking quashal of the denial of the corporation's motion to dismiss and the trial court's findings regarding the constitutionality of the Asbestos and Silica Compensation Fairness Act (Act), § 774.201, Fla. Stat. et seq.


OVERVIEW: The corporation moved to dismiss based on the personal representative's failure to provide evidence satisfying the "prima facie" showing under § 774.204(3), Fla. Stat. The personal representative conceded that she could not satisfy the Act's prima facie showing. However, the trial court ruled that the Act was unconstitutionally retroactive as applied to the personal representative. The appellate court held that the trial court erred. The parties acknowledged that the legislature intended for the Act to apply retroactively. The personal representative, however, argued that the retroactive application of § 774.204(3) divested her of a substantive vested right. The appellate court disagreed. When the personal representative filed her asbestos claim, she was pursuing a common law tort theory. Before the enactment of the Act, the personal representative had, at most, a "mere expectation" that the common law would not be altered by legislation. The personal representative did not have a vested right in her common law asbestos claim. Therefore, retroactive application of the Act was constitutionally permissible.


OUTCOME: The petition was granted, the order under review was quashed, and the case was remanded for entry of an order granting the corporation's motion to dismiss.

 

1584 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


J.L.S. v. State


No. 3D05-2604


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


947 So. 2d 641; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 707; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 263



January 24, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 9, 2007.
Review denied by J.L.S. v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 864 (Fla., May 4, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Maria Espinosa Dennis, Judge. Lower Tribunal No. 05-150.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Florida, denied appellant juvenile's motion to dismiss a charge of trespass in a school safety zone in violation of § 810.0975(2)(b), Fla. Stat. (2005), he pled no contest to that charge and to resisting arrest; he was adjudicated a delinquent. He appealed, alleging § 810.0975(2)(b) was unconstitutional due to its overbreadth, vagueness, and violation of substantive due process.


OVERVIEW: Section 810.0975(2)(b) barred persons from being in a school safety zone within one hour of school closing or opening unless they had legitimate business or were authorized to be there. A police officer saw appellant walking through his high school's safety zone at 7:25 a.m. on a school day and arrested him. Appellant had twice before been warned against such trespassing. The appellate court held that § 810.0975(2)(b) was not unconstitutionally overbroad. It was designed to primarily regulate conduct rather than pure speech; any applications of the statute that violated the First Amendment could be remedied through as-applied litigation. Appellant lacked standing to raise a facial vagueness challenge to the statute with respect to the hypothetical conduct of others because his own actions fell within the statute's proscriptions. Appellant argued that because the statute could be used to punish innocent activities, it violated substantive due process. The appellate court disagreed. The purpose of § 810.0975(2)(b) -- protecting school children -- was both legitimate and compelling, and the geographical and temporal restrictions it imposed bore a rational relation to its purpose.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

A.H. v. State


CASE NO. 1D06-0162


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


949 So. 2d 234; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 484; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 243



January 19, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 6, 2007.
Review denied by A.H. v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1025 (Fla., May 25, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Alachua County (Florida) adjudicated appellant minor delinquent for producing, directing, or promoting a photograph or representation that she knew included sexual conduct of a child, in violation of § 827.071(3), Fla. Stat. (2005), after denying her motion to dismiss the charge. The juvenile appealed.


OVERVIEW: Despite the juvenile's arguments to the contrary, the trial court ruled that there was a compelling state interest in preventing the production of the photographs at issue, and criminal prosecution was the least intrusive means of furthering the State's compelling interest. The appeals court agreed. Further, the juvenile had no reasonable expectation of privacy under the circumstances herein because: (1) the decision to take photographs and to keep a record that might be shown to people in the future weighed against a reasonable expectation of privacy; (2) the photographs which were taken were shared by the two minors who were involved in the sexual activities, and neither had a reasonable expectation that the other would not show the photos to a third party; and (3) the fact that these photographs might have or might not have been shown in no way affected the minor's reasonable expectation that there was a distinct and real possibility that the other teenager involved would at some point make these photos public.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1586 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Hazen v. Allstate Ins. Co.


Case No. 2D06-184


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


952 So. 2d 531; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 347; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 219



January 17, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 25, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Polk County; Ralph Artigliere, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant car owner sued appellee insurer for breach of an alleged oral agreement to repair her vehicle. The Circuit Court for Polk County, Florida, dismissed the suit with prejudice for noncompliance with the nonjoinder statute, § 627.4136, Fla. Stat. (2002). Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant's car was involved in an accident with another vehicle; the owner of the other vehicle had an auto policy with the insurer. The permissive user who drove the other vehicle was negligent. The insurer agreed its insured was liable for the accident and paid for repairs to appellant's car. She alleged the repairs were inadequate and sued the insurer. Her complaint did not allege she had obtained a settlement or verdict against either the insured or the permissive user of the other vehicle. She argued that her acceptance of the insurer's oral offer to repair her car was a "settlement" that satisfied one of the two alternative conditions precedent of § 627.4136 for filing a direct action against an alleged tortfeasor's insurer. The appellate court disagreed. A presuit agreement between an injured third party and an insurer about the adjustment of a claim was not a "settlement" within the meaning of § 627.4136(1) because it did not occur within the course of pending litigation in which the insured was already a party. Nor did the complaint allege sufficient facts to plead that the insurer assumed an obligation to appellant that was independent of the insurance contract.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

R.C. v. State


CASE NO. 1D06-2811


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


948 So. 2d 48; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 97; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 190



January 5, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 23, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Gadsden County. Angela C. Dempsey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile sought review of a disposition order, pursuant to Fla. R. Juv. P. 8.135(b)(2), issued by the Circuit Court for Gadsden County (Florida), which adjudicated the juvenile as delinquent and which deviated from the placement recommended by the Department of Juvenile Justice.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile was found guilty by the trial court, after a hearing, for aggravated assault on a law enforcement officer, resisting an officer with violence, and disruption of a school function. In a predisposition report, the Department recommended probation. The trial court placed the juvenile in a moderate-risk residential commitment with the Department, in part because the trial court found that the juvenile was a confirmed gang member, drug user, and likely dealer. The court found that there was insufficient evidence to establish that the juvenile met two of the eight criteria set forth in § 874.03(2), Fla. Stat. (2005). Although there was testimony to identify the juvenile as a gang member, there was insufficient evidence to establish any of the other statutory criteria. There was no evidence that the juvenile resided in an area or associated with known criminal street gang members. There was no evidence that the informants who identified the juvenile as a gang member were reliable and their testimony was not corroborated. The trial court erred in relying on the juvenile's alleged gang membership to support a deviation from the Department's recommendation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court and remanded the matter to the trial court for further proceedings.

Lipton v. First Union Nat'l Bank


No. 4D06-175


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


944 So. 2d 1256; 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 38; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 159



January 3, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 19, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Dorian K. Damoorgian, Judge; L.T. Case No. 02-10232 CACE 12.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant borrower sued appellee bank, alleging that the bank breached a contract to maintain a line of credit by refusing to perform its obligations under it. The Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), entered judgment in favor of the bank. The borrower appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the borrower made a material misrepresentation to the bank when he did not disclose that he was involved in Federal Trade Commission (FTC) litigation before the closing on the line of credit. The appellate court found that the evidence showed that the FTC litigation severely affected the borrower's income and would have led a reasonable person to conclude that there was a serious problem with the borrower's ability to pay the loan in the future. The loan agreement allowed the bank to suspend the loan if it reasonably believed that the borrower would be unable to repay the loan due to a material change in his financial circumstances. The bank could reasonably have believed that any effect the litigation might have on the borrower's income was substantial and materially affected his financial circumstances. There was substantial competent evidence to support the trial court's findings and no error in its conclusion that the bank had not breached the contract. Because the bank was allowed to waive the provision that the termination must be in writing, the trial court could properly have found that the borrower's oral termination was effective.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Newby v. State


No. 4D05-3555


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


945 So. 2d 636; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 21609; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 111



December 27, 2006, Decided

1590 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Kasischke v. State


CASE NO. 3D04-2149


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


946 So. 2d 1155; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 21282; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 48



December 20, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Kasischke v. State, 954 So. 2d 1156, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 757 (Fla., 2007)
Quashed by, Remanded by Kasischke v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1241 (Fla., July 10, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Henry Leyte-Vidal, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 00-21911.
Kasischke v. State, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 19958 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., Dec. 20, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of three counts of lewd and lascivious assault on a child under 16. The Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Florida, revoked defendant's community control under former § 948.03(5)(a)7, Fla. Stat. (1999), for violating a condition of community control that prohibited him from possessing pornography. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant paid a 15-year-old boy to allow him to perform oral sex on the boy. Additionally, he masturbated in the boy's presence. As a condition of community control, he was prohibited from viewing, owning, or possessing any obscene, pornographic, or sexually stimulating materials. Police found in his home a pornographic video and photos of males performing various sexual acts. Defendant contended that, since he was convicted of a sexual offense on a child under 16, the State had to prove that the pornographic materials involved a minor under 16 for a community control violation to be found. The appellate court disagreed. The legislative history of § 948.03(5)(a)7 showed that the legislature did not intend to alter the preexisting ban on all pornographic or obscene material for sex offenders who were on probation or under community control. Thus, the limiting phrase in § 948.03(5)(a)7, "relevant to the offender's deviant behavior pattern," modified only the words "sexually stimulating material," and not the terms "obscene" or "pornographic." Therefore, defendant's community control was properly revoked.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1591 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Lescher v. Dep't of Highway Safety & Motor Vehicles


No. 4D06-2291


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


946 So. 2d 1140; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 21284; 32 Fla. L. Weekly D 10



December 20, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 5, 2007.
Review granted by Lescher v. Fla. Dep't of Highway Safety & Motor Vehicles, 949 So. 2d 198, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 290 (Fla., 2007)
Approved by Lescher v. Fla. Dep't of Highway Safety & Motor Vehicles, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1221 (Fla., July 3, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for writ of certiorari to the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Diana Lewis, Timothy P. McCarthy and Karen Miller, Judges; L.T. Case No. 502005CA00841XXXXM.



DISPOSITION: Petition for Certiorari Denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner applicant sought a writ of certiorari to the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), which upheld the denial by respondent, the Florida Department of Highway Safety and Motor Vehicles, of his request for reinstatement of his driver's license, which was permanently revoked based on his four prior DUI convictions, on hardship grounds as authorized by a statute that was no longer in effect.


OVERVIEW: The applicant argued that when the legislature reenacted § 322.271(4), Fla. Stat., effective July 1, 2003, the elimination of the hardship license violated the ex post facto prohibition in Art. I, § 10, Fla. Const., as applied to him. His driver's license was permanently revoked in 2000. On appeal, the court held that because the ex post facto clauses of the United States and Florida Constitutions, U.S. Const. art. I, § 9; U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, cl. 1; Art. I, § 10, Fla. Const., applied only to criminal legislation and proceedings, and driver's license revocation was not criminal punishment, the amendment eliminating the hardship driver's license, when applied to the applicant who could have sought a hardship license before the amendment became effective, was not unconstitutional as an ex post facto law. Because the court was seeing a number of petitions raising the issue, and anticipated that other districts would also face the issue, the court certified the question of whether the amendment violated the prohibition against ex post fact laws to persons who could have applied for a hardship license before the amendment became effective as one of great public importance.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition for certiorari but certified the following question as one of great public importance: whether the amendment to § 322.271(4), Fla. Stat., which eliminated hardship driver's licenses effective July 1, 2003, violated the prohibition against ex post facto laws as to persons who could have applied for a hardship license before the amendment became effective.

 

1592 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Rollins, Inc. v. Butland


Case No. 2D05-368


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


951 So. 2d 860; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 20861; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 3148



December 15, 2006, Decided  
December 15, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 19, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Rollins, Inc. v. Butland, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 979 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., Jan. 2, 2007)
Review denied by Butland v. Rollins, Inc., 962 So. 2d 335, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1328 (Fla., July 9, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from nonfinal order of the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County; Emmett Lamar Battles, Judge.
Rollins, Inc. v. Butland, 932 So. 2d 1172, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 10807 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2006)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee customers filed a class action against appellants, the exterminating company and its parent corporation, in the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County (Florida), for claims arising from the exterminating company's contractual undertakings as to the control of subterranean termites. The court certified a class and one subclass under Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.220(b)(2) and 1.220(b)(3). The exterminating company and its parent corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: The customers, each of whom entered into a contract with the exterminating company, claimed that they sustained termite damage to their homes caused by the company's deficient performance of its obligations under the contract. The customers made claims of deceptive and unfair trade practices, misleading advertising, criminal racketeering, breach of contract, and unjust enrichment, and for declaratory and injunctive relief. On appeal, the court found that (1) questions affecting individual members of the putative class on the first five claims overwhelmed the common questions arising from the provisions of the contract; (2) the proposed class action did not meet the requirements for certification under Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.220(b)(3) because it was unmanageable; and (3) class certification was not superior to other methods available for the fair and efficient adjudication of the controversy. Thus, the circuit court abused its discretion in certifying the class under Rule 1.220(b)(3). Additionally, because issues pertaining to money damages predominated in the case, class certification of the declaratory and injunctive relief claim under Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.220(b)(2) was inappropriate.


OUTCOME: The order of class certification was reversed, and the case was remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings. On remand, the customers could attempt to narrow the scope of their claims and to modify the proposed class.

 

1593 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Zimmerman v. Office of Ins. Regulation


No. 4D06-1516


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


944 So. 2d 1163; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 20785; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 3126



December 13, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 25, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Zimmerman v. State, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 1133 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Jan. 25, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the State of Florida, Department of Financial Services Office of Insurance Regulation; L.T. Case No. 81914.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners challenged insurance premium rate increases. Appellee, the State of Florida, Department of Financial Services Office of Insurance Regulation (OIR), determined that there was no probable cause showing that appellee underwriting association, the predecessor in interest of appellee insurance company, violated the insurance premium rating law in setting wind damage rates. The property owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The property owners asserted two main arguments in the appeal from the OIR's finding of no probable cause. First, they argued that the rate increase was invalid because a public hearing was not held on the underwriting association's rate filing, as provided by § 627.0629(7), Fla. Stat. (1999), and Fla. Admin. Code Ann. R. 4-166.051(3) (1999) (recodified as Fla. Admin. Code Ann. R. 69O-166.051). Second, they claimed that the rate increase was invalid because private arbitration to set the underwriting association's rates was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court found that prior litigation and the case before the court involved the same parties and issues. Further, the prior litigation, which led to an appellate opinion, was fully litigated and determined in a contest which resulted in a final decision of a court of competent jurisdiction. Thus, the property owners' claims were barred by the doctrine of collateral estoppel. Additionally, even if the court were to reach the merits, the court was without the authority to order credits or refunds because only the OIR had the authority to do so, not the courts.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

1594 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


In re Jane Doe 06-C


CASE NO. 1D06-5226


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


948 So. 2d 30; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 20755; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 3100



December 12, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 29, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. Angela C. Dempsey, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Leon County (Florida) entered a final order dismissing appellant minor's petition for a judicial waiver of parental notice of termination of pregnancy. The minor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The minor asserted that the trial judge improperly disqualified one of her attorneys, thereby depriving her of the counsel of her choice at the hearing on her petition. The appeals court agreed, and found that such error was not harmless. Although the trial judge referenced three authorities for her ruling: (1) the Parental Notice of Abortion Act, § 390.01114, Fla. Stat.; (2) § 27.51, Fla. Stat.; and (3) the "ethical rules," none of these authorities precluded an attorney who wished to provide private representation in connection with a non-criminal petition for judicial waiver of parental notice of termination of pregnancy from doing so merely because the attorney also served as an assistant public defender in unrelated criminal cases. But, remand for a new hearing was not authorized in proceedings of this type. Hence, having found that there was no necessity for the disqualification of the minor's counsel, it ordered the trial court to grant the minor's petition for a judicial waiver of parental notice of termination of pregnancy.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the trial judge was ordered to grant the minor's petition.

 

1595 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Paey v. State


Case No. 2D04-2318


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


943 So. 2d 919; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 20376; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 3021



December 6, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 26, 2006.
Review denied by Paey v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 508 (Fla., Mar. 9, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Pasco County; Daniel D. Diskey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Circuit Court for Pasco County (Florida) of trafficking in oxycodone, possession of hydrocodone, and obtaining or attempting to obtain a controlled substance by misrepresentation, fraud, forgery, deception, or subterfuge. Defendant was sentenced to a 25-year prison sentence for each trafficking count and to one year and one day for each possession and obtaining by fraud count. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the mandatory minimum sentencing term for trafficking in oxycodone violated the Eighth Amendment and former Fla. Const. art. I, § 17 (1997). The appellate court held that the mandatory minimum sentences were not grossly disproportionate to the trafficking crime. The Florida legislature could reasonably decide that trafficking in oxycodone warranted a significant term of imprisonment, even in the absence of a prior offense or violent behavior. The amount of oxycodone possessed by defendant fell into the highest weight category under § 893.135(1)(c)(1), Fla. Stat. (Supp. 1996). Defendant did not possess such an extraordinarily small amount of oxycodone that his crime should not be considered severe. The sentence also was constitutional under former Fla. Const. art. I, § 17 (1997). Although the substantial majority by weight of each prescription was composed of acetaminophen, under § 893.135(1)(c)(1), Fla. Stat. (Supp. 1996), an individual could be convicted for possessing "any mixture" containing oxycodone that weighed at least four grams. Finally, the executive branch had the power to consider the mitigating factors and to grant pardons and commute sentences.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Floridians Against Expanded Gambling v. Floridians for a Level Playing Field


CASE NO. 1D05-0575


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


945 So. 2d 553; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 20034; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 3008



November 30, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 23, 2007.
Review granted by, in part Floridians for a Level Playing Field v. Floridians Against Expanded Gambling, 952 So. 2d 1189, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 570 (Fla., 2007)
Discharged by, Review dismissed by Floridians for a Level Playing Field v. Floridians Against Expanded Gambling, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1786 (Fla., Sept. 27, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Leon County. Judge Nikki Ann Clark.
Floridians Against Expanded Gambling v. Floridians For a Level Playing Field, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 13198 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Aug. 8, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant organizations sued appellees, a citizen group and state and local agencies and officials, seeking a declaration that a "slots initiative" petition proposing to amend the Florida Constitution was invalid because it did not comply with Fla. Const. art. XI, § 3 or § 100.371, Fla. Stat. After the election was held, the Circuit Court for Leon County, Florida, granted appellees summary judgment. The organizations appealed.


OVERVIEW: The organizations claimed paid petition gatherers forged signatures and fabricated names on initiative petitions, in violation of Fla. Const. art. XI, § 3, and the names and addresses of the paid petition gatherers were not included, in violation of § 100.371, Fla. Stat. The trial court held the election cured any failure by appellees to obtain the constitutionally required number of petition signatures, even if they and their agents committed fraud. The appellate court agreed with the trial court that Florida law did not mandate the invalidation of signature petition forms that did not include the name and address of the paid petition gatherers. However, the trial court erred in ruling that it was precluded by the separation of powers doctrine from reviewing the method used by the supervisors of elections to verify signatures. Summary judgment was entered in error on the claim that the petition did not comply with Fla. Const. art. XI, § 3, as the suit was filed before the election, and an election could cure only minor, technical defects in the form of the submission of a proposed amendment -- not fraud. The trial court erred in denying the organizations an expedited trial.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the summary judgment to the extent it was entered on separation of powers grounds and on the organizations' claim that the petitions did not comply with Fla. Const. art. XI, § 3. It remanded the case for a trial to determine whether appellees failed to obtain the constitutionally required signatures. If the trial court determined they did, and no remaining defenses applied, it had to declare the initiative invalid.

 

1597 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Vill. of Wellington v. Palm Beach County


Nos. 4D05-2666 and 4D05-2687


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


941 So. 2d 595; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 19600; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 2935



November 22, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Vill. of Wellington v. Palm Beach County, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 20265 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Nov. 22, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Consolidated appeals and cross-appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Jonathan D. Gerber, Judge; L.T. Case No. 502004CA9387XXXXMBAB.
Vill. of Wellington v. Palm Beach County, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 15517 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Sept. 20, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant cities sued appellee county, challenging an amendment to the county's charter that intended to provide an exclusive method of voluntary municipal annexation for the county. The Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County, Florida, ruled the amendment was partially valid but contained three invalid provisions. All parties appealed. Appellants moved for rehearing, rehearing en banc, and for clarification.


OVERVIEW: The trial court ruled that portions of the amendment violated § 171.044(4), Fla. Stat. (2004), as the exclusive method of voluntary annexation had to be contained in the charter itself, while the amendment allowed the use of an ordinance to accomplish that goal. It held that the other challenged provisions were valid and upheld the amendment by severing the invalid portions. The appellate court held that § 171.044(4) authorized a county to devise its own methods of voluntary municipal annexation, as long as it was consistent with the Florida Constitution, general law, and special law. Under § 171.044(4), where a county's charter contained an exclusive method of municipal annexation, § 171.044's procedures did not apply; the procedures of the charter had to be followed. The trial court properly removed those portions of the amendment allowing annexation to be accomplished through an ordinance rather than the charter itself, because those provisions violated § 171.044(4), the remaining provisions were valid, and the amendment had a severability clause.


OUTCOME: The appellate court denied appellants' motion for rehearing and rehearing en banc, but grant the motion for clarification to correct typographical errors. It affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

1599 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Gonzalez v. State


Case No. 5D05-3398


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


941 So. 2d 1226; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 19290; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 2886



November 17, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 6, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, John H. Adams, Sr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida) that denied his motion to declare § 828.122(3), Fla. Stat. (2005), which outlawed animal fighting, unconstitutional as overbroad.


OVERVIEW: After defendant admitted to investigators that he had gone to the location to watch cockfights, he was charged with violating § 828.122(3). The State specifically alleged that defendant was present at a cockfight, and possessed spurs, which the roosters wore in order to fight, thus, promoting cockfighting. Defendant argued that the statute was overbroad because it might punish innocent bystanders who happened upon two animals fighting, e.g., a person who observed two dogs fighting in the street or a zoo patron who witnessed animals fighting. The appellate court found that the language of the statute was clear and unambiguous, particularly when considered with the requirement that such attendance be "knowing." Because the statute was not overly broad or vague, the rule of lenity did not apply. Consequently, the statute was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
